Definition and Rulings of Qiran
Definition and rulings of qiran from Nur al-Idah with al-Bahr al-Ra'iq commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of qiran, list its required actions in order, and explain when the sacrifice becomes wajib.

Core Idea
Qiran combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram; its actions follow a set order and sacrifice is wajib after stoning.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi definition of qiran, the actions required for its valid performance, and the obligatory sacrifice. Understanding this form of Hajj is essential for any pilgrim who wishes to combine both journeys without completing them separately. The passage from Nur al-Idah with commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the precise sequence and the conditions under which a person becomes a qarin.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Read the first sentence: 'Qiran is to combine the ihram for Hajj and Umrah.' Identify the key elements: combining in one ihram and the intention.
The definition also includes the case of adding one ihram to the other before certain thresholds.
2
List the actions in order
From 'When he enters Mecca...' to 'then completes the actions of Hajj', list the sequential steps: Umrah tawaf (with ramal), sa'i, arrival tawaf for Hajj, then Hajj rituals.
The order is wajib; the commentary stresses that precedence of Umrah in actions is obligatory.
3
Identify the sacrifice ruling
Find the phrase 'must slaughter a sheep or a seventh of a camel/cow' after stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba. Note that sacrifice is wajib and must occur after stoning.
Delaying sacrifice beyond this point is not invalid but missing it requires dam.
4
Understand the three ways to become a qarin
Analyze the classifications: (1) intending both together, (2) entering Hajj upon Umrah before most Umrah circuits, (3) entering Umrah upon Hajj before arrival tawaf. Note that the third is considered 'wrongdoing' but still makes one a qarin.
The first two have no wrong; the third is 'qarin musī’'.
5
Distinguish from other types
Contrast qiran with mufrid (single intention) and mutamatti‘ (Umrah then Hajj with normal break). Recognize that the key difference is the single ihram or adding within limits.
The commentary lists four muhrims; qarin is one of them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل [في القران] القران هو أن يجمع بين إحرام الحج والعمرة، فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الإحرام: اللهم إني أريد العمرة والحج فيسرهما لي وتقبلهما مني، ثم يلبّي، فإذا دخل مكة بدأ بطواف العمرة سبعة أشواط يرمل في الثلاثة الأول فقط، ثم يصلي ركعتي الطواف ثم يخرج إلى الصفا، ويقوم عليه داعيا مكبرا مهللا ملبيا مصليا على النبي يهبط نحو المروة ويسعى بين الميلين الأخضرين، فيتم سبعة أشواط وهذه أفعال العمرة، والعمرة سنة، ثم يطوف طواف القدوم للحج، ثم يتم أفعال الحج كما تقدم، فإذا رمى يوم النحر جمرة العقبة وجب عليه ذبح شاة أو سُبع بدنة، عامه القرآن إلخ: اعلم أن المحرمين أربعة مفرد بالحج إن أحرم به مفردا، أو مفرد بالعمرة إن أحرم بها في غير أشهر الحج، وطاف لها كذلك، حج من عامه أو لا، أو طاف فيها ولم يحج من عامه، أو أحرم بها في أشهر الحج وطاف كذلك ولم يحج من عامه، أو حج وألم بينهما بأهله إلماما صحيحا، ومتمتع إن أتى بأكثر أشواط العمرة في أشهر الحج بعد ما أحرم بها فقط مطلقا، ثم حج من غير أن يلم بأهله إلماما صحيحا، وقارن إن أحرم بهما معا، أو أدخل إحرام الحج على إحرام العمرة قبل أن يطوف لها أكثر الأشواط، أو أدخل إحرام العمرة على إحرام الحج قبل أن يطوف للقدوم ولو شوطا، ولا إساءة في القسمين الأولين، وهو قارن مسيء في الثالث. [البحر الرائق: ٥٤٤/٢] أن يجمع إلخ: أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان الجمع حقيقة أو حكما، فيدخل فيه ما إذا أحرم بالعمرة ثم أحرم بالحج قبل أن يطوف لها الأكثر، أو أحرم بالحج ثم أحرم بالعمرة قبل أن يطوف له، وإن كان مسيئا في الثاني. [البحر الرائق بتصرف: ٥٤٧/٢] فيقول إلخ: المراد النية لا التلفظ، إن كان عطفه على "يجمع"، فيكون من تمام الحد، وإن رفع كان ابتداء كلام بيانا للسنة، فإن السنة للقارن التلفظ بها [البحر الرائق بزيادة: ٥٤٧/٢] العمرة: اعلم أن تقديم العمرة في الذكر مستحب؛ لأن الواو للترتيب [البحر الرائق بزيادة: ٥٤٧/٢] بدأ إلخ وهذا الترتيب، أعني تقديم العمرة في أفعال الحج، واجب. [البحر الرائق: ٥٤٨/٢] وجب عليه قيد بالذبح بعد الرمي؛ لأن الذبح قبله لا يجوز؛ لوجوب الترتيب. [البحر الرائق: ٥٤٩/٢] بدنة: أطلق البدنة، فشملت البعير والبقرة، والسبع جزء من سبعة أجزاء. [البحر الرائق: ٥٤٩/٢]
Section on Qiran. Qiran is to combine the ihram for Hajj and Umrah. He says after praying the two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend Umrah and Hajj, so make them easy for me and accept them from me.' Then he recites the talbiya. When he enters Mecca, he begins with the circumambulation of Umrah, seven circuits, performing ramal in the first three only. Then he prays two rak'ahs of the circumambulation, then goes out to Safa and stands upon it supplicating, saying Allahu Akbar, la ilaha illa Allah, reciting talbiya and sending blessings on the Prophet. He descends towards Marwa and runs between the two green markers, completing seven circuits. These are the actions of Umrah, and Umrah is sunna. Then he performs the circumambulation of arrival for Hajj, then completes the actions of Hajj as previously mentioned. When he throws the pebbles at the Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Sacrifice, he must slaughter a sheep or a seventh of a camel/cow. 'The general of the Quran etc.': Know that the muhrims are four: mufrid for Hajj if he assumes ihram for Hajj alone; mufrid for Umrah if he assumes ihram for it outside the months of Hajj and performs tawaf for it similarly, whether he performs Hajj in that year or not, or he performs tawaf in it and does not perform Hajj that year, or he assumes ihram for it in the months of Hajj and performs tawaf similarly and does not perform Hajj that year, or he performs Hajj and makes a proper stop between them with his family; mutamatti' if he performs most of the circuits of Umrah in the months of Hajj after having assumed ihram for it only, absolutely, then he performs Hajj without making a proper stop between them with his family; qarin if he assumes ihram for both together, or he enters ihram for Hajj upon ihram for Umrah before performing most of its circuits, or he enters ihram for Umrah upon ihram for Hajj before performing the circumambulation of arrival even if one circuit. There is no wrong in the first two divisions, and he is a wrongdoer qarin in the third. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/544] 'To combine etc.': He made it absolute, so it includes whether the combination is real or legal, thus it includes if he assumes ihram for Umrah then he assumes ihram for Hajj before performing most of its circuits, or he assumes ihram for Hajj then he assumes ihram for Umrah before performing the circumambulation for it, even if he is wrongdoer in the second. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq adapted 2/547] 'He says etc.': The meaning is intention, not utterance; if it is conjoined to 'combines', then it becomes part of the definition; if raised, it is the beginning of a statement explaining the sunna, for it is sunna for the qarin to utter it. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with addition 2/547] 'Umrah': Know that mentioning Umrah first is recommended because the waw is for order. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with addition 2/547] 'He begins etc.': This order, meaning the precedence of Umrah in the actions of Hajj, is obligatory. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/548] 'It is obligatory upon him' is restricted to after the stoning, because slaughtering before it is not permitted due to the necessity of order. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/549] 'Badana': He used it absolutely, so it includes the camel and the cow, and 'seven' is a part of seven parts. [al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 2/549]
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage defines qiran and details its performance. It begins by defining qiran as combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram with a specific intention and talbiya. The actions are then listed: perform Umrah first (tawaf with ramal in first three circuits, sa'i), then perform the arrival tawaf for Hajj, then complete the rest of Hajj. On the Day of Sacrifice, a sacrifice is obligatory. The commentary clarifies the types of muhrims (four: mufrid for Hajj, mufrid for Umrah, mutamatti', qarin) and the conditions for each. It notes that qiran can be achieved by combining the two intentions at the start or by adding one later before certain thresholds. The commentary also explains that the order of actions in qiran is wajib (obligatory), and the sacrifice must occur after stoning, as order is required. The 'badana' includes camel and cow, with one-seventh counted as a share.

Key Terms
القران (al-qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, either by intending both together or adding one to the other before specified limits.
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah in the months of Hajj then performs Hajj in the same year without returning home between them.
المفرد (al-mufrid): One who performs Hajj or Umrah alone without combining.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when must a qarin perform the sacrifice?
A) Immediately after entering Mecca.
B) On the Day of Sacrifice after stoning the Jamrat al-Aqaba.
C) Before the tawaf of Umrah.
D) There is no sacrifice required in qiran.

Key Takeaway
Qiran is a single ihram for Hajj and Umrah with wajib order and sacrifice after stoning; missing the threshold for adding one to the other prevents becoming a qarin.

Tamattu': Definition and Rules of Substitute Fasting
Defines tamattu' and details the fasting substitute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of tamattu', explain the obligation of the sacrificial animal (hady), and apply the rules of the fasting substitute when unable to sacrifice.

Core Idea
Tamattu' requires sacrifice; fasting replaces it only when unable, with strict timing and conditions.

This lesson defines tamattu' and explains the obligation of sacrifice. It then details the substitute fasting when one cannot afford the sacrifice, covering the precise timing of the three-day and seven-day fasts, the conditions for validity, and the effect of later ability to sacrifice. We follow the Hanafi position as explained in the classical texts.

Guided Path
1
Define tamattu'
Identify the definition: entering ihram for umrah only from the miqat during the months of hajj, then performing hajj in the same year without returning home.
The key condition is that most of the tawaf of umrah occurs in the months of hajj.
2
Identify the obligation of hady
State that the hady (sacrificial animal) is wajib for tamattu', and if unable, fasting is prescribed as a substitute.
The substitute is only valid when the original is impossible.
3
Analyze the timing of the three-day fast
The three days must be fasted during the hajj season, from the time of ihram for umrah up to the day of sacrifice. The best is the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, Tarwiyah, and Arafah, but any time in that window is valid.
The phrase 'fi al-hajj' in the Qur'an indicates the time, not the actions.
4
Analyze the timing of the seven-day fast
The seven days must be after returning from Mina and completing the wajibat, as indicated by 'idha raja'tum' in the verse.
It cannot be advanced before the condition is met.
5
Apply the rules of badal (substitute)
If one becomes able to sacrifice during the three-day fast period or before the day of sacrifice, the fast is invalidated and the sacrifice becomes obligatory. If ability comes after tahlul (halq), the fast stands.
Similar to tayammum: seeing water after prayer does not break the tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
٢٦٥
بيان التمتع
فإذا لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام قبل مجيء يوم النحر من أشهر الحج، وسبعة أيام بعد
الفراغ من الحج ولو بمكة بعد مضي أيام التشريق، ولو فرقها جاز.
فصل في التمتع]
التمتع هو أن يحرم بالعمرة فقط من الميقات،
ثلاثة أيام قال الطحطاوي آخرها يوم عرفة إلخ، وفي "البحر": وهو بيان للأفضل، وإلا فوقته وقت الحج بعد الإحرام بالعمرة؛ لأن المراد بالحج في الآية: فَصِيَامُ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ (البقرة: ١٩٦) وقته؛ لأن نفسه لا يصلح ظرفا، وإنما كان الأفضل التأخير؛ لأن الصوم بدل عن الهدي، فيستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته رجاء أن يقدر على الأصل قبل مجيء إلخ وإن لم يصم الثلاثة حتى دخل يوم النحر لم يجزه الصوم أصلا، وصار الدم متعينا؛ لأن الصوم بدل، والأبدال لا تنصب إلا شرعا والنص خصه بوقت ،الحج، وجواز الدم على الأصل. واعلم أن شرط إجزائها وجود الإحرام بالعمرة في أشهر الحج وإن كان في شوال وكلما أخرها إلى آخر وقتها فهو أفضل لرجاء أن يدرك الهدي، ولذا كان الأفضل أن يجعلها السابع من ذي الحجة، ويوم التروية، ويوم عرفة، وأما صوم السبعة فلا يجوز تقديمه على الرجوع عن منى بعد إتمام أعمال الواجبات؛ لأنه معلق بالرجوع، قال تعالى: ﴿وَسَبْعَةِ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ [البقرة: ١٩٦] والمعلق بالشرط عدم قبل وجوده، فتقديمه عليه تقديم على وقته، الثلاثة، فإنه تعالى أمر به في الحج، قال تعالى: ﴿فَصِيَامُ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَّ [البقرة: ١٩٦] والمراد: وقته؛ لاستحالة كون أعماله ظرفا له، فإذا صام بعد الإحرام بالعمرة في أشهر الحج، فقد صام في وقته فيجوز، فإن قدر على الهدي في خلال الثلاثة أو بعدها قبل يوم النحر لزمه الهدي، وسقط الصوم؛ لأنه خلف، وإذا قدر على الأصل قبل تأدّي الحكم بالخلف بطل الخلف، وإن قدر عليه بعد الحلق قبل أن يصوم السبعة في أيام الذبح أو بعدها، لم يلزمه الهدي؛ لأن التحلل قد حصل بالحلق، فوجود الأصل بعده لا ينقض الخلف، كرؤية المتيمم الماء بعد الصلاة بالتيمم، وكذا لو لم يجد حتى مضت أيام الذبح، ثم وجد الهدي؛ لأن الذبح موقت بأيام النحر، فإذا مضت فقد حصل المقصود، وهو إباحة التحلل بلا هدي وكأنه تحلّل ثم وجده، ولو صام في وقته مع وجود الهدي ينظر، فإن بقي الهدي إلى يوم النحر لم يجزه؛ للقدرة على الأصل، وإن هلك قبل الذبح جاز؛ للعجز عن الأصل، فكان المعتبر وقت التحلل [فتح القدير : ٤١٨/٢، والبحر الرائق]
بخلاف
من
صوم
الميقات: هو للاحتراز عن مكة، فإنه ليس لأهلها تمتع ولا قران لا للاحتراز عن دويرة أهله أو غيرها، ولم يقيد إحرامها بأشهر الحج؛ لأنه ليس بشرط، لكن أداء أكثر طوافها فيها شرط، فلو طاف الأقل في رمضان مثلا، ثم طاف الباقي في شوال، ثم حج من عامه كان متمتعا البحر الرائق بحذف: ٥٥٢/٢]
Book of Hajj. 265. Explanation of Tamattu'. If he does not find [a sacrifice], then fasting three days before the coming of the Day of Sacrifice from the months of Hajj, and seven days after completing Hajj, even if in Mecca after the days of Tashriq, and if he separates them it is permissible. Chapter on Tamattu': Tamattu' is that one enters ihram only for Umrah from the miqat. Three days: Al-Tahtawi said its last is the Day of Arafah etc. In Al-Bahr: it is an explanation of what is best; otherwise its time is the time of Hajj after entering ihram for Umrah because what is meant by 'Hajj' in the verse 'fifty three days in the Hajj' (2:196) is its time, because the Hajj itself cannot be a receptacle. The best is to delay because fasting is badal for the hady, so it is recommended to delay until the end of its time hoping to be able to do the original before it comes. If he does not fast the three until the Day of Sacrifice enters, fasting does not avail him at all, and the blood becomes definite because fasting is badal, and badals are not established except by Sharia, and the text specified it to the time of Hajj, and the permissibility of blood is on the original. Know that the condition of its validity is the existence of ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj even if it is in Shawwal. The more he delays it to its last time is better, hoping to obtain the hady. So it is best to make it the seventh of Dhul Hijjah, the Day of Tarwiyah, and the Day of Arafah. As for fasting the seven, it is not permissible to advance before returning from Mina after completing the wajibat because it is conditioned upon returning. Allah says 'and seven when you return' (2:196). What is conditioned does not exist before the condition, so advancing it is advancing it before its time. The three: He commanded it in the Hajj; what is meant is its time. So if he fasts after ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj, he has fasted in its time and it is permissible. If he is able to perform hady during the three or after before the Day of Sacrifice, hady becomes incumbent and the fasting falls because it is badal. If he is able to perform the original before the performance of the ruling by badal, the badal becomes invalid. If he is able after halq before he fasts the seven in the days of sacrifice or after, hady does not become incumbent because tahlul has occurred by halq. So the existence of the original after it does not annul the badal, like the case of the mutayammim seeing water after prayer with tayammum. Similarly, if he does not find until the days of sacrifice pass, then finds hady, because sacrifice is time-bound to the days of Nahr. When they pass, the objective is achieved, which is the permissibility of tahlul without hady, as if he had tahlul and then found it. If he fasts in its time while hady exists, then: if the hady remains until the Day of Sacrifice, it does not suffice, due to ability over the original. If it perishes before slaughter, it is permissible, due to inability. So the consideration is the time of tahlul. [Fath al-Qadir 2:418 and Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq] Contrary to fasting of [the one who is]... Miqat: it is to exclude Mecca, because its residents do not have tamattu' or qiran, and it is not to exclude one's own dwelling or others. The ihram for Umrah is not restricted to the months of Hajj because it is not a condition, but performing most of its tawaf therein is a condition. So if he performed the lesser part in Ramadan, then performed the rest in Shawwal, then performed Hajj in the same year, he is a mutamatti'. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq with abridgement: 2:552]
Source pages p. 266

Commentary
This passage defines Tamattu' (تمتع), which consists of performing Umrah first during the months of Hajj and then Hajj in the same year without returning home between them. The pilgrim must sacrifice a hady (animal) as an obligation; if he cannot afford it, he must fast three days during the Hajj season (before the Day of Sacrifice, best on 7th, Day of Tarwiyah, and Day of Arafah) and seven days after completing the Hajj (even after returning home). The commentary explains that the three-day fast is a substitute (badal) for the sacrifice and is valid from the moment of ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj. The seven-day fast is conditioned upon returning from Mina after completing the wajibat. The passage discusses complex scenarios: if one becomes able to sacrifice before the Day of Sacrifice, the fast is replaced by the sacrifice; if able after tahlul (halq), the sacrifice is not required because tahlul has already occurred. This is analogous to tayammum becoming void upon seeing water only before prayer. The miqat condition ensures that residents of Mecca do not have tamattu' or qiran because they are not traveling from the miqat. The lesson includes the Hanafi position on timing and conditions for the fasting substitute.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing Umrah during the months of Hajj, then Hajj in the same year without returning home.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal for tamattu' and qiran, obligatory for those who are not residents of Mecca.
البدل (al-badal): The substitute (fasting) for the sacrifice when unable; it is only valid if the original cannot be performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, if a mutamatti' cannot sacrifice and chooses to fast, when must he complete the seven-day fast?
A) Before the Day of Sacrifice
B) Immediately upon entering ihram for Hajj
C) After returning from Mina and completing the wajibat
D) During the days of Tashriq only

Key Takeaway
Tamattu' requires a sacrifice; if unable, one must fast three days during the hajj season (after ihram for umrah) and seven days after returning from Mina, with careful rules on when the substitute remains valid.

The Sunnah of Umrah and Its Actions
States the ruling and actions of Umrah with commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of Umrah and list its required actions.

Core Idea
Umrah is a confirmed sunnah, valid anytime, with four actions: ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and hair removal.

This passage from Nur al-Idah establishes the legal ruling of Umrah and outlines its constitutive actions. While Umrah is not obligatory like Hajj, it is a highly recommended act of worship that can be performed throughout the year, with special merit in Ramadan. The author also clarifies details regarding the choice between shaving and shortening hair, and the case of a mutamatti' who brought a hadi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the legal classification of Umrah according to the Hanafi school.
The passage explicitly states 'العمرة سنة' (Umrah is sunnah).
2
List the required actions
Identify the essential components (arkan) of Umrah as mentioned in the text.
Ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir are the four actions.
3
Note the conditions for validity
Understand when Umrah is valid and any exceptions mentioned.
Valid throughout the year; specific rulings on hair condition and prohibition for mutamatti' with hadi.
4
Understand restrictions for mutamatti' with hadi
Learn the extra rule for those performing tamattu' who have brought a sacrificial animal.
They do not perform tahallul from Umrah; shaving requires a dam.
5
Note additional virtues
Recognize the recommended times and virtues mentioned in the commentaries.
Umrah in Ramadan is best; the Day of Tarwiyah is a permissible but not mandatory time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في العمرة]
العمرة سنة وتصح في جميع السنة
ثم يحلق: إنما ذكر الحلق لبيان تمام أفعال العمرة، لا لأنه شرط في التمتع؛ لأنه مخير بينه وبين بقائه محرما بها إلى أن يدخل إحرام الحج، ولا يرد عليه المتمتع الذي ساق الهدي فإنه لا يجوز له الحلق للعمرة، حتى لو حلق لها لزمه دم؛ لأن سوق الهدي عارض منعه من التحلل على خلاف الأصل. [البحر الرائق: 552/2] أو يقصر: قال شيخ الإسلام في "مبسوطه": هذا التخيير إنما كان له إذا لم يكن شعره ملبدا، أو معقوصا أو مضفرا، وأما إذا كان ملبدا، فإنه لا يتخير؛ لأن التقصير لا يتهيأ إلا بالقص، وذلك متعذر فيتعين الحلق. [العناية 422/2] يوم التروية: وهو الثامن من ذي الحجة، بيان للجواز، وإلا فالأفضل أن يكون قبله للمسارعة إلى الخير. [البحر الرائق: 553/2] من الحرم بيان للميقات المكاني لأهل مكة. [البحر الرائق: 553/2] صام بعد إحرامها في أشهر الحج. (حاشية الطحطاوي العمرة سنة وهي إحرام وطواف وسعي، وحلق أو تقصير. (الدر المختار: 472/2)] أي إذا أتى بها مرة فقد أقام السنة، غير مقيد بوقت غير ما ثبت النهي عنها، إلا أنها في رمضان أفضل، هذا إذا أفردها، فلا ينافيه أن القران أفضل؛ لأن ذلك أمر يرجع إلى الحج لا العمرة. [رد المحتار: 472/2]
Section on Umrah. Umrah is sunnah and is valid throughout the entire year. Then he shaves: He mentioned shaving only to indicate the completion of the actions of Umrah, not because it is a condition for tamattu'; because he is given a choice between shaving and remaining in ihram for it until he enters the ihram of Hajj. This does not apply to the mutamatti' who brought a hadi, for it is not permissible for him to shave for Umrah; even if he shaves for it, a blood sacrifice is required because bringing the hadi is an obstacle that prevents him from tahallul contrary to the original. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/552] Or he shortens: Shaykh al-Islam said in his Mabsut: This option is for him if his hair is not matted, braided, or plaited. If it is matted, then he does not have a choice because shortening cannot be done except by cutting, which is difficult, so shaving becomes determined. [al-Inayah 2/422] The Day of Tarwiyah: it is the 8th of Dhu al-Hijjah, an explanation of permissibility; otherwise, it is better to be before it to hasten to good. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/553] From the Haram: an explanation of the place miqat for the people of Makkah. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/553] He fasted after its ihram in the months of Hajj. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: Umrah is sunnah and it is ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or shortening. (al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2/472)) Meaning: if one performs it once, he has established the sunnah, not restricted to a time other than what the prohibition is established against, except that it is best in Ramadan. This is when he performs it alone; it does not contradict that qiran is better because that pertains to Hajj, not Umrah. [Radd al-Muhtar 2/472]
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage from the section on Umrah states the ruling that Umrah is a sunnah (recommended) act, valid at any time of the year. It then explains details related to the actions of Umrah. First, shaving (halq) or shortening (taqsir) of hair: for the mutamatti' who does not bring a hadi, he has a choice between shaving and shortening after completing the tawaf and sa'y. However, if he has brought a hadi, he does not perform tahallul from Umrah; he remains in ihram until he completes Hajj. If such a person shaves for Umrah, he must offer a blood sacrifice (dam) because bringing the hadi prevents him from early tahallul. Second, the option to shorten is only valid if the hair is not matted, braided, or plaited; if it is matted, only shaving is possible. The passage also notes that the Day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhu al-Hijjah) for entering ihram of Hajj is merely a permissible time, but it is better to do so earlier to hasten to good. The miqat (place of entering ihram) for Makkans is the Haram itself. Finally, it confirms the summary definition of Umrah: ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir. The virtue of Umrah in Ramadan is mentioned as best, but performing it alone does not contradict that qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) is better overall, since qiran concerns Hajj.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): A visit to the Sacred Mosque in Mecca consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taqsir, valid at any time of the year.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet regularly performed; its omission is not sinful but leaves reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a mutamatti' who brings a hadi and then shaves his head for Umrah?
A) It is permissible and he becomes halal.
B) It is not permissible and he must offer a blood sacrifice.
C) He must only shorten, not shave.
D) He must repeat the Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Umrah is a confirmed sunnah consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and hair removal, valid year-round, with special rules for mutamatti' who bring a hadi.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

'Umrah Procedure and Tamattu' Rulings
Procedural description with conditional ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the procedure of 'Umrah and distinguish the rulings for a mutamatti' who brings a hadiy versus one who does not.

Core Idea
For tamattu', bringing a sacrificial animal (hadiy) obligates remaining in ihram after 'Umrah until Hajj rituals.

This passage from Nur al-Idah details the actions of 'Umrah and the critical differentiation within tamattu'. Understanding when a pilgrim becomes halal is essential for correct practice, especially given the common confusion about the role of the hadiy.

Guided Path
1
Trace the 'Umrah sequence
List the steps of 'Umrah as described: supplication, talbiyah, tawaf with raml, two rak'ahs, sa'y, and halq/taqsir.
Note that talbiyah is cut at the start of tawaf.
2
Identify the decisive factor
Find the condition that splits the ruling: whether the pilgrim has brought a hadiy (sacrificial animal).
The text says: 'if he did not bring a hadiy' and 'if he brought a hadiy'.
3
Apply the condition to the ruling
Without hadiy: he shaves/trims and becomes halal. With hadiy: he does not become free from 'Umrah and remains in ihram.
Ruling applies specifically to the mutamatti'.
4
Connect to Hajj integration
For both cases, the pilgrim later assumes ihram for Hajj from the Haram on Tarwiyah day. The difference is the state of ihram in between 'Umrah and Hajj.
5
Handle the sacrifice obligation
After stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah, the mutamatti' must slaughter a sheep or share in a camel. If unable, alternative fasting is explained.
Fasting: 3 days before Nahr and 7 after return; if 3 days missed, slaughter becomes mandatory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيقول بعد صلاة ركعتي الإحرام: اللهم إني أريد العمرة فيسرها لي، وتقبلها مني، ثم يلبي حتى يدخل مكة، فيطوف لها، ويقطع التلبية بأول طوافه، ويرمل فيه، ثم يصلي ركعتي الطواف ثم يسعى بين الصفا والمروة بعد الوقوف على الصفا - كما تقدم - سبعة أشواط، ثم يحلق رأسه أو يقصر إذا لم يسق الهدي، وحل له كل شيء من الجماع ،وغيره ويستمر حلالا وإن ساق الهدي لا يتحلل من عمرته، فإذا جاء يوم التروية يحرم بالحج من الحرم ويخرج إلى منى، فإذا رمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر لزمه ذبح شاة أو سبع ،بدنة، فإن لم يجد صام ثلاثة أيام قبل مجيء يوم النحر، وسبعة إذا رجع كالقارن، فإن لم يصم الثلاثة حتى جاء يوم النحر تعين عليه ذبح شاة، ولا يجزئه صوم، ولا صدقة.
He says after praying the two rak'ahs of ihram: 'O Allah, I intend 'Umrah, so make it easy for me and accept it from me.' Then he recites talbiyah until he enters Mecca, then performs tawaf for it, cutting off talbiyah at the start of his tawaf, and does raml in it. Then he prays two rak'ahs of tawaf, then performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah after standing on Safa - as previously mentioned - seven circuits. Then he shaves his head or shortens (his hair) if he did not bring a hadiy, and everything (including) intercourse and other things becomes permissible for him, and he remains in a state of halal. But if he brought a hadiy, he does not become free from his 'Umrah. Then when the day of Tarwiyah comes, he enters ihram for Hajj from the Haram and goes out to Mina. Then when he throws the Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he is obliged to slaughter a sheep or one-seventh of a camel. If he cannot, he fasts three days before the Day of Nahr and seven days when he returns, like the qarin. If he does not fast the three days until the Day of Nahr comes, he is obligated to slaughter a sheep, and fasting nor charity suffices for him.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the procedure for 'Umrah, specifically in the context of tamattu' (combining 'Umrah and Hajj with a break in between). The text follows the Hanafi school. It begins with the supplication at the miqat, then the acts of 'Umrah: entering Mecca, tawaf with raml (quick pace) for the first three circuits, two rak'ahs after tawaf, sa'y between Safa and Marwah. After sa'y, the mutamatti' who did not bring a hadiy (sacrificial animal) may shave or trim his hair, thereby concluding his 'Umrah and becoming halal (permissible to resume ordinary life including marital relations). However, if he brought a hadiy, he must remain in ihram and cannot perform halq (shaving) until after the Hajj rituals. On the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah), he assumes ihram for Hajj from the Haram and goes to Mina. After stoning the Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the 10th, he is required to slaughter a sheep or share in a camel. If he cannot afford it, he must fast three days before the Day of Nahr and seven days after returning home, just like the qarin (one who performs Hajj and 'Umrah combined). If he misses fasting the three days before the Day of Nahr, then the obligation becomes slaughtering a sheep; fasting or charity is not acceptable as a substitute.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah during the Hajj season and then performing Hajj in the same year with a break in between.
الهدي (al-hadiy): A sacrificial animal brought to the Haram by pilgrims performing tamattu' or qiran.
القارن (al-qarin): One who combines the intentions of Hajj and 'Umrah from a single ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hadiy) regarding the conclusion of 'Umrah?
A) He may shave his head and become halal immediately after sa'y.
B) He must remain in ihram and cannot shave until after the Hajj rituals.
C) He must fast three days before shaving.
D) He must slaughter the animal before the 'Umrah.

Key Takeaway
Whether a mutamatti' becomes halal after 'Umrah depends solely on whether he has brought a hadiy; without hadiy, he is halal; with hadiy, he must remain in ihram.

Ruling on 'Umrah: Sunnah and Valid Throughout the Year
States that 'Umrah is sunnah and valid any time, explains hair cutting and timing of ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah, identify its permissible times, and explain the rules for hair removal after 'Umrah, including the exception for the mutamatti' who brought a hadiy.

Core Idea
'Umrah is a highly recommended sunnah, valid any time of year, with the best time being Ramadan.

This lesson covers the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah from Nur al-Idah. The source text states clearly that 'Umrah is sunnah and can be performed throughout the entire year. The accompanying commentaries clarify the actions of 'Umrah, especially the options for hair removal and the special case of the mutamatti' who brings a hadiy. We will unpack these rulings step by step, understanding the legal reasoning behind each detail.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Ruling
The matn states: 'العمرة سنة' — 'Umrah is sunnah. In Hanafi fiqh, this means sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), which carries a reward but is not obligatory. This is the foundational hukm.
2
Recognize the Temporal Validity
The text says 'وتصح في جميع السنة' — valid throughout the year. This means 'Umrah can be performed any day except the three days of tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) and possibly the day of Arafah and Nahr, though not mentioned here explicitly.
The commentary from Radd al-Muhtar adds that it is best in Ramadan, but not restricted to it.
3
Analyze the Two Hair Removal Options
After completing the rituals, one may either shave (halq) or trim (taqsir). The text clarifies that shaving is not a condition for tamattu' but merely indicates the completion of 'Umrah. However, if the hair is matted (mulabbad), shaving becomes obligatory because trimming would be difficult.
The source cites Al-Inayah for this ruling.
4
Examine the Mutamatti' with Hadiy
A mutamatti' who has brought a sacrificial animal (hadiy) is not permitted to shave after 'Umrah. If he does, he owes a dam (compensatory sacrifice). The hadiy prevents him from exiting ihram until Hajj begins.
This is an exception to the general permissibility of shaving after 'Umrah.
5
Note the Spatial Miqat for Meccans
For people of Mecca, the miqat for Hajj is from the Haram itself (i.e., they can assume ihram from their homes). The day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah) is mentioned as a permissible time, but it is better to do it earlier.
This is from Al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في العمرة] العمرة سنة وتصح في جميع السنة ثم يحلق: إنما ذكر الحلق لبيان تمام أفعال العمرة، لا لأنه شرط في التمتع؛ لأنه مخير بينه وبين بقائه محرما بها إلى أن يدخل إحرام الحج، ولا يرد عليه المتمتع الذي ساق الهدي فإنه لا يجوز له الحلق للعمرة، حتى لو حلق لها لزمه دم؛ لأن سوق الهدي عارض منعه من التحلل على خلاف الأصل. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٢/٢] أو يقصر: قال شيخ الإسلام في "مبسوطه": هذا التخيير إنما كان له إذا لم يكن شعره ملبدا، أو معقوصا أو مضفرا، وأما إذا كان ملبدا، فإنه لا يتخير؛ لأن التقصير لا يتهيأ إلا بالقص، وذلك متعذر فيتعين الحلق. [العناية ٤٢٢/٢] يوم التروية: وهو الثامن من ذي الحجة، بيان للجواز، وإلا فالأفضل أن يكون قبله للمسارعة إلى الخير. [البحر الرائق: ٥٥٣/٢] من الحرم بيان للميقات المكاني لأهل مكة. البحر الرائق: ٥٥٣/٢] صام بعد إحرامها في أشهر الحج. (حاشية الطحطاوي العمرة سنة وهي إحرام وطواف وسعي، وحلق أو تقصير. (الدر المختار: ٤٧٢/٢)] أي إذا أتى بها مرة فقد أقام السنة، غير مقيد بوقت غير ما ثبت النهي عنها، إلا أنها في رمضان أفضل، هذا إذا أفردها، فلا ينافيه أن القران أفضل؛ لأن ذلك أمر يرجع إلى الحج لا العمرة. [رد المحتار: ٤٧٢/٢]
Chapter on 'Umrah: 'Umrah is sunnah and valid throughout the entire year. Then he shaves: He mentioned shaving only to indicate the completion of the actions of 'Umrah, not because it is a condition for tamattu'; for he is given a choice between it and remaining in ihram with it until he enters the ihram of Hajj. It does not apply to the mutamatti' who brought a hadiy, for he is not permitted to shave for 'Umrah; even if he shaved for it, he would owe a dam, because bringing the hadiy is a preventing factor that prevents him from becoming free contrary to the principle. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/552] Or he shortens: Shaykh al-Islam said in his Mabsut: This choice was given to him when his hair is not matted, or knotted, or braided. But if it is matted, then he has no choice, because shortening is only possible by cutting, and that is difficult, so shaving becomes necessary. [Al-Inayah 2/422] Day of Tarwiyah: It is the eighth of Dhul Hijjah, an explanation of permissibility; otherwise it is better to do it before to hasten to goodness. [Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/553] From the Haram: explanation of the spatial miqat for the people of Mecca. Al-Bahr al-Raiq 2/553] He fasted after its ihram in the months of Hajj. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 'Umrah is sunnah, and it consists of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or shortening. (Al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2/472)] That is, if he performs it once, he has established the sunnah, not restricted to a time other than what is established of prohibition, except that it is best in Ramadan. This applies when he performs it individually; it does not contradict that qiran is better, because that relates to Hajj, not 'Umrah. [Radd al-Muhtar 2/472]
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This is a self-contained chapter on 'Umrah. The author states the fundamental ruling: 'Umrah is sunnah (a highly recommended act) and valid at any time of the year. The commentary elaborates on several points: First, regarding shaving (halq) after 'Umrah—this is only to mark completion, not a condition for tamattu'. The mutamatti' may choose to shave or remain in ihram until Hajj. However, if he brought a hadiy, he cannot shave, and doing so would require a compensatory sacrifice (dam). Second, shortening (taqsir) is only an option if the hair is not matted or braided; if it is matted, shaving is necessary because cutting such hair is difficult. Third, the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah) is mentioned as a permissible time to assume ihram for Hajj from the Haram, though it is better to do so earlier. Fourth, the 'from the Haram' indicates the spatial miqat for Meccans. The commentary from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi and Radd al-Muhtar summarizes: 'Umrah's pillars are ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and shaving/trimming; performing it once is sufficient; it is best in Ramadan; and its virtue does not conflict with qiran (combined Hajj and 'Umrah) being better overall.

Key Terms
التقصير (al-taqsir): Trimming or shortening the hair, an alternative to shaving (halq) at the end of 'Umrah or Hajj.
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs 'Umrah first during the Hajj season, then performs Hajj later in the same year.
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head completely, one of the two options for hair removal after 'Umrah or Hajj.
الهدي (al-hadiy): A sacrificial animal brought by a pilgrim performing tamattu' or qiran, or as an offering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only in the month of Ramadan
B) Only during the days of Hajj
C) Any time of the year except the prohibited days of tashreeq
D) Only on Fridays

Key Takeaway
'Umrah is a sunnah mu'akkadah that can be performed at any time of the year, with the best time being Ramadan, and the mutamatti' with a hadiy cannot shave after 'Umrah.

Initiating 'Umrah on Arafah, Nahr, and Tashreeq: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with commentary expanding on the karahah and its exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on initiating 'Umrah on the days of Arafah, Nahr, and Tashreeq, identify the consequence (dam), and explain the exception for performing 'Umrah with a prior ihram.

Core Idea
Initiating a new 'Umrah on these Hajj days is makruh tahrimi and incurs a dam, even if abandoned.

This passage addresses a common situation: a pilgrim in Mecca during the days of Hajj who wishes to perform an additional 'Umrah. The Hanafi school holds that initiating a new 'Umrah on these specific days is disliked (makruh tahrimi) and, if done, requires a blood offering (dam). However, if one is already in ihram for 'Umrah from before, there is no dislike. The passage also explains the proper method of 'Umrah for Meccans and those coming from outside the miqat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is initiating a new 'Umrah on the day of 'Arafah, Nahr, or Tashreeq. The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh) and obligates a blood sacrifice (dam).
This is a distinct ruling from performing 'Umrah on these days with a prior ihram.
2
Recognize the exception
If one performs 'Umrah on these days with a prior ihram (e.g., due to a missed Hajj), it is not disliked. The karahah is only for initiating a new 'Umrah.
The text says 'لا أداؤها فيها بالإحرام السابق'.
3
Understand the method of 'Umrah
For a Meccan, ihram for 'Umrah is from the Hal area outside the Haram; for Hajj, it is from the Haram. For an afaqi (non-Meccan), ihram is from the miqat when entering Mecca.
The passage contrasts 'Umrah and Hajj ihram locations.
4
Note the consequence even if abandoned
The dam is obligatory even if the initiated 'Umrah is abandoned. This shows the severity of the disliked act.
Text: 'حتى يلزمه دمّ وإن كان رفضها'.
5
Distinguish afaqi's obligation
The afaqi must assume ihram at the miqat only if he intends to enter Mecca. If he passes the miqat for another purpose, he does not need ihram.
Example of a Kufan entering a garden of Bani 'Amir without intending Mecca.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكره يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وأيام التشريق، وكيفيتها: أن يحرم لها من مكة من الحل، بخلاف إحرامه للحج، فإنه من الحرم، وأما الآفاقي الذي لم يدخل مكة فيحرم إذا قصدها من الميقات ثم يطوف ويسعى لها، ثم يحلق، وقد حل منها كما بيناه بحمد الله. وتكره أي كره إنشاء الإحرام لها في هذه الأيام حتى يلزمه دمّ وإن كان رفضها، لا أداؤها فيها بالإحرام السابق كفائت الحج، فاعتمر فيها لم يكره يوم عرفة أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان قبل الزوال أو بعده. وأما الآفاقي: يعني أن وجوب الإحرام لمن أراد دخول مكة مقيد بما إذا أراده عند المواقيت، وإلا فلا يجب عليه الإحرام، كما إذا أراد كوفي دخول بستان بني عامر لحاجة لا دخول مكة، ثم أراد دخولها، فيجوز له أن يدخل مكة من غير إحرام.
And it is disliked (makruh) on the day of 'Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashreeq. And its method: that he assumes ihram for it from Mecca from the Hal, unlike his ihram for Hajj, which is from the Haram. As for the afaqi (person from outside the miqat) who has not entered Mecca, he assumes ihram when he intends it from the miqat, then performs tawaf and sa'y for it, then shaves, and he has become free from it as we explained, by the praise of Allah. And it is disliked—meaning, it is disliked to initiate ihram for it during these days, such that it obligates a blood offering even if he abandons it; but performing it during them with a prior ihram, like a missed Hajj, is not disliked. So if one performs 'Umrah during it on the day of 'Arafah, it is not disliked—this is general, covering before or after noon. And regarding the afaqi: it means that the obligation of ihram for one who intends to enter Mecca is conditioned upon his intending it at the miqat; otherwise, ihram is not obligatory upon him. For example, if a Kufan intends to enter the garden of Bani 'Amir for a need, not entering Mecca, then later intends to enter it, he may enter Mecca without ihram.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on the time for 'Umrah. The author states that it is makruh (disliked, but not haram) to initiate the ihram for 'Umrah on the day of 'Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah), the day of Nahr (10th), and the days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th). However, if one performs 'Umrah during these days with a pre-existing ihram (e.g., if one forgot and was in ihram from before), it is not disliked. The commentary clarifies that the dislike is for initiating a new 'Umrah; if one performs 'Umrah on the day of 'Arafah with a prior ihram (like one who missed Hajj), it is not makruh. The method of 'Umrah for the resident of Mecca is to enter ihram from the 'Hal' area outside the Haram, whereas for Hajj, the Meccan enters ihram from the Haram. For the afaqi (a non-Meccan who has not entered Mecca), he must enter ihram from the miqat appropriate for his direction. The commentary also distinguishes the obligation of ihram: it is only required when one intends to enter Mecca itself; if one passes the miqat for another purpose, he does not need to assume ihram.

Key Terms
الآفاقي (al-afaqi): A person who lives outside the miqat boundaries (afaq al-ard), for whom it is obligatory to assume ihram at the miqat when intending Hajj or 'Umrah.
إنشاء الإحرام (insha' al-ihram): Initiating a new state of ihram for a pilgrimage act (as opposed to continuing a previous ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is not disliked.
C) It is invalid.
D) It is sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Initiating 'Umrah on Arafah, Nahr, or Tashreeq is disliked and requires a dam, but performing 'Umrah with a prior ihram is not disliked.

Evaluating the Hadith on 'Arafah Friday's Virtue
Critical refinement of a hadith claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the claimed hadith about 'Arafah on Friday being better than seventy Hajj, and evaluate its authenticity based on the criticism of hadith scholars such as al-Munawi and Ibn Hajar.

Core Idea
The hadith claiming 'Arafah on Friday equals seventy Hajj is false (batil) according to leading hadith experts.

This lesson examines a specific claim about the virtue of 'Arafah when it falls on Friday. While the day itself is undoubtedly virtuous, some sources report a hadith stating it is better than seventy Hajj on other days. We will follow the Hanafi commentators' critical refinement of this report, distinguishing between established virtues and unverified narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed virtue
Read the passage to find the specific claim: that the day of 'Arafah coinciding with Friday is better than seventy Hajj performed on other days.
This claim is attributed to a marfu' hadith, but the chain is questionable.
2
Examine the source citation
Note how the author cites the claim: from 'Ma'raj al-Dirayah', 'Tajrid al-Sihah', and al-Zayla'i. Understand that these are Hanafi sources that initially present the hadith, but then the critical voices appear.
The author uses 'however' (لكن) to shift to criticism.
3
Consider the criticism of hadith scholars
Read al-Munawi's statement: the hadith is batil (false) and has no basis. Also note Ibn Hajar's analysis: the report from Ruzeyn is unknown, not in the Muwatta', and lacks a companion narrator.
Ibn Hajar points out that the addition of 'seventy Hajj' is not found in any Muwatta' work.
4
Evaluate the overall status
Conclude that while the virtue of 'Arafah and Friday is affirmed by other evidence (e.g., the revelation of Ayah al-Ikmal, the Prophet's statement about two 'ids), this specific reward (seventy Hajj) is not authenticated and is rejected by many scholars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه وأفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق يوم الجمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير جمعة، رواه صاحب معراج الدراية" بقوله : وقد صح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: أفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق جمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة، ذكره في تجريد" "الصحاح" بعلامة الموطأ، وكذا قاله الزيلعي له شارح "الكنز"، وقد صح إلخ لكن نقل المناوي عن بعض الحفاظ: أن هذا حديث باطل لا أصل له، نعم ذكر الغزالي في "الإحياء": قال بعض السلف : إذا وافق يوم عرفة يوم جمعة غفر لكل أهل عرفة، وهو أفضل يوم في الدنيا، وفيه: حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حجة الوداع، وكان واقفا إذا نزل قوله تعالى: ﴿الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتْمَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي [المائدة: ۳] ، فقال أهل الكتاب: لو أنزلت هذه الآية علينا لجعلناه يوم عيد، فقال ه: أشهد لقد أنزلت في يوم عيدين اثنين: يوم عرفة ويوم جمعة على رسول الله وهو واقف بعرفة. عمر رد المحتار: ٦٢١/٢] بعلامة الموطأ : قال شيخ الإسلام الحافظ ابن حجر له في "شرح البخاري" في تفسير المائدة عند قول البخاري: باب قوله أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ [المائدة: ۳] في أثناء كلامه ما نصه وأما ما ذكره رزين في جامعه مرفوعا: سبعين حجة في غيرها"، فهو حديث يوم جمعة وهو أفضل من "خير طلعت فيه الشمس يوم عرف عرفة وافق يوم . لا أعرفه؛ لأنه لم يذكر صحابيه ولا من خرجه، بل أدرجه في حديث الموطأ الذي ذكره مرسلا عن بن جرير، وليست الزيادة في شيء من الموطآت. شلبي على الكنــ عبيد الله طلحة بن
Notice: The best of days is the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj in other than Friday. This was narrated by the author of Ma'raj al-Dirayah, saying: It has been authenticated from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, that he said: The best of days is the day of 'Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj. He mentioned it in Tajrid al-Sihah with the mark of the Muwatta', and likewise al-Zayla'i said it for him, the commentator of al-Kanz. And it has been authenticated, etc. However, al-Munawi quoted from some hadith memorizers that this hadith is false and has no basis. Yes, al-Ghazali mentioned in al-Ihya': Some of the Salaf said: If the day of 'Arafah coincides with Friday, forgiveness is granted to all of Arafah, and it is the best day in the world. And in it: The Messenger of Allah performed the Farewell Hajj, and he was standing when the verse descended: {Today I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you} [al-Ma'idah 5:3]. The People of the Book said: If this verse had been revealed to us, we would have taken it as a festival day. He (the Prophet) said: I bear witness that it was revealed on two festival days: the day of 'Arafah and Friday, upon the Messenger of Allah while he was standing at 'Arafah. (from Radd al-Muhtar 2/621) with the mark of the Muwatta': Shaykh al-Islam al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in his commentary on al-Bukhari in the interpretation of al-Ma'idah when al-Bukhari said: Chapter on the saying of Allah {Today I have perfected for you your religion}, in the course of his speech: As for what Ruzayn mentioned in his Jami' as a marfu' hadith: "Seventy Hajj in other than it" — this is a hadith... I do not know it, because he did not mention its companion nor who narrated it; rather he inserted it into the hadith of the Muwatta' which he mentioned as mursal from Ibn Jarir, and the addition is not found in any of the Muwatta' works. (al-Shalabi on al-Kanz)...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement regarding the virtue of the day of 'Arafah when it falls on Friday. The author reports that some sources claim a hadith stating that 'Arafah on Friday is better than seventy Hajj on other days. However, the author also transmits the criticism of this hadith by al-Munawi and other hadith authorities, who declare it false (batil) and without foundation. The text then recounts a story from al-Ghazali's Ihya' that when the verse of completion (al-Ma'idah 5:3) was revealed on the day of 'Arafah which was Friday, the Prophet said it was revealed on two festivals. But Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani, a leading hadith critic, states that the report from Ruzeyn about 'seventy Hajj' is unknown and not found in the Muwatta'. Thus, while the virtue of 'Arafah and Friday is affirmed, the specific claim of seventy Hajj is rejected by many scholars. The passage ends with commentary from al-Shalabi on al-Kanz.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): An invalid or false hadith with no authentic chain.
مرسل (mursal): A hadith in which the Companion is omitted from the chain.
معراج الدراية (Ma'raj al-Dirayah): A work by a Hanafi scholar (probably al-Muhaddith al-Kashmiri or similar) that gathers hadith used in fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is authentic (sahih) and widely accepted.
B) It is considered false (batil) by many hadith experts.
C) It is only found in the Muwatta'.
D) It is agreed upon by all scholars.

Key Takeaway
The hadith that 'Arafah on Friday is better than seventy Hajj is not authentic; stick to verified virtues.

When Initiating Umrah is Disliked
Ruling on makruh times for Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four days on which starting Ihram for Umrah is makruh and explain the reason for the dislike.

Core Idea
Starting Umrah on the Day of Arafah, Nahr, or Tashreeq is makruh because those days are exclusively for Hajj.

This lesson covers a specific ruling from Nur al-Idah: it is disliked (makruh) to initiate Ihram for Umrah on four days of the Hajj season. We will learn those days and why the Hanafi school holds this view. Note that performing Umrah on these days if already in Ihram is not disliked; only the beginning is affected.

Guided Path
1
Identify the days
The passage lists: يوم عرفة (Day of Arafah, 9th Dhul Hijjah), يوم النحر (Day of Nahr, 10th), and أيام التشريق (Days of Tashreeq, 11th, 12th, 13th). So there are four specific days.
2
Understand the scope of karahah
The dislike applies only to starting a new Umrah by entering Ihram on these days. Performing the actions of an ongoing Umrah (if Ihram was entered earlier) is not disliked.
This is a common source of confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان العمرة وتكره يوم عرفة ويوم النحر وأيام التشريق، وكيفيتها: أن يحرم لها من مكة من الحل، بخلاف إحرامه للحج، فإنه من الحرم، وأما الآفاقي الذي لم يدخل مكة فيحرم إذا قصدها من الميقات ثم يطوف ويسعى لها، ثم يحلق، وقد حل منها كما بيناه بحمد الله.
Chapter of Umrah. And it is disliked on the Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq. Commentary
This passage states a ruling and a description of Umrah. First, it declares that initiating ihram for Umrah is makruh (disliked) on four days: the Day of Arafah (9th of Dhul Hijjah), the Day of Nahr (10th), and the three Days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th). This is because these days are dedicated to the rites of Hajj, and engaging in Umrah diverts attention from them. Key Terms
العمرة (al-umrah): A pilgrimage to Makkah consisting of tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir, performed at any time of the year except the five days when it is disliked.
الآفاقي (al-afaqi): A person who resides outside the Miqat boundaries.
الحل (al-hill): The area outside the Haram but within the miqat boundaries.

Where and How to Enter Ihram for Umrah
Description of Umrah rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the place of Ihram for Umrah for a Makkan resident (from al-hill) and for an afaqi (from the miqat), and describe the basic rites of Umrah.

Core Idea
For Umrah, a Makkan enters Ihram from al-hill; an afaqi enters from the miqat. Then tawaf, sa'y, and shaving complete the Umrah.

This lesson explains the method of Umrah as described in Nur al-Idah. We learn that the place of Ihram for Umrah differs from that of Hajj. A person in Makkah must go to the Hill (outside the Haram) to enter Ihram, while a person from outside the Miqat enters Ihram from his respective Miqat. Then the rites are tawaf, sa'y, and shaving or trimming.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of pilgrims
The text distinguishes between a person who is in Makkah (a resident or a visitor who has not left the Haram) and an afaqi (one who comes from outside the Miqat boundaries and has not yet entered Makkah).
2
Determine the place of Ihram for Umrah
For the person in Makkah, the Ihram for Umrah is taken from al-hill (the area outside the Haram but within the larger Haram boundary). For Hajj, it would be from al-Haram itself. For the afaqi, he enters Ihram from the Miqat when he intends to perform Umrah.
The contrast with Hajj is explicitly mentioned: bikhilafi ihramihi lil-hajj, fa innahu min al-haram.
3
Perform the rites
After entering Ihram from the correct place, the pilgrim performs Tawaf around the Kaaba, then Sa'y between Safa and Marwa, then shaves (halq) or trims (taqsir) the hair. This completes the Umrah.
The text says: thumma yatufu wa yas'a laha, thumma yahliq.

The Virtue of Arafah on Friday: Critical Hadith Analysis and Ruling
Critical hadith analysis and fiqh ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critically evaluate the hadith claiming seventy Hajj reward for Arafah on Friday and state the Hanafi ruling on initiating Umrah on that day.

Core Idea
A widely cited hadith about Arafah on Friday is not authentic; critical scrutiny is essential in fiqh.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents a hadith extolling the virtue of Arafah coinciding with Friday and then subjects it to rigorous criticism. It also reiterates the Hanafi ruling on initiating Umrah on that day. The lesson examines the tension between popular practice and scholarly verification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed virtue
The passage begins by citing a hadith that the best day is Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and that it is better than seventy Hajj without Friday.
This hadith is well-known among many Muslims.
2
Trace the citation chain
The author references Mirqat al-Dirayah and Tajrid al-Sihah, claiming the hadith is authentic and from the Muwatta.
This gives the hadith an appearance of reliability.
3
Examine the criticism
Al-Munawi and Ibn Hajar discredit the hadith: it is baseless, has no known chain, and is not found in any version of the Muwatta.
The criticism is methodological, focusing on transmission (sanad) and inclusion in reliable sources.
4
Observe the alternate narrative
Al-Ghazali in the Ihya' mentions a saying from the Salaf about forgiveness on Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and the story of the revelation of the perfection verse on that day.
These provide a basis for the day's virtue without relying on the weak hadith.
5
Connect to the fiqh ruling
The passage then returns to the ruling: initiating Umrah on the Day of Arafah is makruh tahrimi and requires a blood sacrifice (dam) if one does so.
This ruling stands regardless of the hadith's authenticity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه وأفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق يوم الجمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة في غير جمعة، رواه صاحب معراج الدراية بقوله : وقد صح عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: أفضل الأيام يوم عرفة إذا وافق جمعة، وهو أفضل من سبعين حجة، ذكره في تجريد الصحاح بعلامة الموطأ، وكذا قاله الزيلعي له شارح الكنز، وتكره أي كره إنشاء الإحرام لها في هذه الأيام حتى يلزمه دمّ وإن كان رفضها، لا أداؤها فيها بالإحرام السابق كفائت الحج، فاعتمر فيها لم يكره يوم عرفة أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان قبل الزوال أو بعده. وأما الآفاقي: يعني أن وجوب الإحرام لمن أراد دخول مكة مقيد بما إذا أراده عند المواقيت، وإلا فلا يجب عليه الإحرام، كما إذا أراد كوفي دخول بستان بني عامر لحاجة لا دخول مكة، ثم أراد دخولها، فيجوز له أن يدخل مكة من غير إحرام. وقد صح إلخ لكن نقل المناوي عن بعض الحفاظ: أن هذا حديث باطل لا أصل له، نعم ذكر الغزالي في الإحياء: قال بعض السلف : إذا وافق يوم عرفة يوم جمعة غفر لكل أهل عرفة، وهو أفضل يوم في الدنيا، وفيه: حج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حجة الوداع، وكان واقفا إذا نزل قوله تعالى: ﴿الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتْمَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي﴾ [المائدة: ۳] ، فقال أهل الكتاب: لو أنزلت هذه الآية علينا لجعلناه يوم عيد، فقال ه: أشهد لقد أنزلت في يوم عيدين اثنين: يوم عرفة ويوم جمعة على رسول الله وهو واقف بعرفة. عمر رد المحتار: ٦٢١/٢] بعلامة الموطأ : قال شيخ الإسلام الحافظ ابن حجر له في شرح البخاري في تفسير المائدة عند قول البخاري: باب قوله أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ [المائدة: ۳] في أثناء كلامه ما نصه وأما ما ذكره رزين في جامعه مرفوعا: سبعين حجة في غيرها، فهو حديث يوم جمعة وهو أفضل من خير طلعت فيه الشمس يوم عرف عرفة وافق يوم . لا أعرفه؛ لأنه لم يذكر صحابيه ولا من خرجه، بل أدرجه في حديث الموطأ الذي ذكره مرسلا عن بن جرير، وليست الزيادة في شيء من الموطآت. شلبي على الكنــ
Note: The best of days is the Day of Arafah if it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj without Friday. Reported by the author of Mirqat al-Dirayah with his statement: 'It is authentic from the Messenger of Allah (SAW) that he said: The best of days is the Day of Arafah when it coincides with Friday, and it is better than seventy Hajj.' Mentioned in Tajrid al-Sihah with the mark of Muwatta. Similarly said al-Zayla'i for him, the commentator of al-Kanz. And it is disliked, i.e., initiating ihram for Umrah on these days is disliked, so much so that he is obliged to give blood even if he abandons it, not performing it on those days with a prior ihram like a missed Hajj. So if he performs Umrah on those days, it is not disliked on the Day of Arafah, and it is general whether before or after zawal. As for the afaqi: meaning that the obligation of ihram for one who intends to enter Makkah is conditional upon intending it at the miqat; otherwise ihram is not obligatory upon him. For example, if a Kufan wishes to enter the garden of Bani Amir for a need without intending to enter Makkah, then he intends to enter it; then it is permissible for him to enter Makkah without ihram. It is authentic, etc. However, al-Munawi narrated from some preservers (of hadith) that this hadith is baseless, having no origin. Indeed, al-Ghazali mentioned in al-Ihya': Some predecessors said: If the Day of Arafah coincides with Friday, forgiveness is given to all people of Arafah, and it is the best day in the world. And in it: The Messenger of Allah (SAW) performed the Farewell Pilgrimage, and he was standing when the verse {Today I have perfected your religion...} was revealed. So the People of the Book said: If this verse were revealed to us, we would have made it a day of 'Eid. He (SAW) said: I bear witness that it was revealed on two 'Eids: the Day of Arafah and Friday, upon the Messenger of Allah while he stood at Arafah. 'Umar? Radd al-Muhtar 2/621 with mark of Muwatta: Shaykh al-Islam al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar said in Sharh al-Bukhari in tafsir of al-Ma'idah at the statement of al-Bukhari: Chapter: His statement {Today I have perfected your religion...} in the midst of his speech, the text: 'As for what Razin mentioned in his collection as marfu': 'Seventy Hajj without it' – it is a hadith which I do not know; because he did not mention its companion nor its narrator; rather he inserted it into the Muwatta hadith which he mentioned as mursal from Ibn Jarir. And the addition is not in any of the Muwattas.' Shalabi on al-Kanz...
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a comment (tanbih) that begins by mentioning a hadith about the superiority of Arafah falling on Friday, claiming it is better than seventy Hajj. The author cites sources like Mirqat al-Dirayah and Tajrid al-Sihah attributing it to the Muwatta. Then it returns to the ruling on Umrah, clarifying that the dislike (karaha) for initiating Umrah on these days is tahrimi such that blood (dam) is required. It also distinguishes between initiating ihram and performing actions of a prior ihram. Then it discusses the case of an afaqi who passes the miqat without intending to enter Makkah. After that, it critically examines the hadith: al-Munawi reports from some hadith scholars that it is baseless. Al-Ghazali in Ihya' mentions a similar saying from the Salaf, and recounts the story of the revelation of the verse of perfection. Finally, Ibn Hajar in his commentary on Bukhari criticizes the hadith, saying it is unknown and not in the Muwatta.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice (typically a sheep) required as compensation for violating the prohibition of initiating Umrah on the disliked days.
رفضها (rafadahu): Abandoning or aborting the ihram; if one abandons it after having started, he still owes the dam.
الآفاقي (al-afaqi): A person from outside miqat boundaries.
باطل لا أصل له (bāṭil lā aṣla lahu): Term used to describe a hadith that has no basis in any primary source; it is fabricated or baseless.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Weak (da'if) but still usable for virtues.
C) Baseless (bāṭil lā aṣla lahu) and not found in the Muwatta.
D) Good (hasan) and commonly cited.

Key Takeaway
The hadith claiming seventyfold virtue for Arafah on Friday is not authentic; the Hanafi ruling on initiating Umrah remains makruh tahrimi requiring dam.

Ruling on Residing in Mecca (Mujawara) – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States that continuous residence in Mecca is disliked according to Abu Hanifa and explains the reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement on mujawara in Mecca and state the operative ruling for fatwa.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: residing in Mecca is disliked; Sahibayn: not disliked. The dispute turns on human ability to honor the sacred site.

This passage from Radd al-Muhtar presents a clear intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the legal ruling on continuous residence (mujawara) in Mecca. Abu Hanifa considers it makruh due to the inability of most people to properly fulfill the rights of the Haram, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, negate the dislike entirely. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you grasp how Hanafi jurists weigh the sanctity of place against human capability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State clearly that Abu Hanifa rules mujawara as makruh. Identify the core reason: inability to uphold the rights of the House and the Haram.
The Arabic phrase is 'لعدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's view
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani negate the dislike. Their view is recorded as 'ونفى الكراهة صاحباه'.
These two are frequently referred to as 'Sahibayn' in Hanafi texts.
3
Analyze the reasoning behind Abu Hanifa's view
The text explains that the dislike does not contradict the virtue of Mecca; rather it is due to human weakness. The cause ('illa) is the failure to meet the required rights of the sacred place.
The passage cites al-Ihya' and al-Fath to reinforce this point.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, one should avoid prolonged residence in Mecca; according to the Sahibayn, it is permissible without dislike.
This affects the fatwa given to someone considering moving to Mecca.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Though the text does not explicitly resolve, later Hanafi fatwa tends to adopt the view of the Sahibayn (not makruh) as the relied-upon position, as it is easier and more in line with the virtue of the place.
Check later sources like al-Haskafi or Ibn Abidin for explicit tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم، ونفى الكراهة صاحباه رحمها. مكروهة: قال في المجمع: والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة أي عنده خلافا لهما، وبقوله قال الخائفون المحتاطون من العلماء كما في الإحياء، قال ولا يظن أن كراهة القيام تناقض فضل البقعة؛ لأن هذه الكراهة علتها ضعف الخلق، وقصورهم عن القيام بحق الموضع قال: وفي الفتح وعلى هذا فيجب كون الجوار في المدينة المشرفة مكروها عنده، فإن تضاعف السيآت أو تعاظمها إن فقد فيها فمخافة السآمة، وقلة الأدب المفضي إلى الإخلال بواجب التوقير والإجلال قائم رد المحتار ٥٢٤/٢] كذلك، يعني
And residing in Mecca is disliked according to Abu Hanifa, because of not upholding the rights of the House and the Haram. His two companions negated the dislike. It is disliked: said in al-Majma': Residing in Mecca is disliked, i.e., in his opinion, contrary to them. And by his statement spoke the cautious and careful scholars as in al-Ihya'. He said: And one should not think that the dislike of residing contradicts the virtue of the place; because the cause of this dislike is the weakness of the creation and their failure to uphold the rights of the place. He said: And in al-Fath, on this basis, it should be that residing in the Medina the Noble is also disliked in his opinion, because the doubling of sins or their intensification if he fails in it, and the fear of boredom, and lack of etiquette leading to failing in the obligatory honor and reverence is similarly present. Radd al-Muhtar 2/524. Similarly, meaning.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. Abu Hanifa rules that continuous residence (mujawara) in Mecca is makruh (disliked). The reasoning is that the sanctity of the place demands certain rights and etiquettes which most people cannot maintain, leading to negligence. His two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, deny the dislike. The text then clarifies that this dislike does not negate the virtue of Mecca; rather it is due to human weakness. It extends the reasoning to Medina, suggesting that if the same applies, then residing there would also be disliked. The source cited is Radd al-Muhtar.

Key Terms
المجاورة (al-mujawara): Continuous residence in Mecca (or Medina) for a prolonged period.
صاحباه (sahibahu): His two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Mecca is not a suitable place to live.
B) Because people fail to uphold the rights of the House and the Haram.
C) Because the climate is harsh.
D) Because it is a form of bid'ah.

Key Takeaway
The intra-Hanafi dispute on mujawara illustrates that a ruling can be makruh due to human weakness without diminishing the sanctity of the place; the mufta bihi is the permission of the Sahibayn.

Residing in Mecca: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute (Mujawara)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on residing in Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two companions regarding residing in Mecca (mujawara), explain the rationale for Abu Hanifa's view, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Residing in Mecca is disliked only due to human weakness, not the place itself.

This passage from Radd al-Muhtar presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of prolonged residence (mujawara) in Mecca. Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh tanzihi, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, do not. The key lies in the reason: Abu Hanifa's concern is that most people cannot fulfill the heightened obligations and etiquette due to the sacred site. Let's walk through the dispute and its resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
The act is 'mujawara' – residing in the vicinity of the Haram in Mecca for an extended period. The dispute is whether this is makruh (disliked) or not.
The ruling does not apply to temporary visits for Hajj or Umrah.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his reason
Abu Hanifa holds that mujawara is makruh because most people fail to fulfill the rights of the Kaaba and the Haram.
The reason (illa) is human shortcoming, not a flaw in the place.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their reason
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani negated the dislike, considering it permissible. Their reasoning is not detailed in the text, but it is based on the virtue of the place and original permissibility.
The Sahibayn's view is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
4
Analyze the resolution of the apparent contradiction
The text clarifies that the disbelief is not due to the place but due to human weakness. This preserves the virtue of Mecca while acknowledging practical shortcomings.
The same reasoning extends to Madinah: according to Abu Hanifa, residing there is also makruh.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its basis
Later Hanafi fatwa practice adopts the view of the Sahibayn (no dislike). Abu Hanifa's view is seen as a caution for the meticulous.
The author in Radd al-Muhtar presents both views but the phrase 'wa nafa al-karahah sahibahu' indicates the preferred view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان العمرة والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لعدم القيام بحقوق البيت والحرم، ونفى الكراهة صاحباه رحمها. قال في "المجمع": والمجاورة بمكة مكروهة أي عنده خلافا لهما، وبقوله قال الخائفون المحتاطون من العلماء كما في "الإحياء"، قال ولا يظن أن كراهة القيام تناقض فضل البقعة؛ لأن هذه الكراهة علتها ضعف الخلق، وقصورهم عن القيام بحق الموضع قال: وفي "الفتح" وعلى هذا فيجب كون الجوار في المدينة المشرفة مكروها عنده، فإن تضاعف السيآت أو تعاظمها إن فقد فيها فمخافة السآمة، وقلة الأدب المفضي إلى الإخلال بواجب التوقير والإجلال قائم [رد المحتار ٢/٥٢٤]
Explanation of Umrah and residing in Mecca: Residing in Mecca is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, due to failing to fulfill the rights of the House and the Sanctuary. His two companions negated the dislike. It is said in al-Mujma': Residing in Mecca is disliked, i.e., according to him, contrary to them. And his statement is held by the God-fearing and cautious scholars, as in al-Ihya. He said: And let it not be thought that the dislikedness of staying contradicts the virtue of the place, because this dislike is caused by the weakness of the creatures and their deficiency in fulfilling the rights of the place. He said: And in al-Fath, on this basis, residing in the honored city of Madinah must be disliked according to him, for the multiplication of evil deeds or their enormity if found there, and the fear of boredom and lack of etiquette leading to neglect of the duty of respect and veneration is present. [Radd al-Muhtar 2/524]
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on residing in Mecca (mujawara). It is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh (disliked) due to the inability of most people to properly fulfill the rights of the Kaaba and the Haram, while his two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, do not consider it disliked. The commentary from al-Mujma' confirms this, noting that cautious scholars follow Abu Hanifa's view. The apparent contradiction between the virtue of the place and the dislikedness is resolved by noting that the dislike is not due to the place itself but due to human weakness. The principle is extended to Madinah: based on the same reasoning, residing there would also be makruh according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
المجاورة (al-mujāwara): Residing in the vicinity of the Haram (Mecca or Madinah) for an extended period.
مكروهة (makrūha): Disliked (tanzihan), not sinful but better avoided.
صاحباه (sāḥibāhu): His two companions: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider residing in Mecca makruh?
A) Because the climate is unhealthy
B) Due to the inability to fulfill the rights of the House and Haram
C) Because it is forbidden by the Quran
D) Only if one is not a pilgrim

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is that residing in Mecca is not disliked, but Abu Hanifa's view serves as a caution about fulfilling the rights of the sacred place.
