Classification of Hajj Offenses and Their Penalties
Classification and gradation of Hajj penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a Hajj offense as against Ihram or the Haram, and state the corresponding penalty (dam, sadaqah, badanah, or lesser charity) for each type of violation.

Core Idea
Hajj offenses compromise the inviolability of Ihram or the Haram; penalties are graded: dam (sheep), badanah (camel), sadaqah (half sa'), or unspecified charity.

Understanding the classification of Hajj offenses and their penalties is essential for every pilgrim. The Hanafi school organizes these violations into two main categories: those committed against the state of Ihram and those against the sacred territory of Mecca. The penalties vary from a simple charity to the sacrifice of a camel, depending on the severity of the act. This lesson will guide you through the core categories and their corresponding requirements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main categories of jinayat
Read the opening of the passage and note the first division: offenses against Ihram (specific to Muhrim) and offenses against the Haram (not specific to Muhrim).
The second type applies to both Muhrim and non-Muhrim.
2
List the five grades of penalties for Muhrim's offenses
The passage mentions: dam (sheep), badanah (camel) in two specific cases, sadaqah (half sa' of wheat), less than that (for lice/grasshoppers), and the penalty for hunting (which may include multiple penalties).
Dam is the default; badanah is only for intercourse before shaving and Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah/haith/nifas.
3
Recognize the conditions that trigger each penalty
For perfume: a mature Muhrim perfuming a limb (whole body in one sitting counts as one) requires dam; wearing a perfumed garment for a full day also requires dam; less than a limb requires sadaqah. For hunting: penalty multiplies if multiple Muhrims killed the same game.
Children and non-Muhrims are exempted in several rules.
4
Apply the multiplication principle for hunting
The text states: if two Muhrims kill game, each must give a separate penalty (because the act is multiplied). For two non-Muhrims in the Haram, only one penalty because the violated space is one.
This illustrates the distinction between offenses against Ihram (personal state) vs. Haram (sacred place).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنايات أحكام الجنايات هي على قسمين جناية على الإحرام وجناية على الحرم والثانية لا تختص بالمحرم، وجناية المحرم على أقسام منها ما يوجب دما، ومنها: ما يوجب صدقة، وهي نصف صاع من بُرّ، ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك، ومنها: ما جزاء الصيد، ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المجرمين، فالتي توجب دما هي: ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا . باب الجنايات جمع جناية، وهي هنا ما تكون حرمته بسبب الإحرام أو الحرم، وقد يجب بها دمان أو دم أو صوم أو صدقة ففصلها. [الدر المختار ٢/٥٤٣] وحاصل الأول سبعة: محرم الإحرام ترك واجب إزالة الشعر وقص الظفر واللبس والوطي مع الدواعي والطيب والدهن وصيد البر وحاصل الثاني: التعرض لصيد الحرم وشجره، قال في "البحر": وخرج بقوله : "بسبب إلخ" ذكر الجماع بحضرة النساء؛ لأنه عنه مطلقا، فلا يوجب الدم. [رد المحتار بتصرف ٢/٥٤٣] اعلم أن الدم حيث أطلق يراد به الشاة، وهي تجزئ في كل شيء إلا في موضعين: الأول: إذا جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق، والثاني: إذا طاف للزيارة جنبا أو حائضا أو نفساء؛ فإن الواجب في هذين الموضعين البدنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤١] اعلم أن كل صدقة في الإحرام غير مقدرة، فهي نصف صاع إلا ما يجب بقتل القمل والجراد، فإنه يطعم ما شاء، وأشار إلى ذلك بقوله: "ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك". [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٧٤١] ويتعدد إلخ : قال في "التنوير" وشرحه ولو قتل محرمان صيدا تعدد الجزاء؛ لتعدد الفعل، ولو حلالان صيد الحرم لا؛ لاتحاد المحل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤١] لو طيب أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا طيب ناسيا أو جاهلا أو مكرها، وشمل العضو الفم ولو بأكل طيب كثير، وما يبلغ عضوا لو جمع والبدن كله كعضو واحد إن اتحد المجلس وإلا فلكل طيب كفارة وأما إذا لبس ثوبا مطيبا أكثره، فيشترط للزوم الدم دوام لبسه يوما محرم أخرج بالمحرم الحلال؛ لأن الحلال لو طيب عضوا، ثم أحرم، فانتقل منه إلى مكان آخر من بدنه فلا شيء عليه ،اتفاقا وأخرج بالبالغ الصبي فلا شيء عليه، وقيد بالعضو؛ لأن تطيب ما دونه فيه صدقة. [حاشية الطحطاوي بتصرف: ٧٤٢]
Chapter of Offenses: Rulings of offenses. They are of two types: an offense against Ihram and an offense against the Haram. The second is not specific to the Muhrim. The offenses of the Muhrim are of categories: among them what necessitates a dam (sacrifice), among them what necessitates sadaqah (charity), which is half a sa' of wheat, among them what necessitates less than that, and among them what is the penalty for hunting. The penalty is multiplied with the multiplicity of the killers who are criminals. So that which necessitates a dam is: if a mature Muhrim perfumes a limb. The chapter of offenses is a plural of jinayah, and here it is that which is prohibited due to Ihram or the Haram, and it may necessitate two dams, or one dam, or fasting, or charity. Their detail follows. [al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2/543] The summary of the first (type) is seven: prohibited acts of Ihram are leaving an obligatory act, removing hair, cutting nails, wearing (sewn clothes), intercourse with provocation, applying perfume, oil, and hunting of game. The summary of the second (type) is: interfering with the game of the Haram and its trees. He said in al-Bahr: Excluded by his saying "due to etc." is mentioning sexual intercourse in the presence of women, because it is absolutely detested, so it does not necessitate dam. [Radd al-Muhtar with adaptation 2/543] Know that wherever dam is mentioned absolutely, it means a sheep (shah). It suffices in everything except in two situations: first, if he had intercourse after standing at Arafah before shaving (the head); second, if he performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah, or menstruation, or postpartum bleeding; then in these two situations the obligatory is a camel (badanah). [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741] Know that every charity in Ihram that is not specified is half a sa', except what is obligatory for killing lice and locusts, for which he feeds whatever he wishes. He indicated that by his saying: "and among them what necessitates less than that." [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 741] "And it multiplies etc.": He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: If two Muhrims kill game, the penalty is multiplied due to the multiplicity of the act. If two non-Muhrims (hunt) the game of the Haram, it is not multiplied because of the unity of the (violated) place. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741] "If he perfumed" is absolute, so it includes if he perfumed forgetfully, or ignorantly, or under compulsion, and it includes the limb including the mouth even by eating much perfume, and what amounts to a limb if combined, and the whole body counts as one limb if the session is the same; otherwise for each perfume there is an expiation. And if he wears a garment whose greater part is perfumed, then for the obligation of dam, the condition is that he wears it continuously for a day. "Muhrim" excludes the non-Muhrim (halal), because if a non-Muhrim perfumed a limb and then entered Ihram and the perfume moved to another place on his body, nothing is required of him, by agreement. And "mature" excludes the child, so nothing is required of him. And it is restricted to a limb because perfuming less than a limb requires sadaqah. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with adaptation: 742]
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on jinayat (offenses) during Hajj. It begins by classifying them into two types: offenses against Ihram (which affect the pilgrim's state of consecration) and offenses against the Haram (the sacred territory of Mecca). The latter applies to both Muhrims and non-Muhrims. For Muhrims, violations are graded: some require a dam (sacrifice of a sheep), some require sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat), some require less than that (like for killing lice), and some involve the penalty for hunting game. The penalty for hunting is multiplied if multiple Muhrims participate. The text then elaborates on the rulings: dam generally means a sheep, except in two cases where a camel is required. Sadaqah is generally half a sa', except for killing lice/grasshoppers where one can feed as much as one wishes. It explains that if two Muhrims kill the same game, each must offer a separate penalty because the act is multiplied. For applying perfume, the ruling is detailed: it applies to any limb of a mature Muhrim, whether done intentionally, forgetfully, or under compulsion. If the whole body is perfumed in one sitting, it counts as one offense; if multiple sittings, multiple expiations. Wearing a perfumed garment requires continuous wear for a day to necessitate dam. By consensus, if a non-Muhrim applies perfume and then enters Ihram, and the perfume transfers to another spot, no penalty. A child is exempt.

Key Terms
الجنايات (al-jināyāt): Offenses during Hajj that break the inviolability of Ihram or the Haram.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (usually a sheep) required as a penalty for violating Ihram or the Haram.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity (half sa' of wheat) given for certain minor violations during Ihram.
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or cow) sacrificed for specific major violations like intercourse before shaving.
محرم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of Ihram for Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One dam (sheep)
B) One sadaqah (half sa')
C) Multiple dams for each limb
D) No penalty if done forgetfully

Key Takeaway
Hajj offenses are graded by severity; the penalty depends on the nature of the violation (Ihram vs. Haram, limb vs. less than limb, etc.) and who commits it.

Definition and Types of Jinayah in Hajj
Defines jinaayat and lists seven acts requiring a blood sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define jinayah in the context of Hajj according to the Hanafi school and differentiate between offenses against ihram and offenses against the Haram.

Core Idea
Jinayah in Hajj has two types: one specific to the muhrim, the other binding on anyone in the Haram.

In this passage, the author introduces the concept of jinayah (offenses) related to Hajj. He divides them into two broad categories: those arising from the state of ihram and those arising from the sanctity of the Haram. Understanding this distinction is essential because different rulings apply, and the second type does not require being in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of jinayah
The passage states: 'jinayah, and here it is what is forbidden due to ihram or the Haram.' This is the key definition.
Note that it includes both types.
2
List the two main categories
The text explicitly says: 'They are of two types: offense against ihram and offense against the Haram.'
3
Note the scope of each category
The first type applies only to the muhrim (one in ihram). The second type applies to anyone, muhrim or not, because it concerns the sanctity of the place.
4
Understand the subcategories of muhrim's offenses
The passage then mentions that muhrim's offenses have levels: those requiring dam, those requiring sadaqah, etc. This leads to further detail.
5
Recognize the significance of the distinction
The penalty for Haram violations (hunting, cutting trees) applies even to non-muhrims, which is a unique feature.

The Book of Hajj. Chapter of Offenses. Rulings of Offenses. They are of two types: offense against ihram and offense against the Haram, and the second is not specific to the muhrim. The offense of the muhrim is of categories: some obligate a dam, some obligate sadaqah, which is half a sa' of wheat, some obligate less than that, and some are the penalty for hunting. The penalty is multiplied by the number of killers. So those that obligate a dam are: if a muhrim adult applies perfume to a limb. Chapter of Offenses is plural of jinayah, and here it is what is forbidden due to ihram or the Haram, and it may necessitate two dams, or one dam, or fasting, or sadaqah, as detailed. [al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2/543] The summary of the first is seven: violation of ihram, leaving an obligatory act, removing hair and cutting nails, wearing [sewn clothes], intercourse with inducements, perfume, oil, and hunting land game. The summary of the second: interfering with the game of the Haram and its trees. He said in al-Bahr: and by his saying 'due to etc.' is excluded mentioning intercourse in the presence of women, because it is [؟] absolutely, so it does not obligate a dam. [Radd al-Muhtar 2/543] Know that when dam is used absolutely, it refers to a sheep, and it suffices for everything except in two places: first, if one has intercourse after standing at Arafat before shaving, and second, if one performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, menstruating, or postpartum; then the obligatory in these two places is a camel. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741] Sadaqah: know that every sadaqah in ihram that is not specified is half a sa', except what is obligatory for killing lice and locusts, for which one feeds as he wishes. And he indicated that by his saying: 'and among them what obligates less than that'. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 741] And it multiplies etc.: He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: if two muhrims kill game, the penalty is multiplied due to multiplicity of action, and if two non-muhrims [kill] the game of the Haram, not [multiplied] due to unity of the place. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741]
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an introductory definition and classification of jinaayat (offenses) in Hajj. The author first distinguishes between violations of the state of ihram (specific to the muhrim) and violations of the sanctity of the Haram (applicable to anyone). He then categories muhrim's offenses into those requiring a dam (blood sacrifice), those requiring sadaqah (charity of half a sa' of wheat), those requiring less, and those related to hunting. The text mentions that the penalty multiplies with the number of killers. The seven acts requiring a dam are listed: violating ihram by leaving a wajib, removing hair, cutting nails, wearing sewn clothes, intercourse (with inducements), applying perfume, applying oil, and hunting land game. The second type (Haram violations) involves hunting or cutting trees in the Haram. The commentator notes that mentioning intercourse in front of women does not obligate a dam. He also clarifies that 'dam' normally means a sheep, but in two specific cases (intercourse after Arafat before shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of impurity) a camel is required. The sadaqah for undefined offenses is half a sa', except for lice and locusts where one feeds as he wishes. The principle of multiple penalties is explained: if two muhrims jointly kill game, each pays a penalty because the actions are multiple; but if two non-muhrims kill game in the Haram, only one penalty is due because the violation is against the place, not the persons.

Key Terms
جناية (jinayah): In this context, an act whose prohibition arises from ihram or the sanctity of the Haram.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, normally a sheep, but in two exceptions a camel.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity of half a sa' of wheat, unless otherwise specified (e.g., for lice/locusts, one feeds as wished).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It always requires a blood sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
Jinayah in Hajj is any act prohibited due to ihram or the sanctity of the Haram, and it falls into two distinct categories with different scopes.

The Seven Acts Requiring a Dam and Exceptions
Defines jinaayat and lists seven acts requiring a blood sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven acts that obligate a dam in Hajj and identify the two exceptional cases where a camel is required instead of a sheep.

Core Idea
Seven specific violations of ihram obligate a dam, but two exceptional cases require a camel.

After defining jinayah, the passage enumerates seven specific acts that fall under 'violation of ihram' and require a blood sacrifice (dam). It further clarifies that the default animal for dam is a sheep, except in two instances: intercourse after Arafat before shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in major impurity. Understanding these specifics is crucial for correct penalty application.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the seven acts
The passage says: 'The summary of the first is seven: violation of ihram, leaving an obligatory act, removing hair and cutting nails, wearing [sewn clothes], intercourse with inducements, perfume, oil, and hunting land game.' Learn these well.
Note that 'violation of ihram' is a general act; the others are specific.
2
Recognize the default dam animal
The text states: 'when dam is used absolutely, it refers to a sheep.'
3
Learn the two exceptions requiring a camel
The two exceptions are: (1) intercourse after Arafat before shaving, and (2) Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, menstruating, or postpartum. In these cases, a camel is obligatory.
4
Understand sadaqah and lesser penalties
The passage also mentions that some offenses require sadaqah (half a sa' of wheat) or less, such as for killing lice or locusts.
5
Apply the principle of multiple penalties
If two muhrims kill game, each pays a penalty. But if two non-muhrims kill game in the Haram, only one penalty is due because the violation is against the place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
باب الجنايات
أحكام الجنايات
هي على قسمين جناية على الإحرام وجناية على الحرم والثانية لا تختص بالمحرم، وجناية المحرم على أقسام منها ما يوجب دما، ومنها: ما يوجب صدقة، وهي نصف صاع من بُرّ، ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك، ومنها: ما جزاء الصيد، ويتعدد الجزاء بتعدد القاتلين المجرمين، فالتي توجب دما هي: ما لو طيب محرم بالغ عضوا .
باب الجنايات جمع جناية، وهي هنا ما تكون حرمته بسبب الإحرام أو الحرم، وقد يجب بها دمان أو دم أو صوم أو صدقة ففصلها. [الدر المختار ٥٤٣/٢] وحاصل الأول سبعة:
محرم الإحرام ترك واجب
إزالة الشعر وقص الظفر
واللبس والوطي مع الدواعي والطيب والدهن وصيد البر
وحاصل الثاني: التعرض لصيد الحرم وشجره، قال في "البحر": وخرج بقوله : "بسبب إلخ" ذكر الجماع بحضرة النساء؛ لأنه عنه مطلقا، فلا يوجب الدم. رد المحتار بتصرف : ٥٤٣/٢] دما اعلم أن الدم حيث أطلق
منهي
یراد به الشاة، وهي تجزئ في كل شيء إلا في موضعين: الأول: إذا جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة قبل الحلق، والثاني: إذا طاف للزيارة جنبا أو حائضا أو نفساء؛ فإن الواجب في هذين الموضعين البدنة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤١] صدقة: اعلم أن كل صدقة في الإحرام غير مقدرة، فهي نصف صاع إلا ما يجب بقتل القمل والجراد، فإنه
يطعم ما شاء، وأشار إلى ذلك بقوله: "ومنها ما يوجب دون ذلك". [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٧٤١] ويتعدد إلخ : قال في "التنوير" وشرحه ولو قتل محرمان صيدا تعدد الجزاء؛ لتعدد الفعل، ولو حلالان صيد الحرم لا؛ لاتحاد المحل. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤١]
The Book of Hajj. Chapter of Offenses. Rulings of Offenses. They are of two types: offense against ihram and offense against the Haram, and the second is not specific to the muhrim. The offense of the muhrim is of categories: some obligate a dam, some obligate sadaqah, which is half a sa' of wheat, some obligate less than that, and some are the penalty for hunting. The penalty is multiplied by the number of killers. So those that obligate a dam are: if a muhrim adult applies perfume to a limb. Chapter of Offenses is plural of jinayah, and here it is what is forbidden due to ihram or the Haram, and it may necessitate two dams, or one dam, or fasting, or sadaqah, as detailed. [al-Durr al-Mukhtar 2/543] The summary of the first is seven: violation of ihram, leaving an obligatory act, removing hair and cutting nails, wearing [sewn clothes], intercourse with inducements, perfume, oil, and hunting land game. The summary of the second: interfering with the game of the Haram and its trees. He said in al-Bahr: and by his saying 'due to etc.' is excluded mentioning intercourse in the presence of women, because it is [؟] absolutely, so it does not obligate a dam. [Radd al-Muhtar 2/543] Know that when dam is used absolutely, it refers to a sheep, and it suffices for everything except in two places: first, if one has intercourse after standing at Arafat before shaving, and second, if one performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, menstruating, or postpartum; then the obligatory in these two places is a camel. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741] Sadaqah: know that every sadaqah in ihram that is not specified is half a sa', except what is obligatory for killing lice and locusts, for which one feeds as he wishes. And he indicated that by his saying: 'and among them what obligates less than that'. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition: 741] And it multiplies etc.: He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: if two muhrims kill game, the penalty is multiplied due to multiplicity of action, and if two non-muhrims [kill] the game of the Haram, not [multiplied] due to unity of the place. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 741]
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an introductory definition and classification of jinaayat (offenses) in Hajj. The author first distinguishes between violations of the state of ihram (specific to the muhrim) and violations of the sanctity of the Haram (applicable to anyone). He then categories muhrim's offenses into those requiring a dam (blood sacrifice), those requiring sadaqah (charity of half a sa' of wheat), those requiring less, and those related to hunting. The text mentions that the penalty multiplies with the number of killers. The seven acts requiring a dam are listed: violating ihram by leaving a wajib, removing hair, cutting nails, wearing sewn clothes, intercourse (with inducements), applying perfume, applying oil, and hunting land game. The second type (Haram violations) involves hunting or cutting trees in the Haram. The commentator notes that mentioning intercourse in front of women does not obligate a dam. He also clarifies that 'dam' normally means a sheep, but in two specific cases (intercourse after Arafat before shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah in a state of impurity) a camel is required. The sadaqah for undefined offenses is half a sa', except for lice and locusts where one feeds as he wishes. The principle of multiple penalties is explained: if two muhrims jointly kill game, each pays a penalty because the actions are multiple; but if two non-muhrims kill game in the Haram, only one penalty is due because the violation is against the place, not the persons.

Key Terms
جناية (jinayah): In this context, an act whose prohibition arises from ihram or the sanctity of the Haram.
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice, normally a sheep, but in two exceptions a camel.
صدقة (sadaqah): Charity of half a sa' of wheat, unless otherwise specified (e.g., for lice/locusts, one feeds as wished).
بدنة (badanah): A camel, required as dam in two specific cases.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which of the following cases is a camel required instead of a sheep?
A) Removing hair
B) Performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub
C) Applying perfume
D) Hunting land game

Key Takeaway
The seven acts that obligate a dam are specific, and the default sacrifice is a sheep except in two situations where a camel is obligatory.

Ruling on Applying Perfume and Henna in Ihram
Details the ruling on applying perfume to a limb, including exceptions and consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume during ihram, distinguish between expiation for a limb vs. less than a limb, and state the conditions for dam and sadaqah.

Core Idea
Applying perfume to a limb or more in ihram requires a dam; less than a limb requires sadaqah.

Ihram is a sacred state with specific prohibitions. Among them, applying perfume (tayyib) is a major offense that requires expiation. The Hanafi school details the exact measurements and conditions for these expiations, including the definition of a limb and the effect of intent. This passage from Nur al-Idah and its commentaries clarifies these rulings with precision, ensuring the pilgrim knows what is required to maintain the validity of their ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine whether the act involves applying perfume (including henna, oil) to the body, wearing sewn clothes, covering the head, shaving, cutting nails, etc. The ruling is that these are prohibited and require expiation.
The passage lists multiple acts; focus on perfume first.
2
Distinguish between limb and less than limb
For perfume, the amount applied determines the expiation: a limb or more requires a dam; less than a limb requires sadaqah. The entire body counts as one limb if done in one session.
Mouth is considered a limb if large quantity is eaten.
3
Consider the effect of intent and status
The ruling applies regardless of forgetfulness, ignorance, or coercion. However, a non-muhrim or child is not liable. If a non-muhrim applies perfume before ihram and it transfers after, no expiation.
This is an exception to the general rule.
4
Identify specific acts that require a dam
Besides perfume, dyeing head with henna (considered perfume), oiling, wearing sewn clothes, covering head for a day, shaving a quarter of head, etc., each require a dam. Henna if caked (talbīd) may require two dams.
The passage provides detailed definitions for each act.
5
Apply the ruling to a composite scenario
Combine the rules: a muhrim who commits multiple prohibited acts in one session must calculate expiations for each, considering whether acts are separate or combined under one category.
The text states each perfume application in separate sessions requires its own expiation.

أيضا، والتلبيد أن يأخذ شيئا من الخطمي والآس ،والصمغ، فيجعله في أصول الشعر ليتلبد. [البحر الرائق: ٨/٣] بزيت أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان مطبوخا أو غير مطبوخ مطيبا أو غير مطيب، وأراد بالزيت دهن الزيتون والسمسم، وهو المسمى بالشيرج، فخرج بقية الأدهان كالشحم والسمن وقيد بالادهان؛ لأنه لو أكله أو داوی به شقوق رجليه أو أقطر في أذنه لا يجب دم ولا صدقة البحر الرائق بحذف: ٩/٣] أو لبس مخيطا: اعلم أن حقيقة لبس المخيط أن يحصل بواسطة الخياطة اشتمال على البدن واستمساك، فلذا لو ارتدى بالقميص أو اتشح أو التزرها ،بالسراويل فلا بأس به؛ لأنه لم يلبسه لبس المخيط؛ لعدم الاشتمال، أطلق في اللبس فشمل ما إذا أحدث اللبس بعد الإحرام، أو أحرم وهو لابسه فدام على ذلك، بخلاف انتفاعه بعد الإحرام بالطيب السابق عليه قبله؛ للنص، ولولاه لأوجبنا فيه أيضا وشمل ما إذا كان ناسيا أو عامدا، عالما أو جاهلا، مختارا أو مكرها، وشمل ما إذا لبس ثوبا واحدا أو جمع اللباس كله القميص والعمامة والخفين، ولذا لم يقل لبس ثوبا كغيره البحر الرائق بحذف: ١١/٣]
If he applies perfume, it is unrestricted, so it includes if he applies perfume forgetfully, ignorantly, or coerced, and it includes the limb even the mouth if he eats much perfume, and what reaches a limb if gathered, and the entire body is like one limb if the session is one, otherwise for each perfume there is an expiation. And if he wears a garment most of which is perfumed, then for the obligation of a dam, the condition is continuous wearing for a day. Muhrim excludes the non-muhrim; because if a non-muhrim perfumes a limb, then enters ihram, and it transfers to another part of his body, nothing is due upon him, by consensus. And by 'adult' is excluded the child, so nothing is due upon him. And it is restricted to 'limb' because perfuming less than that requires sadaqah. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi adapted: 742] Or he dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil and the like, or wears sewn clothes, or covers his head for a complete day, its color meaning he applied oil, refers to wearing and covering, or shaves a quarter of his head, or his [cupping?] site, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and his feet in one sitting or one hand or one foot, or leaves an obligatory act as previously explained, and in taking his mustache there is a compensation. One [note: henna with kasr of ha and tashdid of nun, a plant that is cultivated and grows until it approaches large trees, its leaves like pomegranate leaves and its branches like its branches, it has white flowers like clusters; from its leaves is taken red dye. And he explicitly mentioned henna although it is included under perfume, because of his statement: 'Henna is a perfume,' due to difference. And he restricted to the head and did not mention the beard as occurred in al-Asl, to indicate that the head alone is liable, and that the waw means 'or' in the wording of al-Asl, as evidence by the restriction to the head in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And since it is stated later that covering the head obligates a dam, he did not restrict henna to being liquid, for if it is solid (caked) then in it there is a dam for perfume absolutely, and a dam for covering if it continues a day and night and covers all or a quarter. So if the caking was with other than henna, a dam is also required, and it would be two dams. And al-talbid is when one takes some marshmallow, myrtle, and gum, and puts it in the roots of the hair to make it stick. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/3] He said 'oil' unrestricted, so it includes whether cooked or uncooked, perfumed or not perfumed. And by 'oil' he meant olive oil and sesame oil, which is called al-shiraj; other oils like fat and ghee are excluded. And he restricted to oiling because if he eats it, or treats cracks in his feet with it, or puts drops in his ear, no dam or sadaqah is due. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 9/3] Or wears sewn clothes: Know that the reality of wearing a sewn garment is that by sewing there is a wrapping of the body and holding. Therefore, if one wraps himself in a shirt or cloaks himself or wears trousers as a waist-wrapper, there is no harm, because he did not wear it as a sewn garment, due to lack of wrapping. The term 'wearing' is unrestricted, so it includes if he wears it after ihram, or he enters ihram while wearing it and continues, unlike benefiting after ihram from perfume applied before ihram, due to the text, otherwise we would have obligated it as well. And it includes whether forgetful or intentional, knowing or ignorant, voluntary or coerced. And it includes whether he wears one garment or combines all clothing - shirt, turban, and khuffs. For this reason, he did not say 'wears a garment' like others do. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 11/3]
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage elaborates on the ruling for applying perfume (tayyib) during ihram. The author states that the ruling is general: perfume applied to a limb or more requires a dam (blood sacrifice), while applying to less than a limb requires sadaqah. This applies regardless of intent (forgetful, ignorant, coerced). The mouth is considered a limb, and if perfume is consumed in large quantity, it is like applying to a limb. The entire body is considered one limb if the application occurs in one sitting; if multiple sittings, each requires its own expiation. If one wears a garment most of which is perfumed, a dam is only due if worn continuously for a day. A non-muhrim who perfumes before ihram and then the perfume transfers to another spot after ihram is not liable. A child is not liable. The text then lists specific actions that also require a dam: dyeing the head with henna (which is considered a perfume), oiling with oil (olive or sesame), wearing sewn clothes, covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or any of specified body parts (armpit, pubic area, neck), cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting or even one hand/foot, leaving an obligatory act, and trimming the mustache (which requires a compensation value). The commentary explains the details of henna: it is explicitly mentioned because there is a difference of opinion whether it is perfume; the Prophet said 'Henna is a perfume.' The head is singled out because covering it later requires a dam. If henna is caked (talbīd) and not just liquid, then two dams may be due: one for perfume and one for covering. Talbīd is defined as applying a mixture of marshmallow, myrtle, and gum to the roots of the hair. For oiling, only actual oiling (applying to skin/hair) triggers the ruling; eating oil or using it medicinally does not. For wearing sewn clothes, the key is that the garment encloses the body and holds by sewing; merely draping a shirt or wrapping a turban loosely does not count as 'wearing' in the technical sense. The ruling applies whether one puts on the garment after ihram or enters ihram already wearing it (by continuing).

Key Terms
طيب (tayyib): Perfume or any fragrant substance applied to the body or clothing.
حناء (hinna'): Henna, a plant used for dyeing, considered a perfume in this context.
مخيط (mukhiṭ): A sewn garment that encloses and holds the body by sewing.
تلبيد (talbīd): Applying a sticky mixture (marshmallow, myrtle, gum) to the hair to make it matted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim applies perfume to less than a limb (e.g., a small spot on his arm). What expiation is due?
A) A dam (sheep)
B) Sadaqah of half a sa' of wheat
C) Nothing, as it is less than a limb
D) Two dams

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, applying perfume during ihram requires a dam if applied to a limb or more, and sadaqah if applied to less than a limb, regardless of intent, with specific acts like henna dyeing, oiling, and wearing sewn clothes also triggering a dam.

Rulings on Shaving and Related Acts in Ihram
Specifies which shaving or hair removal actions require a dam or compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific acts in ihram that require a dam or hukuma and explain how compensation is calculated for mustache trimming.

Core Idea
Hair removal in ihram—even accidental—may require a dam, but mustache trimming only incurs proportional food compensation.

This lesson examines the detailed rulings of the Hanafi school on which acts of hair removal during ihram obligate a blood sacrifice (dam) and which require a lesser compensation (hukuma). The passage, with its commentary, clarifies that shaving is defined broadly to include any form of removal, and that the number of dams can multiply depending on how the acts are performed. Understanding these distinctions is essential for a muhrim to fulfill hajj correctly and avoid penalties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the specified acts
List the acts mentioned: shaving a quarter of the head, cupping site, armpit, pubic area, neck, cutting nails (hands and feet), leaving a wajib, and trimming the mustache.
The list is exhaustive for these categories.
2
Understand the scope of 'shaving'
The commentary expands 'shaving' to include any removal, whether by razor, depilatory, plucking, or even accidental (e.g., burning, touching and falling). The method does not affect the obligation.
Intent is irrelevant; the act itself triggers the ruling.
3
Analyze the 'in one sitting' condition
For nail cutting, if done in one sitting, all fingers and toes count as one act requiring one dam. If done in separate sittings, each sitting (e.g., one hand) requires a separate dam, potentially up to four.
This condition only applies to nail cutting, not to other listed acts.
4
Grasp the hukuma calculation
For mustache trimming, the compensation is hukuma: a proportional amount of food calculated based on how much hair is taken relative to a quarter of the beard. For example, taking half of an eighth of the beard requires a quarter of a dam.
This is a unique calculation not applied to other parts.
5
Apply the ruling to leaving a wajib
Leaving any wajib act of hajj (as previously explained) also requires a dam. The passage concludes by reminding the reader of this general principle.
This is a catch-all for omitted obligations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حلق ربع رأسه أو محجمه أو أحد إبطيه، أو عانته أو رقبته، أو قص أظفار يديه ورجليه بمجلس أو يدا أو رجلا أو ترك واجبا مما تقدم بيانه، وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة.
حلق إلخ أراد المصنف بالحلق الإزالة، سواء كان بالموسى أو بغيره، وسواء كان مختارا أو لا، فلو أزاله بالنورة، أو نتف لحيته، أو احترق شعره بخبزة، أو مسه بيد فسقط، فهو كالحلق كما في "المحيط". [البحر الرائق: ١٤/٣] بمجلس قيد بالمجلس؛ لأنه لو قصَّ الكل في المجالس، في كل مجلس عضو ، لزمه أربعة دماء. [البحر الرائق: ١٨/٣] حكومة: وتفسيره: أنه ينظر أن هذا المأخوذ كم يكون من ربع اللحية، فيجب عليه بحسابه من الطعام، حتى إذا أخذ منه نصف ثمن اللحية يجب عليه ربع الدم، وذكر الأخذ في الشارب، وهو القصّ؛ لأنه هو السنة يقص منه حتى يوازي الإطار، وهو الحرف الأعلى من الشفة العليا. تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٩/٢]
Or shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping site, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or one hand or one foot, or leaves an obligatory act as previously explained, and in taking his mustache there is a compensation (hukuma). Shaving etc.: The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, whether voluntarily or not. So if he removes it with depilatory paste (nurah), or plucks his beard, or his hair burns by bread, or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving, as in al-Muhit. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 14/3] 'In one sitting' is a restriction; because if he cuts all in different sittings, each sitting a limb, then four dams are required. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 18/3] Hukuma: its explanation is that one looks at how much this taken [hair] is from a quarter of the beard, then it is required proportional amount of food, so if he takes half of an eighth of the beard, he must give a quarter of a dam. And he mentioned 'taking' in the mustache, which is trimming, because it is the Sunnah; he trims it until it aligns with the rim, which is the upper edge of the upper lip. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/359]
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage details the specific acts of shaving or removing hair during ihram that require a blood sacrifice (dam). The text lists: shaving a quarter of the head, the cupping site (where cupping glasses were applied), one armpit, the pubic area, the neck, or cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting (or even just one hand or one foot). Leaving any obligatory act (wajib) also requires a dam, as explained earlier. For trimming the mustache, a different compensation called 'hukuma' is required, which is proportional to the amount taken relative to a quarter of the beard. The commentary explains that 'shaving' means any removal, regardless of method (razor, depilatory, plucking, or even accidental removal like burning or falling out). The phrase 'in one sitting' is crucial: if one cuts nails in multiple sittings, each limb's removal requires a separate dam, potentially up to four dams (for both hands and both feet). The 'hukuma' for the mustache is calculated by determining how much of the beard's quarter is taken; for example, if half of an eighth of the beard is trimmed, one owes a quarter of a dam (in food value). This is because the Sunnah is to trim the mustache to the rim of the upper lip.

Key Terms
حكومة (ḥukūmah): A proportional compensation in food for hair removal from the mustache, calculated based on the amount taken relative to a quarter of the beard.
محجم (maḥjim): The site where cupping is applied; shaving this area requires a dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim cuts the nails of both hands and both feet in separate sittings (each limb in its own sitting), how many dams are required according to the passage?
A) One dam
B) Two dams
C) Four dams
D) No dam because it is not shaving

Key Takeaway
During ihram, any removal of hair from specified body parts obligates a dam, but mustache trimming only requires proportional food compensation (hukuma), and the method or intent does not affect the obligation.

Major Hajj Violations Requiring Blood Sacrifice (Dam)
Major violations requiring dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the major jinayat in Hajj that require a blood sacrifice (dam) and explain the conditions for each.

Core Idea
A pilgrim who wears stitched clothing, applies henna, or shaves a quarter of his head owes a blood sacrifice.

This lesson covers the first category of Hajj violations from the classical Hanafi manual. These are acts that invalidate the perfection of ihram and require a specific expiation called dam (blood sacrifice). We will examine each violation and its conditions as presented in the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major violations
Read the passage and list all actions that incur a dam: henna, oiling, stitched clothing, head covering, shaving, cupping, nail cutting, leaving a wajib, and mustache trimming (which uses hukuma).
2
Understand the expiation type
For each act, determine if the expiation is a full dam (blood sacrifice) or a pro-rated hukuma. The text explains that trimming the mustache requires a hukuma (proportional charity).
Hukuma is used when the exact amount is not fixed.
3
Analyze the conditions
Note the conditions: e.g., covering head for a full day, cutting nails in one sitting, etc. The commentary clarifies nuances like liquid vs. caked henna and the definition of stitched clothing.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., a pilgrim applies henna and covers his head for a day), determine the expiation. Use the text to justify.

The Book of Hajj: Rulings of Violations. Or he dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil and the like, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head for a complete day. Its color: meaning he coated with oil. It refers to wearing and covering. Or he shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping cup, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or foot, or leaves an obligatory [act] from what has been explained, and regarding trimming his mustache: [there is] a government evaluation. One: Concerning henna: with kasr of the ha and tashdid of the nun, a plant that is cultivated and grows until it approaches large trees, its leaves like pomegranate leaves and its branches like its branches, it has white flowers like clusters, from its leaves the red dye is made. He explicitly mentioned henna even though it falls under perfume because of his statement, peace be upon him: "Henna is a perfume," due to a difference [of opinion]. He restricted [the mention] to the head and did not mention the beard as occurs in al-Asl; to indicate that the head alone is guaranteed, and that the waw means "or" in the phrasing of al-Asl, evidenced by restricting to the head in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And since it is clearly stated later that covering the head obligates blood, he did not restrict henna to being liquid; if it is caked, then for it is blood for perfume absolutely, and blood for covering if it continues for a day and night and covers all or a quarter. So if the caking is with other than henna, he owes blood: two bloods as well. Caking means taking some marshmallow, myrtle, and gum, and placing it at the roots of the hair to become caked. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/3] He is absolute regarding oil, so it includes whether it is cooked or uncooked, perfumed or not perfumed. By oil he means olive oil and sesame oil, which is called shiraj. So the rest of the oils like fat and ghee are excluded. He restricted it to oiling because if he eats it or treats the cracks of his feet with it or drips it into his ear, no blood or charity is obligatory. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 9/3] Or wears stitched clothing: Know that the reality of wearing stitched clothing is that through stitching, covering of the body and retention occurs. Therefore, if he wraps himself in a shirt or cloaks himself or tucks himself into trousers, there is no problem; because he does not wear it as stitched clothing, due to lack of covering. He is absolute regarding wearing, so it includes whether he initiated wearing after ihram, or he entered ihram while wearing it and continued that, unlike his benefit after ihram from perfume applied before it, due to the text; and if not, we would have obligated it in that case as well. And it includes whether he was forgetful or intentional, knowing or ignorant, choosing or compelled. And it includes whether he wore one garment or combined all clothing: shirt, turban, and socks. Therefore, he did not say "wore a garment" like others. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 11/3] Shaving, etc.: The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, and whether he is choosing or not. So if he removes it with depilatory, or plucks his beard, or his hair burns with a bread loaf, or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving, as in al-Muhit. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 14/3] In one sitting: he restricted it to the sitting because if he cuts all in sittings, in each sitting a limb, he owes four bloods. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 18/3] Government evaluation: Its interpretation is that one looks at how much of the quarter of the beard this taken amount is, and he is obligated accordingly from food, so that if he takes half of an eighth of the beard, he owes a quarter of blood. The mention of taking from the mustache is the trimming because it is the Sunnah; he trims it until it aligns with the rim, which is the upper edge of the upper lip. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/359] It is that. And what obligates charity of half a sa' of wheat or its value is: if he perfumed less than a limb, or wore stitched clothing, or covered his head less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut a nail. Likewise for each nail, half a sa', unless the total reaches a blood, then he deducts from it whatever he wishes, such as five [nails] scattered. Or he performed tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr while in a state of minor impurity (hadath). And a sheep is obligated even if he performed tawaf while junub, or left one circuit (shawt) of tawaf al-sadr, and likewise for each circuit from the minimum of it, or one pebble from one of the stonings, and likewise for each pebble when it does not reach the stoning of a day, unless it reaches a blood, then he deducts whatever he wishes. Or he shaved another's head or cut his nails. And if he perfumed, wore, or shaved due to an excuse, he has a choice between slaughtering or giving charity of three sa's to six poor people, or fasting three days. And what obligates less than half a sa' is: if he kills a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And what obligates the value is: if he kills game, then two just men appraise it at its place of killing. Half a sa': the ba is for depiction, or charity meaning the act of giving charity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] And a sheep is obligated: meaning the obligation of half a sa' or its value was regarding when he performed tawaf while in a state of minor impurity. As for when he performed tawaf while junub, a sheep is obligatory. Or left: coordinated to what incurs charity. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And likewise for each etc.: meaning likewise what is mentioned of half a sa' or its value is obligatory if he leaves a circuit from the minimum of tawaf, which is three circuits. A pebble: meaning likewise what is mentioned is obligatory if he leaves one pebble from the pebbles of stoning if the leaving does not amount to the left stoning of a day. In what does not amount: as for if it amounts to that or the majority of it, then there is blood. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] Unless it amounts etc.: meaning unless the total of what obligates him reaches the price of blood, then he may deduct from it whatever he wishes. Others: he is absolute, so it includes whether the other is in ihram or not. This is contrary to if he perfumed another's limb or dressed him in stitched clothing, for he owes nothing by consensus. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743] Due to excuse: he restricted it to an excuse because if he does any of it for another purpose, he owes blood or a specific charity, and nothing else suffices, as explicitly stated by Imam al-Isbijabi. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 20/3] Killing a louse: he is absolute, so it includes whether he kills it after removing it from his body, or throws it away, or throws his garment in the sun so that it dies. For a multitude of them, which is more than three, half a sa' is obligatory. And compensation is obligatory for lice by analogy to game. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743]
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings (ahkam) on violations (jinayat) committed during the state of ihram in Hajj. The author, a Hanafi jurist, enumerates various actions that invalidate or diminish the perfection of the pilgrimage and specifies the required expiations. The commentary, drawn from authoritative Hanafi works such as al-Bahr al-Raiq and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, clarifies the definitions and applications.

First, the passage lists actions that require a blood sacrifice (dam): applying henna to the head (with detailed discussion on liquid vs. caked henna), oiling the body, wearing stitched clothing (explaining that the essence is covering and retention, thus wrapping without stitching is allowed), covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or more, cupping, shaving armpits/pub/neck, cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, leaving any wajib act, and trimming the mustache (which requires a pro-rated evaluation or 'hukuma'). The commentary explains that henna is explicitly mentioned despite being a perfume because the Prophet confirmed it as perfume, and the rulings differentiate between liquid and caked henna (the latter may require two bloods: one for perfume and one for covering if it persists). Oil includes all types (cooked/raw, scented/unscented), but other fats like tallow are excluded. For stitched clothing, the ruling applies to wearing it intentionally or forgetfully, and covers all garments. Shaving is interpreted as removal by any means, and if done in multiple sittings, multiple bloods are due.

Second, the passage presents three categories of less severe violations and their fixed penalties:
- Violations requiring charity (sadaqah) of half a sa' of wheat (or its value): applying perfume to less than a full limb, wearing stitched clothing, covering the head for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, cutting one nail. If multiple nails are cut, half a sa' is due for each, but if the total value of these half-sa' obligations equals the price of a blood sacrifice, one may deduct and pay only one blood. However, if a sheep (shah) is explicitly due—such as for tawaf while in major impurity (janabah), leaving a circuit (shawt) from tawaf al-sadr, or leaving a pebble from the stoning—then a full sheep must be sacrificed, not half-sa' equivalents.
- Violations requiring less than half a sa': killing a single louse or locust; one gives charity as one wishes (the minimum is unspecified, but a handful is recommended). For multiple lice (more than three), half a sa' becomes obligatory.
- Violations requiring payment of market value: killing game (sawd/qatar); the animal is appraised by two just men at the site of killing, and the value must be given as charity.

Additionally, if a person perfumes, wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to a legitimate excuse (e.g., illness, heat), they have a choice: sacrifice a sheep, give three sa's of food to six poor people, or fast three days. This leniency does not apply if the act is done deliberately without excuse.

The passage also notes consensus that applying perfume or clothing to another person (even a non-muhrim) does not obligate anything. However, shaving another's head or cutting their nails obligates the same penalty as if done to oneself. The compensation for lice is analogized to game, indicating the principle that even harmful creatures are protected during ihram.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that the rulings apply regardless of knowledge, intent, or compulsion, except where specific exceptions are made (e.g., excuse). The commentary uses Hanafi legal terminology such as 'dam' (blood sacrifice), 'sadaqah' (charity), 'hukuma' (pro-rata valuation), and 'asl al-mas'alah' (case basis). This passage is a typical Hanafi fiqh manual section, providing a comprehensive overview of the expiations required to rectify or complete an imperfect Hajj.

Key Terms
الدم (ad-dam): A blood sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required for certain major violations of ihram.
الحكومة (al-hukuma): A pro-rated valuation of the part removed (e.g., from the beard) to determine proportionate expiation.
المخيط (al-makhit): Stitched clothing that covers and retains the body; wrapping without stitching is not considered 'wearing stitched'.
التلبيد (at-talbíd): Caking the hair with a mixture (e.g., marshmallow, myrtle, gum) to keep it in place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this lesson, what expiation does a pilgrim owe for trimming his mustache during ihram?
A) A full blood sacrifice (dam)
B) Half a sa‘ of wheat (sadaqah)
C) A pro-rated charity (hukuma) based on the portion removed
D) Nothing, as trimming mustache is permissible

Key Takeaway
Major jinayat in Hajj require a dam (blood sacrifice) or hukuma (pro-rated charity) for mustache trimming; the ruling is strict and applies regardless of intent.

Minor Hajj Violations – The Half-Sa‘ Charity and Tawaf Rulings
Minor violations and tawaf expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify minor violations that require half a sa‘ of charity and distinguish when a full sheep (shah) is due for tawaf-related violations.

Core Idea
Minor violations like cutting a single nail or perfume on less than a limb require half a sa‘; but multiple such acts may combine to require a dam.

This lesson continues the Hajj rulings, focusing on the second category of violations that incur a fixed charity (sadaqah) of half a sa‘ of wheat or its value. It also covers specific tawaf violations that require a full sheep (shah). The text explains accumulation rules and the boundary between charity and blood sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify minor violations
List the acts that incur half a sa‘: perfume on less than a limb, wearing stitched clothing for less than a day, covering head less than a day, shaving less than a quarter head, cutting one nail.
Each nail is half a sa‘.
2
Understand the accumulation rule
If multiple minor violations add up to the value of a dam, the pilgrim may substitute one dam instead of paying multiple half sa‘s. The text says 'unless the total reaches a blood, then he deducts whatever he wishes'.
3
Identify tawaf violations requiring a sheep
The passage states that performing tawaf al-qudum or al-sadr while in minor impurity (hadath) requires half a sa‘, but tawaf while junub requires a full sheep. Also, leaving a circuit (shawt) of tawaf al-sadr incurs half a sa‘ per circuit, unless it reaches the value of a dam.
4
Apply to scenarios
Given a scenario (e.g., a pilgrim performs tawaf al-sadr without wudu and later cuts three nails), determine the total expiation using the accumulation rule.

ورجليه بمجلس أو يدا أو رجلا أو ترك واجبا مما تقدم بيانه، وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة.
واحد
بحناء: بكسر الحاء وتشديد النون، نبات يزرع ويكبر حتى يقارب الشجر الكبار، ورقه كورق الرمان وعيدانه كعيدانه، له زهر أبيض كالعناقيد يتخذ من ورقه الخضاب الأحمر. وإنما صرح بالحناء مع دخولها تحت الطيب؛ لقوله عليه: "الحناء طيب"، للاختلاف، وإنما اقتصر على الرأس، ولم يذكر اللحية كما وقع في "الأصل"؛ ليفيد أن الرأس بانفرادها مضمونة، وأن الواو بمعنى "أو " في عبارة "الأصل" بدليل الاقتصار على الرأس في "الجامع الصغير"، ولما كان مصرحا فيما يأتي بأن تغطية الرأس موجبة للدم لم يقيد الحناء بأن تكون مائعة، فإن كانت ملبدة ففيه دم للطيب مطلقا، ودم للتغطية إن دام يوما وليلة وغطى الكل أو الربع فلو كان التلبيد بغير الحناء لزمه دم
:دمان
أيضا، والتلبيد أن يأخذ شيئا من الخطمي والآس ،والصمغ، فيجعله في أصول الشعر ليتلبد. [البحر الرائق: ٨/٣] بزيت أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان مطبوخا أو غير مطبوخ مطيبا أو غير مطيب، وأراد بالزيت دهن الزيتون والسمسم، وهو المسمى بالشيرج، فخرج بقية الأدهان كالشحم والسمن وقيد بالادهان؛ لأنه لو أكله أو داوی به شقوق رجليه أو أقطر في أذنه لا يجب دم ولا صدقة البحر الرائق بحذف: ٩/٣] أو لبس مخيطا: اعلم أن حقيقة لبس المخيط أن يحصل بواسطة الخياطة اشتمال على البدن واستمساك، فلذا لو ارتدى بالقميص أو اتشح أو التزرها ،بالسراويل فلا بأس به؛ لأنه لم يلبسه لبس المخيط؛ لعدم الاشتمال، أطلق في اللبس فشمل ما إذا أحدث اللبس بعد الإحرام، أو أحرم وهو لابسه فدام على ذلك، بخلاف انتفاعه بعد الإحرام بالطيب السابق عليه قبله؛ للنص، ولولاه لأوجبنا فيه أيضا وشمل ما إذا كان ناسيا أو عامدا، عالما أو جاهلا، مختارا أو مكرها، وشمل ما إذا لبس ثوبا واحدا أو جمع اللباس كله القميص والعمامة والخفين، ولذا لم يقل لبس ثوبا كغيره البحر الرائق بحذف: ١١/٣]
حلق إلخ أراد المصنف بالحلق الإزالة، سواء كان بالموسى أو بغيره، وسواء كان مختارا أو لا، فلو أزاله بالنورة، أو نتف لحيته، أو احترق شعره بخبزة، أو مسه بيد فسقط، فهو كالحلق كما في "المحيط". [البحر الرائق: ١٤/٣] بمجلس قيد بالمجلس؛ لأنه لو قصَّ الكل في المجالس، في كل مجلس عضو ، لزمه أربعة دماء. [البحر الرائق: ١٨/٣] حكومة: وتفسيره: أنه ينظر أن هذا المأخوذ كم يكون من ربع اللحية، فيجب عليه بحسابه من الطعام، حتى إذا أخذ منه نصف ثمن اللحية يجب عليه ربع الدم، وذكر الأخذ في الشارب، وهو القصّ؛ لأنه هو السنة
يقص منه حتى يوازي الإطار، وهو الحرف الأعلى من الشفة العليا. تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٩/٢]
وهو
أن
والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر أو قيمته هي ما لو طيب أقل من عضو، أو لبس مخيطا، أو غطى رأسه أقل من يوم أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه، أو قصّ ظفرا، وكذا لكل ظفر نصف صاع، إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دما، فينقص ما شاء منه،
كخمسة متفرقة، أو طاف للقدوم، أو للصدر ،محدثا وتجب شاة ولو طاف جنبا، أو
وصلية
ترك شوطا من طواف الصدر، وكذا لكل شوط من أقله، أو حصاة من إحدى الجمار، وكذا لكل حصاة فيما لم يبلغ رمي يوم إلا أن يبلغ دما، فينقص ما شاء، أو حلق رأس غيره، أو قص أظفاره، وإن تطيب أو لبس أو حلق بعذر تخير بين الذبح أو التصدق بثلاثة أصوع على ستة مساكين، أو صيام ثلاثة أيام، والتي توجب أقل من نصف صاع، فهي ما لو قتل قملة أو جرادة، فيتصدق بما شاء.
والتي توجب القيمة
جمع صاع
هي
ما لو قتل صيدا، فيقومه عدلان في مقتله،
بنصف صاع: الباء للتصوير أو الصدقة بمعنى التصدق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٢] وتجب شاة: أي وجوب نصف صاع أو قيمته كان فيما إذا طاف وهو محدث، وأما إذا طاف جنبا فيجب شاة. أو ترك: عطف على ما تجب فيه صدقة. (حاشية الطحطاوي وكذا لكل إلخ أي وكذا يجب ما ذكر من نصف الصاع، أو قيمته إذا ترك شوطا من أقل ،الطواف، وهو ثلاثة أشواط حصاة أي وكذا يجب ما ذكر إذا ترك حصاة من حصيات الرمي إذا لم يبلغ الترك متروك رمي يوم. فيما لم يبلغ: أما إذا بلغه أو أكثره ففيه .دم. [ حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٢] إلا أن يبلغ إلخ: أي إلا أن يبلغ مجموع وجب عليه ثمن ،دم فله أن ينقص ما شاء غيره: أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الغير محرما أو حلالا، وهذا بخلاف ما لو طيب عضو غيره، أو ألبسه مخيطا، فإنه لا شيء عليه إجماعا [حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٧٤٣] بعذر : قيد بالعذر؛ لأنه لو فعل شيئا منها لغيره لزمه دم، أو صدقة معينة، ولا يجزئه غيره كما صرح به الإمام الإسبيجابي. [البحر الرائق: ٢٠/٣] قتل قملة : أطلقه فشمل ما إذا قتلها بعد ما أخرجها من ،بدنه أو ألقاها أو ألقى ثوبه في الشمس؛ لتموت، ويجب في الكثير منه، وهو ما زاد على ثلاثة نصف صاع ويجب الجزاء في القمل بالدلالة عليه كالصيد. حاشية الطحطاوي بزيادة: ٧٤٣]
The Book of Hajj: Rulings of Violations. Or he dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil and the like, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head for a complete day. Its color: meaning he coated with oil. It refers to wearing and covering. Or he shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping cup, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or foot, or leaves an obligatory [act] from what has been explained, and regarding trimming his mustache: [there is] a government evaluation. One: Concerning henna: with kasr of the ha and tashdid of the nun, a plant that is cultivated and grows until it approaches large trees, its leaves like pomegranate leaves and its branches like its branches, it has white flowers like clusters, from its leaves the red dye is made. He explicitly mentioned henna even though it falls under perfume because of his statement, peace be upon him: "Henna is a perfume," due to a difference [of opinion]. He restricted [the mention] to the head and did not mention the beard as occurs in al-Asl; to indicate that the head alone is guaranteed, and that the waw means "or" in the phrasing of al-Asl, evidenced by restricting to the head in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And since it is clearly stated later that covering the head obligates blood, he did not restrict henna to being liquid; if it is caked, then for it is blood for perfume absolutely, and blood for covering if it continues for a day and night and covers all or a quarter. So if the caking is with other than henna, he owes blood: two bloods as well. Caking means taking some marshmallow, myrtle, and gum, and placing it at the roots of the hair to become caked. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/3] He is absolute regarding oil, so it includes whether it is cooked or uncooked, perfumed or not perfumed. By oil he means olive oil and sesame oil, which is called shiraj. So the rest of the oils like fat and ghee are excluded. He restricted it to oiling because if he eats it or treats the cracks of his feet with it or drips it into his ear, no blood or charity is obligatory. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 9/3] Or wears stitched clothing: Know that the reality of wearing stitched clothing is that through stitching, covering of the body and retention occurs. Therefore, if he wraps himself in a shirt or cloaks himself or tucks himself into trousers, there is no problem; because he does not wear it as stitched clothing, due to lack of covering. He is absolute regarding wearing, so it includes whether he initiated wearing after ihram, or he entered ihram while wearing it and continued that, unlike his benefit after ihram from perfume applied before it, due to the text; and if not, we would have obligated it in that case as well. And it includes whether he was forgetful or intentional, knowing or ignorant, choosing or compelled. And it includes whether he wore one garment or combined all clothing: shirt, turban, and socks. Therefore, he did not say "wore a garment" like others. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 11/3] Shaving, etc.: The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, and whether he is choosing or not. So if he removes it with depilatory, or plucks his beard, or his hair burns with a bread loaf, or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving, as in al-Muhit. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 14/3] In one sitting: he restricted it to the sitting because if he cuts all in sittings, in each sitting a limb, he owes four bloods. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 18/3] Government evaluation: Its interpretation is that one looks at how much of the quarter of the beard this taken amount is, and he is obligated accordingly from food, so that if he takes half of an eighth of the beard, he owes a quarter of blood. The mention of taking from the mustache is the trimming because it is the Sunnah; he trims it until it aligns with the rim, which is the upper edge of the upper lip. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/359] It is that. And what obligates charity of half a sa' of wheat or its value is: if he perfumed less than a limb, or wore stitched clothing, or covered his head less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut a nail. Likewise for each nail, half a sa', unless the total reaches a blood, then he deducts from it whatever he wishes, such as five [nails] scattered. Or he performed tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr while in a state of minor impurity (hadath). And a sheep is obligated even if he performed tawaf while junub, or left one circuit (shawt) of tawaf al-sadr, and likewise for each circuit from the minimum of it, or one pebble from one of the stonings, and likewise for each pebble when it does not reach the stoning of a day, unless it reaches a blood, then he deducts whatever he wishes. Or he shaved another's head or cut his nails. And if he perfumed, wore, or shaved due to an excuse, he has a choice between slaughtering or giving charity of three sa's to six poor people, or fasting three days. And what obligates less than half a sa' is: if he kills a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And what obligates the value is: if he kills game, then two just men appraise it at its place of killing. Half a sa': the ba is for depiction, or charity meaning the act of giving charity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] And a sheep is obligated: meaning the obligation of half a sa' or its value was regarding when he performed tawaf while in a state of minor impurity. As for when he performed tawaf while junub, a sheep is obligatory. Or left: coordinated to what incurs charity. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And likewise for each etc.: meaning likewise what is mentioned of half a sa' or its value is obligatory if he leaves a circuit from the minimum of tawaf, which is three circuits. A pebble: meaning likewise what is mentioned is obligatory if he leaves one pebble from the pebbles of stoning if the leaving does not amount to the left stoning of a day. In what does not amount: as for if it amounts to that or the majority of it, then there is blood. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] Unless it amounts etc.: meaning unless the total of what obligates him reaches the price of blood, then he may deduct from it whatever he wishes. Others: he is absolute, so it includes whether the other is in ihram or not. This is contrary to if he perfumed another's limb or dressed him in stitched clothing, for he owes nothing by consensus. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743] Due to excuse: he restricted it to an excuse because if he does any of it for another purpose, he owes blood or a specific charity, and nothing else suffices, as explicitly stated by Imam al-Isbijabi. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 20/3] Killing a louse: he is absolute, so it includes whether he kills it after removing it from his body, or throws it away, or throws his garment in the sun so that it dies. For a multitude of them, which is more than three, half a sa' is obligatory. And compensation is obligatory for lice by analogy to game. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743]
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings (ahkam) on violations (jinayat) committed during the state of ihram in Hajj. The author, a Hanafi jurist, enumerates various actions that invalidate or diminish the perfection of the pilgrimage and specifies the required expiations. The commentary, drawn from authoritative Hanafi works such as al-Bahr al-Raiq and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, clarifies the definitions and applications.

First, the passage lists actions that require a blood sacrifice (dam): applying henna to the head (with detailed discussion on liquid vs. caked henna), oiling the body, wearing stitched clothing (explaining that the essence is covering and retention, thus wrapping without stitching is allowed), covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or more, cupping, shaving armpits/pub/neck, cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, leaving any wajib act, and trimming the mustache (which requires a pro-rated evaluation or 'hukuma'). The commentary explains that henna is explicitly mentioned despite being a perfume because the Prophet confirmed it as perfume, and the rulings differentiate between liquid and caked henna (the latter may require two bloods: one for perfume and one for covering if it persists). Oil includes all types (cooked/raw, scented/unscented), but other fats like tallow are excluded. For stitched clothing, the ruling applies to wearing it intentionally or forgetfully, and covers all garments. Shaving is interpreted as removal by any means, and if done in multiple sittings, multiple bloods are due.

Second, the passage presents three categories of less severe violations and their fixed penalties:
- Violations requiring charity (sadaqah) of half a sa' of wheat (or its value): applying perfume to less than a full limb, wearing stitched clothing, covering the head for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, cutting one nail. If multiple nails are cut, half a sa' is due for each, but if the total value of these half-sa' obligations equals the price of a blood sacrifice, one may deduct and pay only one blood. However, if a sheep (shah) is explicitly due—such as for tawaf while in major impurity (janabah), leaving a circuit (shawt) from tawaf al-sadr, or leaving a pebble from the stoning—then a full sheep must be sacrificed, not half-sa' equivalents.
- Violations requiring less than half a sa': killing a single louse or locust; one gives charity as one wishes (the minimum is unspecified, but a handful is recommended). For multiple lice (more than three), half a sa' becomes obligatory.
- Violations requiring payment of market value: killing game (sawd/qatar); the animal is appraised by two just men at the site of killing, and the value must be given as charity.

Additionally, if a person perfumes, wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to a legitimate excuse (e.g., illness, heat), they have a choice: sacrifice a sheep, give three sa's of food to six poor people, or fast three days. This leniency does not apply if the act is done deliberately without excuse.

The passage also notes consensus that applying perfume or clothing to another person (even a non-muhrim) does not obligate anything. However, shaving another's head or cutting their nails obligates the same penalty as if done to oneself. The compensation for lice is analogized to game, indicating the principle that even harmful creatures are protected during ihram.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that the rulings apply regardless of knowledge, intent, or compulsion, except where specific exceptions are made (e.g., excuse). The commentary uses Hanafi legal terminology such as 'dam' (blood sacrifice), 'sadaqah' (charity), 'hukuma' (pro-rata valuation), and 'asl al-mas'alah' (case basis). This passage is a typical Hanafi fiqh manual section, providing a comprehensive overview of the expiations required to rectify or complete an imperfect Hajj.

Key Terms
الصاع (as-sa‘): Volume measure of approximately 2.4 kg of wheat, used for charity expiations.
الحدث (al-hadath): Minor impurity (e.g., breaking wudu) that requires wudu for tawaf.
الجمار (al-jimar): The stoning pillars at Mina; leaving one pebble incurs half a sa‘ unless reaching a day's stoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What expiation is due for a pilgrim who performs tawaf al-sadr while in a state of janabah (major impurity)?
A) Half a sa‘ of wheat
B) A full sheep (shah)
C) Three days of fasting
D) Pro-rated charity (hukuma)

Key Takeaway
Minor violations incur half a sa‘, but tawaf in janabah requires a full sheep; multiple half-sa‘s can be commuted to a dam if the value reaches a blood sacrifice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
advanced
10 min
Hajj Expiations: Excuse, Killing Creatures, and Game Valuation
Excuse option and creature expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the three options for expiation when a Pilgrim with an excuse commits a violation, and distinguish between expiations for killing lice, game, and other creatures.

Core Idea
A pilgrim with a legitimate excuse may choose between slaughter, feeding six poor people, or fasting; but deliberate violations require fixed expiations.

This lesson covers special cases in Hajj expiations: the leniency granted for violations committed due to an excuse (like illness or extreme heat), and the rulings for killing lice, locusts, and game. The text also addresses shaving another's head and cutting another's nails. Understanding these exceptions is vital for correct fatwa issuance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excuse option
The text says that if a pilgrim perfumes, wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to an excuse, he has a choice: slaughter a sheep, give three sa‘s to six poor people, or fast three days. Note that this applies only to these three acts.
The excuse must be legitimate (e.g., illness, extreme heat).
2
Distinguish intentional vs. excuse
If the act is done deliberately without excuse, the fixed expiation (dam or sadaqah) applies without the three options.
3
Understand rulings for killing creatures
Killing a louse or locust requires less than half a sa‘ (charity as one wishes); killing more than three lice incurs half a sa‘. Killing game requires payment of market value assessed by two just men.
Lice are analogized to game for compensation.
4
Note shaving/cutting another's hair/nails
Shaving another's head or cutting their nails incurs the same expiation as if done on oneself, even if the other is not in ihram.
This is based on the absolute wording of the text.

ورجليه بمجلس أو يدا أو رجلا أو ترك واجبا مما تقدم بيانه، وفي أخذ شاربه حكومة.
واحد
بحناء: بكسر الحاء وتشديد النون، نبات يزرع ويكبر حتى يقارب الشجر الكبار، ورقه كورق الرمان وعيدانه كعيدانه، له زهر أبيض كالعناقيد يتخذ من ورقه الخضاب الأحمر. وإنما صرح بالحناء مع دخولها تحت الطيب؛ لقوله عليه: "الحناء طيب"، للاختلاف، وإنما اقتصر على الرأس، ولم يذكر اللحية كما وقع في "الأصل"؛ ليفيد أن الرأس بانفرادها مضمونة، وأن الواو بمعنى "أو " في عبارة "الأصل" بدليل الاقتصار على الرأس في "الجامع الصغير"، ولما كان مصرحا فيما يأتي بأن تغطية الرأس موجبة للدم لم يقيد الحناء بأن تكون مائعة، فإن كانت ملبدة ففيه دم للطيب مطلقا، ودم للتغطية إن دام يوما وليلة وغطى الكل أو الربع فلو كان التلبيد بغير الحناء لزمه دم
:دمان
أيضا، والتلبيد أن يأخذ شيئا من الخطمي والآس ،والصمغ، فيجعله في أصول الشعر ليتلبد. [البحر الرائق: ٨/٣] بزيت أطلقه، فشمل ما إذا كان مطبوخا أو غير مطبوخ مطيبا أو غير مطيب، وأراد بالزيت دهن الزيتون والسمسم، وهو المسمى بالشيرج، فخرج بقية الأدهان كالشحم والسمن وقيد بالادهان؛ لأنه لو أكله أو داوی به شقوق رجليه أو أقطر في أذنه لا يجب دم ولا صدقة البحر الرائق بحذف: ٩/٣] أو لبس مخيطا: اعلم أن حقيقة لبس المخيط أن يحصل بواسطة الخياطة اشتمال على البدن واستمساك، فلذا لو ارتدى بالقميص أو اتشح أو التزرها ،بالسراويل فلا بأس به؛ لأنه لم يلبسه لبس المخيط؛ لعدم الاشتمال، أطلق في اللبس فشمل ما إذا أحدث اللبس بعد الإحرام، أو أحرم وهو لابسه فدام على ذلك، بخلاف انتفاعه بعد الإحرام بالطيب السابق عليه قبله؛ للنص، ولولاه لأوجبنا فيه أيضا وشمل ما إذا كان ناسيا أو عامدا، عالما أو جاهلا، مختارا أو مكرها، وشمل ما إذا لبس ثوبا واحدا أو جمع اللباس كله القميص والعمامة والخفين، ولذا لم يقل لبس ثوبا كغيره البحر الرائق بحذف: ١١/٣]
حلق إلخ أراد المصنف بالحلق الإزالة، سواء كان بالموسى أو بغيره، وسواء كان مختارا أو لا، فلو أزاله بالنورة، أو نتف لحيته، أو احترق شعره بخبزة، أو مسه بيد فسقط، فهو كالحلق كما في "المحيط". [البحر الرائق: ١٤/٣] بمجلس قيد بالمجلس؛ لأنه لو قصَّ الكل في المجالس، في كل مجلس عضو ، لزمه أربعة دماء. [البحر الرائق: ١٨/٣] حكومة: وتفسيره: أنه ينظر أن هذا المأخوذ كم يكون من ربع اللحية، فيجب عليه بحسابه من الطعام، حتى إذا أخذ منه نصف ثمن اللحية يجب عليه ربع الدم، وذكر الأخذ في الشارب، وهو القصّ؛ لأنه هو السنة
يقص منه حتى يوازي الإطار، وهو الحرف الأعلى من الشفة العليا. تبيين الحقائق: ٣٥٩/٢]
وهو
أن
والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر أو قيمته هي ما لو طيب أقل من عضو، أو لبس مخيطا، أو غطى رأسه أقل من يوم أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه، أو قصّ ظفرا، وكذا لكل ظفر نصف صاع، إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دما، فينقص ما شاء منه،

بنصف صاع: الباء للتصوير أو الصدقة بمعنى التصدق [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٢] وتجب شاة: أي وجوب نصف صاع أو قيمته كان فيما إذا طاف وهو محدث، وأما إذا طاف جنبا فيجب شاة. أو ترك: عطف على ما تجب فيه صدقة. (حاشية الطحطاوي وكذا لكل إلخ أي وكذا يجب ما ذكر من نصف الصاع، أو قيمته إذا ترك شوطا من أقل ،الطواف، وهو ثلاثة أشواط حصاة أي وكذا يجب ما ذكر إذا ترك حصاة من حصيات الرمي إذا لم يبلغ الترك متروك رمي يوم. فيما لم يبلغ: أما إذا بلغه أو أكثره ففيه .دم.
