The Book of Hajj: Rulings of Violations. Or he dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil and the like, or wears stitched clothing, or covers his head for a complete day. Its color: meaning he coated with oil. It refers to wearing and covering. Or he shaves a quarter of his head, or his cupping cup, or one of his armpits, or his pubic area, or his neck, or cuts the nails of his hands and feet in one sitting, or a hand or foot, or leaves an obligatory [act] from what has been explained, and regarding trimming his mustache: [there is] a government evaluation. One: Concerning henna: with kasr of the ha and tashdid of the nun, a plant that is cultivated and grows until it approaches large trees, its leaves like pomegranate leaves and its branches like its branches, it has white flowers like clusters, from its leaves the red dye is made. He explicitly mentioned henna even though it falls under perfume because of his statement, peace be upon him: "Henna is a perfume," due to a difference [of opinion]. He restricted [the mention] to the head and did not mention the beard as occurs in al-Asl; to indicate that the head alone is guaranteed, and that the waw means "or" in the phrasing of al-Asl, evidenced by restricting to the head in al-Jami' al-Saghir. And since it is clearly stated later that covering the head obligates blood, he did not restrict henna to being liquid; if it is caked, then for it is blood for perfume absolutely, and blood for covering if it continues for a day and night and covers all or a quarter. So if the caking is with other than henna, he owes blood: two bloods as well. Caking means taking some marshmallow, myrtle, and gum, and placing it at the roots of the hair to become caked. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 8/3] He is absolute regarding oil, so it includes whether it is cooked or uncooked, perfumed or not perfumed. By oil he means olive oil and sesame oil, which is called shiraj. So the rest of the oils like fat and ghee are excluded. He restricted it to oiling because if he eats it or treats the cracks of his feet with it or drips it into his ear, no blood or charity is obligatory. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 9/3] Or wears stitched clothing: Know that the reality of wearing stitched clothing is that through stitching, covering of the body and retention occurs. Therefore, if he wraps himself in a shirt or cloaks himself or tucks himself into trousers, there is no problem; because he does not wear it as stitched clothing, due to lack of covering. He is absolute regarding wearing, so it includes whether he initiated wearing after ihram, or he entered ihram while wearing it and continued that, unlike his benefit after ihram from perfume applied before it, due to the text; and if not, we would have obligated it in that case as well. And it includes whether he was forgetful or intentional, knowing or ignorant, choosing or compelled. And it includes whether he wore one garment or combined all clothing: shirt, turban, and socks. Therefore, he did not say "wore a garment" like others. [al-Bahr al-Raiq abridged 11/3] Shaving, etc.: The author intended by shaving removal, whether with a razor or otherwise, and whether he is choosing or not. So if he removes it with depilatory, or plucks his beard, or his hair burns with a bread loaf, or he touches it with his hand and it falls, it is like shaving, as in al-Muhit. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 14/3] In one sitting: he restricted it to the sitting because if he cuts all in sittings, in each sitting a limb, he owes four bloods. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 18/3] Government evaluation: Its interpretation is that one looks at how much of the quarter of the beard this taken amount is, and he is obligated accordingly from food, so that if he takes half of an eighth of the beard, he owes a quarter of blood. The mention of taking from the mustache is the trimming because it is the Sunnah; he trims it until it aligns with the rim, which is the upper edge of the upper lip. [Tabyin al-Haqa'iq 2/359] It is that. And what obligates charity of half a sa' of wheat or its value is: if he perfumed less than a limb, or wore stitched clothing, or covered his head less than a day, or shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut a nail. Likewise for each nail, half a sa', unless the total reaches a blood, then he deducts from it whatever he wishes, such as five [nails] scattered. Or he performed tawaf al-qudum or tawaf al-sadr while in a state of minor impurity (hadath). And a sheep is obligated even if he performed tawaf while junub, or left one circuit (shawt) of tawaf al-sadr, and likewise for each circuit from the minimum of it, or one pebble from one of the stonings, and likewise for each pebble when it does not reach the stoning of a day, unless it reaches a blood, then he deducts whatever he wishes. Or he shaved another's head or cut his nails. And if he perfumed, wore, or shaved due to an excuse, he has a choice between slaughtering or giving charity of three sa's to six poor people, or fasting three days. And what obligates less than half a sa' is: if he kills a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. And what obligates the value is: if he kills game, then two just men appraise it at its place of killing. Half a sa': the ba is for depiction, or charity meaning the act of giving charity. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] And a sheep is obligated: meaning the obligation of half a sa' or its value was regarding when he performed tawaf while in a state of minor impurity. As for when he performed tawaf while junub, a sheep is obligatory. Or left: coordinated to what incurs charity. (Hashiyat al-Tahtawi) And likewise for each etc.: meaning likewise what is mentioned of half a sa' or its value is obligatory if he leaves a circuit from the minimum of tawaf, which is three circuits. A pebble: meaning likewise what is mentioned is obligatory if he leaves one pebble from the pebbles of stoning if the leaving does not amount to the left stoning of a day. In what does not amount: as for if it amounts to that or the majority of it, then there is blood. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi 742] Unless it amounts etc.: meaning unless the total of what obligates him reaches the price of blood, then he may deduct from it whatever he wishes. Others: he is absolute, so it includes whether the other is in ihram or not. This is contrary to if he perfumed another's limb or dressed him in stitched clothing, for he owes nothing by consensus. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743] Due to excuse: he restricted it to an excuse because if he does any of it for another purpose, he owes blood or a specific charity, and nothing else suffices, as explicitly stated by Imam al-Isbijabi. [al-Bahr al-Raiq 20/3] Killing a louse: he is absolute, so it includes whether he kills it after removing it from his body, or throws it away, or throws his garment in the sun so that it dies. For a multitude of them, which is more than three, half a sa' is obligatory. And compensation is obligatory for lice by analogy to game. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi with addition 743]
Source pages p. 271

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings (ahkam) on violations (jinayat) committed during the state of ihram in Hajj. The author, a Hanafi jurist, enumerates various actions that invalidate or diminish the perfection of the pilgrimage and specifies the required expiations. The commentary, drawn from authoritative Hanafi works such as al-Bahr al-Raiq and Hashiyat al-Tahtawi, clarifies the definitions and applications.

First, the passage lists actions that require a blood sacrifice (dam): applying henna to the head (with detailed discussion on liquid vs. caked henna), oiling the body, wearing stitched clothing (explaining that the essence is covering and retention, thus wrapping without stitching is allowed), covering the head for a full day, shaving a quarter of the head or more, cupping, shaving armpits/pub/neck, cutting nails of both hands and feet in one sitting, leaving any wajib act, and trimming the mustache (which requires a pro-rated evaluation or 'hukuma'). The commentary explains that henna is explicitly mentioned despite being a perfume because the Prophet confirmed it as perfume, and the rulings differentiate between liquid and caked henna (the latter may require two bloods: one for perfume and one for covering if it persists). Oil includes all types (cooked/raw, scented/unscented), but other fats like tallow are excluded. For stitched clothing, the ruling applies to wearing it intentionally or forgetfully, and covers all garments. Shaving is interpreted as removal by any means, and if done in multiple sittings, multiple bloods are due.

Second, the passage presents three categories of less severe violations and their fixed penalties:
- Violations requiring charity (sadaqah) of half a sa' of wheat (or its value): applying perfume to less than a full limb, wearing stitched clothing, covering the head for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, cutting one nail. If multiple nails are cut, half a sa' is due for each, but if the total value of these half-sa' obligations equals the price of a blood sacrifice, one may deduct and pay only one blood. However, if a sheep (shah) is explicitly due—such as for tawaf while in major impurity (janabah), leaving a circuit (shawt) from tawaf al-sadr, or leaving a pebble from the stoning—then a full sheep must be sacrificed, not half-sa' equivalents.
- Violations requiring less than half a sa': killing a single louse or locust; one gives charity as one wishes (the minimum is unspecified, but a handful is recommended). For multiple lice (more than three), half a sa' becomes obligatory.
- Violations requiring payment of market value: killing game (sawd/qatar); the animal is appraised by two just men at the site of killing, and the value must be given as charity.

Additionally, if a person perfumes, wears stitched clothing, or shaves due to a legitimate excuse (e.g., illness, heat), they have a choice: sacrifice a sheep, give three sa's of food to six poor people, or fast three days. This leniency does not apply if the act is done deliberately without excuse.

The passage also notes consensus that applying perfume or clothing to another person (even a non-muhrim) does not obligate anything. However, shaving another's head or cutting their nails obligates the same penalty as if done to oneself. The compensation for lice is analogized to game, indicating the principle that even harmful creatures are protected during ihram.

Throughout, the author emphasizes that the rulings apply regardless of knowledge, intent, or compulsion, except where specific exceptions are made (e.g., excuse). The commentary uses Hanafi legal terminology such as 'dam' (blood sacrifice), 'sadaqah' (charity), 'hukuma' (pro-rata valuation), and 'asl al-mas'alah' (case basis). This passage is a typical Hanafi fiqh manual section, providing a comprehensive overview of the expiations required to rectify or complete an imperfect Hajj.

Key Terms
العذر (al-‘udhr): A legitimate excuse such as illness or extreme heat that permits leniency in expiation.
القيمة (al-qimah): Market value of game killed, assessed by two just men at the place of killing.
الجمع (al-jam‘): Plural of sa‘, referring to volume measure for food charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What expiation options does a pilgrim have if he wears a stitched garment due to a legitimate excuse?
A) He must sacrifice a sheep only
B) He may choose between slaughter, feeding six poor people 3 sa‘s, or fasting three days
C) He must give half a sa‘ of wheat
D) He must fast three days only

Key Takeaway
The excuse option offers flexibility for three specific acts, but other violations and deliberate acts require fixed expiations; killing creatures has graded penalties from charity to market value.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
8 min
Categories of Hajj Violations and Their Compensations
Categorized list of Hajj violations and compensations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five categories of Hajj violations and identify the required compensation for each violation.

Core Idea
Hajj violations are compensated in tiers: half sa', sheep, choice, less than half sa', or value of game.

This lesson organizes the many prohibitions a muhrim may encounter during Hajj and the corresponding compensations. The text classifies violations into distinct groups based on the severity and type of penalty — from a simple charity of half a sa' to the full value of sacrificed game. By mastering this classification, you will be able to quickly identify the ruling for any common violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first category: half sa' violations
Read the passage and list all acts that require half a sa' of wheat or its value: perfuming less than a limb, wearing sewn garments, covering head less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, cutting a nail, and for each additional nail half a sa' unless the total reaches a sheep.
These are minor infractions; the compensation is modest.
2
Identify the second category: sheep (dam) violations
Find acts that require a full sheep: performing tawaf (arrival or departure) while in minor impurity (hadath), performing tawaf while in major impurity (janabah), omitting one circuit from the departure tawaf, omitting a pebble from stoning, shaving another's head, or cutting another's nails.
These are more serious and demand a sacrificial animal.
3
Identify the third category: violations with excuse (choice)
When a muhrim perfumes, wears sewn garments, or shaves due to a valid excuse (e.g., illness), he may choose between slaughtering a sheep, giving three sa' to six poor people, or fasting three days.
The choice offers flexibility; each option has the same reward.
4
Identify the fourth and fifth categories: less than half sa' and value of game
Killing a louse or locust requires a charity of less than half sa' (any amount he wishes). Killing game (sayd) requires paying its assessed value by two just men; if the value equals a sacrificial animal, he may choose to buy and slaughter it, give food, or fast.
Game violations are unique because they require valuation.
5
Note special cases: predatory animals and Haram vegetation
Killing a predatory animal that attacks requires nothing; otherwise, compensation does not exceed a sheep. Cutting grass or trees of the Haram (except idhkhir and truffles) requires value, not fasting.
These exceptions protect the sanctity of the Haram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الجنايات والتي توجب الصدقة بنصف صاع من بر أو قيمته هي ما لو طيب أقل من عضو، أو لبس مخيطا، أو غطى رأسه أقل من يوم أو حلق أقل من ربع رأسه، أو قصّ ظفرا، وكذا لكل ظفر نصف صاع، إلا أن يبلغ المجموع دما، فينقص ما شاء منه، كخمسة متفرقة، أو طاف للقدوم، أو للصدر محدثا وتجب شاة ولو طاف جنبا، أو ترك شوطا من طواف الصدر، وكذا لكل شوط من أقله، أو حصاة من إحدى الجمار، وكذا لكل حصاة فيما لم يبلغ رمي يوم إلا أن يبلغ دما، فينقص ما شاء، أو حلق رأس غيره، أو قص أظفاره، وإن تطيب أو لبس أو حلق بعذر تخير بين الذبح أو التصدق بثلاثة أصوع على ستة مساكين، أو صيام ثلاثة أيام، والتي توجب أقل من نصف صاع، فهي ما لو قتل قملة أو جرادة، فيتصدق بما شاء. والتي توجب القيمة هي ما لو قتل صيدا، فيقومه عدلان في مقتله، أو قريب منه، فإن بلغت هديا فله الخيار إن شاء اشتراه وذبحه، أو اشترى طعاما وتصدق به، لكل فقير نصف صاع أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به، أو صام يوما، وتجب قيمة ما نقص، وبنتف ريشه الذي لا يطير به وشعره، وقطع عضو لا يمنعه الامتناع به، وتجب القيمة بقطع بعض قوائمه، ونتف ريشه، وكسر بيضه، ولا يجاوز عن شاة بقتل السبع، وإن صال لا شيء بقتله، ولا يجزئ الصوم بقتل الحلال صيد الحرم، ولا بقطع حشيش الحرم وشجرة النابت بنفسه، وليس مما ينبته الناس بل القيمة، وحرم رعى حشيش الحرم وقطعه، إلا الإذخر والكمأة.
Rulings of violations. Those that necessitate charity (sadaqah) of half a sa' of wheat or its value are: if one perfumed less than a limb, wore sewn garments, covered his head for less than a day, shaved less than a quarter of his head, or cut a nail. Likewise, for each nail half a sa', unless the total reaches a dam (sheep), then he may reduce as he wishes, like five scattered [nails]. Or if he performed the arrival tawaf or the departure tawaf while in a state of minor impurity (hadath), a sheep is required. And if he performed tawaf while in major impurity (janaba), a sheep is required. Or if he omitted one circuit (shaut) of the departure tawaf, likewise for each circuit from the minimum [three]; or a pebble from one of the stoning sites, likewise for each pebble if it does not reach the stoning of a day, unless it reaches a dam, then he may reduce as he wishes. Or if he shaved someone else's head or cut his nails. And if he perfumed, wore [sewn garments], or shaved due to an excuse, he may choose between slaughtering (a sheep), giving charity of three sa' to six poor people, or fasting three days. Those that necessitate less than half a sa' are: if one killed a louse or a locust, then he gives charity as he wishes. Those that necessitate value are: if one killed game, then two just men assess its value at the place of killing or near it. If it amounts to a hadi (sacrificial animal), he has the choice: if he wishes, he buys it and slaughters it; or buys food and gives it in charity, to each poor person half a sa'; or fasts one day for each poor person's food. If there remains less than half a sa', he gives it in charity or fasts one day. The value of what is diminished is required: by plucking feathers with which it cannot fly, or its hair; by cutting a limb that does not prevent its ability to flee. Value is required by cutting some of its legs, plucking its feathers, breaking its egg. It does not exceed a sheep for killing a predatory animal, and if it attacks, nothing is required for killing it. Fasting is not sufficient for a non-muhrim (hillaal) killing game in the Haram, nor for cutting the grass of the Haram or a tree that grows spontaneously and is not of the type planted by people; rather, value [is required]. The grazing and cutting of Haram grass is prohibited, except idhkhir and truffles.
Source pages p. 272

Commentary
This passage is from the rulings of violations (jinayat) during Hajj. It categorizes the compensations required for various prohibited acts committed by a muhrim. The categories are: (1) Acts requiring half a sa' of wheat or its value, such as applying perfume to less than a limb, wearing sewn garments, covering the head for less than a day, shaving less than a quarter of the head, or cutting a nail. For multiple nails, each requires half a sa' unless the total reaches the value of a sheep, in which case the obligation is reduced. (2) Acts requiring a sheep, such as performing tawaf while in a state of minor impurity (hadath) for arrival or departure tawaf, or while in major impurity (janaba), or omitting one circuit from the departure tawaf, or one pebble from stoning. (3) Acts requiring a choice between slaughtering, charity, or fasting when done with an excuse (e.g., shaving due to illness). (4) Acts requiring less than half a sa', such as killing a louse or locust. (5) Acts requiring the value of the game killed, assessed by two just men. The passage also discusses killing predatory animals (no compensation if it attacks, otherwise at most a sheep), and the prohibition of cutting the grass of the Haram, except certain types. The commentary further explains details, such as that a non-muhrim who kills game in the Haram must pay value and cannot substitute fasting, and that trees that grow spontaneously and not of the type planted by people require value if cut.

Key Terms
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, approximately 2.04 kg of wheat, used as a unit for charitable compensation in Hajj violations.
شاة (shāh): A sheep (or goat) used as a sacrificial animal (dam) for violations requiring a full animal.
صيد (sayd): Wild game that is permissible to eat; killing it while in ihram necessitates compensation by value.
حرم (haram): The sacred precinct of Mecca; special prohibitions apply regarding vegetation and hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A muhrim kills a locust. What compensation is required?
A) Half a sa' of wheat
B) Less than half a sa' (any charity)
C) A sheep (dam)
D) The value of the locust

Key Takeaway
Hajj violations are compensated in five tiers; each act has a specific, proportional penalty.

Rulings on Hunting Penalties for a Muhrim - Detailed Exposition
Detailed exposition of penalties for a Muhrim harming game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi compensations for a Muhrim who harms game or sanctuary vegetation, distinguishing when fasting, food, or animal sacrifice is required, and explain the istihsan reasoning that prevents double liability.

Core Idea
A Muhrim's penalty for harming game depends on the damage value; istihsan prevents double liability for ihram and sanctuary.

This passage from Nur al-Idah presents the intricate Hanafi rulings on penalties (jinaayat) for a Muhrim who harms game or vegetation in the sanctuary. You will learn the precise compensations—animal sacrifice, food charity, or fasting—based on the extent of damage. The text also resolves a critical issue: when both ihram and sanctuary are violated, only one expiation is due, by the principle of istihsan. Understanding these distinctions ensures correct application of Hajj-related penalties.

Guided Path
1
Assess damage value
Determine the monetary value of the harm done to the game or vegetation. For animals, compare the value when sound versus injured.
Partial damage (e.g., feathers) requires calculating the decrease in value.
2
Compare to hady threshold
If the damage value reaches the value of a sacrificial animal (hady), the Muhrim has three options: slaughter an animal, give food in charity, or fast.
Hady value varies by region; see local market value.
3
Apply options for lesser damage
If damage is less than hady value, the Muhrim must pay the exact value in charity or fast accordingly.
For amounts less than half a sa', charity or one day of fasting suffices.
4
Distinguish Muhrim vs non-Muhrim
A non-Muhrim who kills game in the sanctuary must pay the value in charity; fasting is not acceptable. A Muhrim only pays one expiation for ihram due to istihsan.
The sanctuary alone does not trigger an additional penalty for the Muhrim.
5
Classify sanctuary vegetation
Identify whether the vegetation is wild and not of cultivated type; only such trees incur a penalty when cut. Owned trees require payment to both owner and Shari'ah.
After penalty, benefiting from the cut tree is disliked (makruh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام الجنايات
أو قريب منه، فإن بلغت هديا فله الخيار إن شاء اشتراه وذبحه، أو اشترى طعاما وتصدق به، لكل فقير نصف صاع أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوما، وإن فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به، أو صام يوما، وتجب قيمة ما نقص، وبنتف ريشه الذي لا يطير به وشعره، وقطع عضو لا يمنعه الامتناع به، وتجب القيمة بقطع بعض قوائمه، ونتف ريشه، وكسر بيضه، ولا يجاوز عن شاة بقتل السبع، وإن صال لا شيء بقتله، ولا يجزئ الصوم بقتل الحلال صيد الحرم، ولا بقطع حشيش الحرم وشجرة النابت بنفسه، وليس مما ينبته الناس بل القيمة، وحرم رعى حشيش الحرم وقطعه، إلا الإذخر والكمأة.
أو قريب أي مكان قريب من مقتله. ما نقص فيقوم الصيد سليما وجريحا، فيغرم ما بين القيمتين، مثلا كانت قيمته سليما در همين ثم إذا نتف ريشه نقصت قيمته در هما فيغرم ما بين القيمتين، وهو درهم. ولا يجاوز إلخ أي إذا زاد قيمة السبع الذي قتله المحرم على الشاة يؤدي قيمة الشاة، فيكفيه فيه الشاة، ولا يزاد على هذا. السبع : المراد به حيوان لا يوكل ولو خنزيرا أو فيلا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٣] ولا يجزئ إلخ أي إذا قتل رجل حلال غير محرم صيد الحرم، فعليه قيمة ما قتله يتصدق بها على الفقراء والمساكين ولا يجزئه الصوم، قيدنا بالحلال احترازا عن المحرم بقتل صيد الحرم، فإنه يلزمه كفارة واحدة؛ لأجل الإحرام ولا يجب عليه شيء لأجل الحرم استحسانا؛ لأن معنى تفويت الأمن إذا اعتبر مرة؛ لإيجاب الضمان لا يمكن اعتباره ثانيا؛ لإيجاب ضمان وإنما أوجبنا ضمان الإحرام؛ لأن فيه معنى الجزاء وضمان المحل، وضمان الحرم لا يشتمل على معنى ضمان الإحرام فكان في معنى إيجاب ما هو مشتمل على المعنيين أولى. حشيش الحرم: اعلم أن شجر الحرم أنواع أربعة ثلاث يحل قطعها والانتفاع بها من غير جزاء، وواحدة منها لا يحل قطعها والانتفاع بها، وإذا قطعها رجل فعليه الجزاء، أما الثلاث فكل شجر أنبته الناس، وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس، وكل شجر أنبته الناس وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس وكل شجر نبت بنفسه وهو من جنس ما ينبته الناس وأما الواحدة فهي كل شجر نبت بنفسه وهو ليس من جنس ما ينبته الناس، ويستوي في هذه الواحدة أن تكون مملوكة لإنسان بأن تنبت في ملكه أو لم يكن حتى قالوا في رجل نبتت في ملكه أم غيلان فقطعها إنسان فعليه قيمتها لمالكها، وقيمة أخرى لحق الشرع، بمنزلة ما لو قتل صيدا مملوكا في الحرم، وبعد ما أدى جزاء الشجرة يكره للقاطع الانتفاع بها. [الكفاية: ٣٣/٣]
Rulings of offenses. Or near it, for if it reaches the value of a sacrificial animal, he has the choice: if he wishes, he buys it and slaughters it, or buys food and gives charity with it, giving each poor person half a sa', or fasts one day for each poor person's food. And if there remains less than half a sa', he gives charity with it or fasts a day. And the value of what is diminished must be paid. And for plucking feathers with which it does not fly, and its hair, and cutting a limb that does not prevent it from defending itself, and the value must be paid for cutting some of its legs, plucking its feathers, and breaking its eggs. And [the penalty] does not exceed a sheep for killing a predatory animal. And if it attacks, there is no penalty for killing it. And fasting is not acceptable for a non-muhrim killing game of the sanctuary, nor for cutting the grass of the sanctuary and a tree that grows by itself and is not from what people cultivate; rather, the value [must be paid]. And grazing the grass of the sanctuary and cutting it is forbidden, except al-idhkhir and truffles. 'Or near it' meaning a place near its killing place. 'What is diminished' means the game is valued sound and injured, and he pays the difference between the two values. For example, its value when sound was two dirhams, then when he plucked its feathers its value decreased by two dirhams, so he pays the difference, which is one dirham. 'And does not exceed' etc. meaning if the value of the predatory animal that the muhrim killed exceeds a sheep, he pays the value of a sheep, and a sheep suffices him, and no increase beyond that. 'Predatory animal': what is meant is an animal not eaten, even if it is a pig or an elephant [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 743]. 'And fasting is not acceptable' etc. meaning if a non-muhrim man kills game of the sanctuary, he must pay the value of what he killed, giving charity to the poor and needy, and fasting does not suffice him. We restricted it to a non-muhrim as a precaution regarding the muhrim who kills game of the sanctuary, for he is obligated one expiation for ihram, and nothing is obligatory upon him for the sanctuary by istihsan, because the meaning of violating security, if considered once for imposing liability, cannot be considered a second time to impose liability. Rather we imposed the liability of ihram because it contains the meaning of recompense and liability of the place, while the liability of the sanctuary does not include the meaning of liability of ihram, so it is more appropriate to impose something that includes both meanings. 'Grass of the sanctuary': Know that the trees of the sanctuary are four types: three of them are permissible to cut and benefit from without penalty, and one of them is not permissible to cut and benefit from, and if a man cuts it, he must pay a penalty. As for the three: every tree that people cultivated and is not of the type that people cultivate, and every tree that people cultivated and is of the type that people cultivate, and every tree that grows by itself and is of the type that people cultivate. As for the one: every tree that grows by itself and is not of the type that people cultivate. And this one is the same whether it is owned by a person by growing on his property or not, such that they said about a man: if a 'um ghaylan tree grows on his property and someone cuts it, he must pay its value to its owner and another value for the right of the Shari'ah, analogous to if he killed owned game in the sanctuary, and after he pays the penalty for the tree, it is disliked for the cutter to benefit from it. [Al-Kifayah: 33/3]
Source pages p. 273

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on penalties (jinaayat) for a Muhrim who harms game or vegetation in the sanctuary. The author, from Nur al-Idah, states the core rules: if the compensation reaches the value of a hady, the Muhrim may choose to purchase and slaughter an animal, give food, or fast. For partial damage, value is assessed by comparing the sound and injured price. For predatory animals (those not eaten), the penalty does not exceed a sheep; if the animal attacks, no penalty. A key distinction: a non-Muhrim who kills game in the sanctuary must pay its value in charity; fasting is not acceptable. This is because the Muhrim already bears one expiation for ihram, so the sanctuary's violation is waived by istihsan (juristic preference). The passage then details the classification of sanctuary trees: four types based on origin and cultivation, with only wild trees not of cultivated type requiring penalty. If such a tree is owned, the cutter pays both the owner's value and a Shari'ah penalty. After payment, benefiting from the cut tree is disliked (makruh). These rulings are based on the Hanafi school's reasoning, emphasizing istihsan to avoid double liability.

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): An offense or infraction committed by a Muhrim against game or sanctuary vegetation, requiring monetary or fasting compensation.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the sanctuary; when the value of the damage reaches that of a hady, the Muhrim has a choice of slaughtering an animal, giving food, or fasting.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference used here to avoid double liability—the Muhrim is not penalized separately for the sanctuary because the meaning of violating security is already accounted for by the ihram expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for a non-Muhrim who kills game in the sanctuary?
A) He must fast one day for each poor person.
B) He must pay the value of the game in charity to the poor.
C) He must sacrifice an animal.
D) No penalty is required.

Key Takeaway
A Muhrim's compensation for harming game is structured with options, while a non-Muhrim must pay value; istihsan eliminates double liability for the sanctuary.

Animals Permitted to Kill in Ihram
List of exempted animals with commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animals that a Muhrim may kill without penalty and state the principle that any creature not considered game (ṣayd) is exempt.

Core Idea
Harmful and non-game animals are exempt from hunting prohibitions in ihram.

In the state of ihram, the general prohibition of hunting game is strict, but certain animals are exempt from any penalty. This lesson presents the specific list from the Nur al-Idah text, along with the underlying principle: creatures that are not considered ṣayd (edible wild game) or are harmful may be killed freely. Understanding this exemption helps avoid unnecessary expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category of exempted animals
Recognize that the list includes predators, pests, and harmful creatures—not game animals.
The principle is that ṣayd is only what is normally hunted and eaten.
2
Memorize the list of animals
Recite each animal: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, biting dog (wolf/lion), mosquitoes, ants (except magpie), fleas, ticks, turtles.
Note the exception: magpie (العقعق) is excluded, so its killing incurs a penalty.
3
Apply the principle to new cases
For any creature not on the list but similar in nature (harmful, non-game), analogize using the principle that non-ṣayd is exempt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
ولا شيء بقتل غراب وحدأة وعقرب وفارة وحية وكلب عقور وبعوض ونمل أي إلا العقعق بكسر ففتحتين
وبرغوث وقراد وسلحفاة وما ليس بصيد.
بقتل غراب: لم يقل: ليس في قتل المحرم إلخ جزاء، بل أطلق نفي الجزاء في قتلهن ليفيد أنه لا يستعقب جزاء في الحرم، ولا في الإحرام. [فتح القدير : ١٦/٣] وكلب عقور: قيل: المراد به الذئب، وقيل: الأسد. (هداية، فتح القدير) برغوث بياء مضمومة وغين معجمة مضمومة وواو معروفة وثاء مثلثة نوع من الحشرات يقال له بالأردية: يسو.
قراد بضم القاف ودال مهملة دويبة متطفلة تعيش على الحيوانات وخاصة على الكلب، يقال له بالأردية: چیچڑى. سلحفاة بضم الأول وفتح اللام وسكون الحاء المهملة وفاء وتاء حيوان برمائي من الزواحف يقال له بالأردية: کچھوا.
Section: And there is nothing [i.e., no penalty] for killing a crow, a kite, a scorpion, a mouse, a snake, a biting dog, mosquitoes, ants—except the magpie—and fleas, ticks, turtles, and whatever is not game. Regarding 'killing a crow': He did not say 'There is no penalty for the Muhrim killing etc.' but rather he stated the negation of penalty in killing them absolutely to indicate that it entails no penalty in the sanctuary nor in ihram. [Fath al-Qadir: 16/3] 'Biting dog': It is said what is meant is the wolf, and it is said the lion. (Hidayah, Fath al-Qadir) 'Flea' (برغوث): with a damma on the ba', a damma on the ghayn, and a waw and tha'—a type of insect called in Urdu: 'yaso'. 'Tick' (قراد): with a damma on the qaf and an important dal—a parasitic insect living on animals, especially dogs, called in Urdu: 'chichri'. 'Turtle' (سلحفاة): with a damma on the first, fatha on the lam, sukun on the ha', fa', and ta'—an amphibian reptile called in Urdu: 'kacchua'.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This short passage lists animals that a Muhrim may kill without incurring any penalty (not even in the sanctuary). The author, from the chapter on Hadi, explicitly states that there is no compensation required for killing these creatures. The commentary clarifies that the negation of penalty applies in both the state of ihram and within the sanctuary. The list includes common pests and predators: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, biting dog (interpreted as wolf or lion), mosquitoes, ants (except magpie), fleas, ticks, turtles, and anything not considered game (صيد). The commentators (from Fath al-Qadir, Hidayah) provide definitions for some terms in Urdu, aiding the reader. The ruling is straightforward: these animals are excluded from the general prohibition of killing game, and their killing is permissible without any expiation or compensation.

Key Terms
صيد (ṣayd): Game animals that are normally hunted and eaten; the list excludes creatures that are not considered game, so no penalty.
كلب عقور (kalb ʿaqūr): A ravenous dog; interpreted as wolf or lion in the commentary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Rules of Hadi: Types, Conditions, and Exceptions
Definition and conditions of Hadi with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of Hadi, identify the conditions for validity, and apply the rule that a sheep suffices except in two specific cases where a camel is required.

Core Idea
A sheep suffices for Hadi except for Tawaf while junub and intercourse before shaving—then a camel is wajib.

This lesson clarifies the definition of Hadi (sacrificial animal in Hajj), its required types, and the crucial exceptions where only a camel (badanah) is acceptable. Understanding these conditions ensures that your sacrificial offering is valid according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of Hadi
The lowest type is a sheep; camels and cattle are also valid. Minimum ages: camels 5 years, cattle 2 years. Sheep age is not specified but follows Udhiyah rules (typically 1 year or 6 months if fat).
The Hadi must be from the same species as Udhiyah.
2
Note the conditions for validity
The same conditions as Udhiyah regarding physical defects apply: the animal must be free from blindness, lameness, etc. These defects render the Hadi invalid.
This is derived from the text's statement: 'What is permissible for Udhiyah is permissible for Hadi.'
3
Distinguish the general rule and its exceptions
A sheep suffices in all cases except two: (1) performing Tawaf while junub, and (2) intercourse after Arafah before shaving (for Tamattu' and Qiran). In these cases, a camel is required.
The text also mentions that a woman who performs Tawaf while menstruating or postpartum must offer a camel by analogy.
4
Understand the time restriction
The Hadi for Tamattu' and Qiran is specific to the day of sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah). Other penalties (dam) or voluntary Hadi are not time-restricted, though slaughtering on that day is preferable.
This is a key distinction: voluntary Hadi can be offered any time once in the sanctuary.
5
Apply to vow cases
If a person vows to sacrifice a camel, a sheep does not suffice. The text emphasizes that the exception for sheep is not absolute; vows must be fulfilled as specified.
This prevents using the general rule to override a specific vow.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل
الهدي أدناه شاة، وهو من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا.
يفيد أن له أعلى
والشاة تجوز في كل شيء إلا في طواف الركن جنبا، ووطء بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق،
المتعة ففي كل منهما بدنة، وخص هدي والقران بيوم النحر فقط،
الإبل إلخ ويكون مما مضى عليه خمس سنين، ومن البقر ما مضى عليه سنتان، ولو قال: وأعلاه إبل وبقر، لكان أولى [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] جاز في الهدايا فكل ما يشترط في الضحايا من عن العيوب التي تمنع الجواز كالعور والعرج يشترط هنا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] تجوز إلخ يعني أن كل موضع ذكر فيه الدم من كتاب الحج تجزئ فيه الشاة إلا فيما ذكره، وليس مراده التعميم؛ فإن من نذر بدنة أو جزورا لا تجزئه الشاة، وإنما لزمت البدنة فيما إذا طاف جنبا؛ لأن الجنابة أغلظ، نقصانها بالبدنة إظهارا للتفاوت بين الأصغر والأكبر، ويلحق به ما إذا طافت حائضا أو نفساء، فيجب جبر
وليس موضعا ثالثا كما في "فتح القدير"؛ لأن المعنى الموجب للتغليظ واحد. [البحر الرائق: ٩٨/٣] بيوم النحر فقط بيان لكون الهدي مؤقتا بالمكان سواء كان دم شكر أو جناية، وأما توقيته بالزمان فمخصوص والقرآن، وأما بقية الهدايا فلا يتقيد بزمان، وأفاد أن هدي التطوع إذا بلغ الحرم لا يتقيد بزمان، وهو الصحيح، وإن كان ذبحه يوم النحر أفضل البحر الرائق بحذف: ١٠٠/٣]
بهدي المتعة
Section: The Hadi: its lowest [type] is a sheep, and it is from camels, cattle, and sheep. And whatever is permissible for Udhiyah is permissible for Hadi. This indicates that it has a highest [type]. And the sheep suffices in everything except in [the case of] performing the ritual Tawaf while junub, and intercourse after standing at Arafah before shaving [the head]—for Tamattu' and Qiran, in each of these two there is a camel. And the Hadi is specified for the day of sacrifice only. [Commentary:] 'Camels etc.' and it must be one that has completed five years, and from cattle what has completed two years. And if he said: 'And its highest is camels and cattle', it would be better. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 744] 'Whatever is permissible for Udhiyah' so every condition that is required for Udhiyah regarding the defects that prevent permissibility, such as blindness and lameness, is required here. [Hashiyat al-Tahtawi: 744] 'The sheep suffices' etc. meaning that every place where blood [i.e., a sacrifice] is mentioned in the book of Hajj, a sheep suffices for it except for what he mentioned. And his intention is not generalization; for if someone vows a camel or a male camel, a sheep does not suffice for him. The camel became necessary in the case of performing Tawaf while junub because janabah is more severe; its deficiency [is compensated] by a camel to show the difference between the minor and major [impurity]. And annexed to it is the case where a woman performs Tawaf while menstruating or postpartum, so compensation is obligatory. And there is no third place, as in Fath al-Qadir, because the meaning that necessitates intensification is one. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: 98/3] 'For the day of sacrifice only' is a statement that the Hadi is restricted to the place, whether it is blood of thanksgiving or penalty. As for its temporal restriction, it is specific to Tamattu' and Qiran. As for the rest of the Hadi, they are not restricted to a time. And it shows that voluntary Hadi, when it reaches the sanctuary, is not restricted to a time, and that is correct, although slaughtering it on the day of sacrifice is better. [Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq abridged: 100/3] 'With the Hadi of Tamattu'.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This section defines the Hadi (sacrificial animal) obligatory in Hajj. The lowest acceptable animal is a sheep; camels and cattle are also valid, but a sheep suffices for most situations. The conditions for Udhiyah (Eid sacrifice) regarding defects apply similarly to Hadi. However, there are exceptions: if a Muhrim performs Tawaf while junub (major impurity), or has intercourse after standing at Arafah but before shaving, a camel is required instead of a sheep for Tamattu' and Qiran. This is because the violation is more severe, and a camel demonstrates the greater deficiency. Similarly, a woman who performs Tawaf while menstruating or postpartum must also offer a camel. The Hadi for Tamattu' and Qiran is time-specific to the day of sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah), but other Hadi (e.g., for penalties or voluntary) are not restricted to that day; however, slaughtering on that day is preferable. The commentary clarifies that a sheep always suffices unless a specific exception is mentioned; but if one vowed a camel, a sheep is not acceptable. The passage stresses that the Hadi must be free from defects like blindness or lameness.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the sanctuary, either as part of Hajj (Tamattu', Qiran) or as penalty (dam).
بدنة (badanah): A camel used as a sacrificial animal; required for severe violations like Tawaf in janabah.
دم (dam): Literally 'blood', used here to mean a sacrifice (penalty) required for various infractions during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which situation does a sheep NOT suffice for Hadi according to this passage?
A) For a vow (nadhr) to sacrifice a camel
B) For Tamattu' Hadi
C) For performing Tawaf while junub
D) For a penalty (dam) for missing a wajib

Key Takeaway
A sheep suffices for all Hadi except when Tawaf is performed while junub or intercourse occurs before shaving for Tamattu' and Qiran, in which a camel is required.

Exempt Creatures in Ihram: No Penalty for Harmful Animals
A ruling listing creatures exempt from compensation in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the harmful creatures that may be killed in ihram without compensation and identify the exception of the magpie.

Core Idea
Killing harmful creatures in ihram incurs no penalty, except for game animals and the magpie.

During ihram, hunting game is prohibited, but the Hanafi school exempts killing certain harmful creatures that pose a threat or nuisance. This passage from Nur al-Idah specifies which creatures are exempt from compensation (jaza'). Understanding this list helps pilgrims avoid unnecessary penalty while protecting themselves from harm.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the ruling's scope
The passage states that killing certain creatures during ihram requires no compensation. These creatures are considered harmful or nuisance animals, not game.
The ruling applies specifically to the state of ihram.
2
Memorize the exempt list
The text names: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog (interpreted as wolf or lion), mosquito, and ant. Also flea, tick, and tortoise are included.
These are all creatures that can cause harm or annoyance.
3
Identify the exception
The passage explicitly excepts the magpie (al-ʿaqʿaq). Killing a magpie in ihram does require compensation because it is considered game or not exempt.
The exception is key: not all birds are exempt.
4
Apply the underlying principle
The principle is that anything not considered game (sayd) and is harmful is exempt. Game animals are those that are edible and hunted for food; they require compensation if killed in ihram.
This helps extend the ruling to similar creatures not explicitly listed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل ولا شيء بقتل غراب وحدأة وعقرب وفارة وحية وكلب عقور وبعوض ونمل أي إلا العقعق بكسر ففتحتين وبرغوث وقراد وسلحفاة وما ليس بصيد. كلب عقور: قيل: المراد به الذئب، وقيل: الأسد. (هداية، فتح القدير) برغوث بياء مضمومة وغين معجمة مضمومة وواو معروفة وثاء مثلثة نوع من الحشرات يقال له بالأردية: يسو. سلامة قراد بضم القاف ودال مهملة دويبة متطفلة تعيش على الحيوانات وخاصة على الكلب، يقال له بالأردية: چیچڑى. سلحفاة بضم الأول وفتح اللام وسكون الحاء المهملة وفاء وتاء حيوان برمائي من الزواحف يقال له بالأردية: کچھوا.
Fasl: And there is nothing [required] for killing a crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog, mosquito, and ant - meaning except the magpie (with kasrah on the first letter and fatha on the second), flea, tick, tortoise, and whatever is not game. Vicious dog: it is said what is meant is wolf, and it is said lion. (Hidayah, Fath al-Qadir) Flea: with ya' damma, ghayn mu'jama damma, waw, tha' muthallatha, a type of insect called in Urdu 'yasu'. Salama? Tick: with qaf damma and dal muhmala, a parasitic insect living on animals especially dogs, called in Urdu 'chichri'. Tortoise: with damma on first letter, fatha on lam, sukun on ha' muhmala, fa', ta', an amphibious reptile called in Urdu 'kachhua'.
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding animals and insects whose killing by a person in ihram (or in the Haram) does not require any compensation (jaza'). The base text lists: crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, snake, vicious dog (interpreted as wolf or lion), mosquito, and ant. However, an exception is made for the magpie (al-ʿaqʿaq), which is not included in the exemption. The commentary further clarifies the meanings of the terms 'flea', 'tick', and 'tortoise' with Urdu equivalents. The principle is that killing harmful creatures that are not considered game (sayd) is free from penalty, while killing game animals would require compensation.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation required for violating ihram by killing game.
صيد (sayd): Game animals that are lawful to hunt outside ihram; killing them in ihram requires compensation.
عقعق (ʿaqʿaq): Magpie, a bird excepted from the exemption list.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following creatures does NOT incur a penalty when killed by a muhrim according to this passage?
A) Pigeon
B) Magpie
C) Scorpion
D) Locust

Key Takeaway
In ihram, killing harmful creatures such as scorpions, snakes, and mosquitoes does not require compensation, except for game animals and the magpie.

Minimum and Types of Hady
Ruling statement defining minimum and types of hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum and permissible types of hady and list the conditions that must be met for its validity.

Core Idea
The minimum hady is a sheep, but camels and cattle are also valid; all conditions of udhiyah apply.

This lesson establishes the baseline for sacrificial animals in Hajj. The author begins by defining the minimum animal and the species that are permissible, then links the conditions to those of the Eid sacrifice (udhiyah). Understanding these basics is essential before exploring exceptions and additional rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum animal
Find where the text states the minimum (adna) for hady. It explicitly says 'adnahu shaatun' – a sheep is the lowest acceptable.
Note that the Arabic word أدناه means 'the lowest' or 'minimum'.
2
List the permissible species
The text says it is from camels, cattle, and sheep. Identify these as the three categories – ibil, baqar, ghanam.
Other animals like goats may fall under ghanam in some contexts.
3
Connect to udhiyah conditions
The text states 'Ma jaza fi al-dahaya jaza fi al-hadaya' – whatever is permissible for udhiyah is permissible for hady. This implies all the same conditions regarding age, freedom from defects, etc.
This is a key principle linking two related sacrifices.
4
Note the generality of sheep
The author later clarifies that a sheep suffices for most cases where blood (dam) is required, except specific exceptions. This sets up the next lesson.
This is a preview of the exceptions to come.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الهدي أدناه شاة، وهو من الإبل والبقر والغنم، وما جاز في الضحايا جاز في الهدايا. يفيد أن له أعلى والشاة تجوز في كل شيء إلا في طواف الركن جنبا، ووطء بعد الوقوف قبل الحلق، المتعة ففي كل منهما بدنة، وخص هدي والقران بيوم النحر فقط، بقتل غراب: لم يقل: ليس في قتل المحرم إلخ جزاء، بل أطلق نفي الجزاء في قتلهن ليفيد أنه لا يستعقب جزاء في الحرم، ولا في الإحرام. [فتح القدير : ١٦/٣] وكلب عقور: قيل: المراد به الذئب، وقيل: الأسد. (هداية، فتح القدير) برغوث بياء مضمومة وغين معجمة مضمومة وواو معروفة وثاء مثلثة نوع من الحشرات يقال له بالأردية: يسو. السلامة قراد بضم القاف ودال مهملة دويبة متطفلة تعيش على الحيوانات وخاصة على الكلب، يقال له بالأردية: چیچڑى. سلحفاة بضم الأول وفتح اللام وسكون الحاء المهملة وفاء وتاء حيوان برمائي من الزواحف يقال له بالأردية: کچھوا. الإبل إلخ ويكون مما مضى عليه خمس سنين، ومن البقر ما مضى عليه سنتان، ولو قال: وأعلاه إبل وبقر، لكان أولى [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] جاز في الهدايا فكل ما يشترط في الضحايا من عن العيوب التي تمنع الجواز كالعور والعرج يشترط هنا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] تجوز إلخ يعني أن كل موضع ذكر فيه الدم من كتاب الحج تجزئ فيه الشاة إلا فيما ذكره، وليس مراده التعميم؛ فإن من نذر بدنة أو جزورا لا تجزئه الشاة، وإنما لزمت البدنة فيما إذا طاف جنبا؛ لأن الجنابة أغلظ، نقصانها بالبدنة إظهارا للتفاوت بين الأصغر والأكبر، ويلحق به ما إذا طافت حائضا أو نفساء، فيجب جبر وليس موضعا ثالثا كما في "فتح القدير"؛ لأن المعنى الموجب للتغليظ واحد. [البحر الرائق: ٩٨/٣] بيوم النحر فقط بيان لكون الهدي مؤقتا بالمكان سواء كان دم شكر أو جناية، وأما توقيته بالزمان فمخصوص والقرآن، وأما بقية الهدايا فلا يتقيد بزمان، وأفاد أن هدي التطوع إذا بلغ الحرم لا يتقيد بزمان، وهو الصحيح، وإن كان ذبحه يوم النحر أفضل البحر الرائق بحذف: ١٠٠/٣] بهدي المتعة  ٢٧٤ زيارة النبي كتاب الحج وخص ذبح كل هدي بالحرم إلا أن يكون تطوعا وتعيب في الطريق، فينحر في محله، ولا يشترط له منى ولا يأكله غني وفقير الحرم وغيره سواء، وتقلّد بدنة التطوع والمتعة والقرآن فقط، لكن فقيره أفضل ندبا ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولا يعطى أجر الجزار منه ولا يركبه بلا ضرورة، زمام الذباح ولا يحلب لبنه إلا أن بعد المحل فيتصدق به، وينضح ضرعه إن قرب المحل بالنقاخ، هو الماء البارد ولو نذر حجا ماشيا لزمه ولا يركب حتى يطوف للركن، فإن ركب أراق دما، أي صبه وفضل المشي على الركوب للقادر عليه. وفقنا الله تعالى بفضله، ومن علينا بالعود على أحسن حال إليه بجاه سيدنا محمد الحج فصل في زيارة النبي على سبيل الاختصار تبعا لما قال في الاختيار لما كانت زيارة النبي من أفضل القرب وأحسن المستحبات، كل هدي دخل فيه الهدي المنذور، بخلاف البدنة المنذورة، فإنها لا تتقيد بالحرم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد حما. [البحر الرائق: ١٠٠/٣] بجلاله الجلال جمع الجل، وهو ما يلبس على الدابة، والخطام: هو الزمام، وهو ما يجعل في أنف البعير البحر الرائق: ١٠٠/٣] أجر الجزار إلخ قيد بالأجر؛ لأنه لو تصدق بشيء من لحمها عليه سوى أجرته جاز ؛ لأنه أهل للتصدق عليه . [ البحر الرائق: ۱۰۱/۳] ولا يركبه أشار إلى أنه لا يحمل عليها أيضا، وإلى أنه لو ركبها أو حمل عليها فنقصت فعليه ضمان ما نقص [البحر الرائق: ١٠١/٣] وينضح ضرعه إلخ أي يرش بالماء البارد حتى يتقلص والنقاخ بالنون المضمومة والقاف والخاء المعجمة: الماء العذب الذي ينقخ الفؤاد ببرده، كذا في "الصحاح" و"المغرب"، وفي "المصباح المنير": ينضح من بابي "ضرب ونفع" فعلى هذا تكسر ضاده وتفتح قالوا: هذا إذا كان قريبا من وقت الذبح وإن كان بعيدا يحلبها، ويتصدق بلبنها، كي لا يضر بها ذلك. [البحر الرائق: ۱۰۱/۳] لزمه قيل: يمشي من حين يحرم، وقيل: من بيته، وهو الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٥ زيارة النبي إلخ : قالوا: إن كان الحج فرضا قدمه عليها، وإلا يخير، =
Fasl: The lowest [type] of hady is a sheep. It is from camels, cattle, and sheep. And whatever is permissible for udhiyah is permissible for hady. It indicates that it has a highest [type]. And the sheep is permissible for everything except for the tawaf of the rukn while junub, and intercourse after standing [at Arafat] before shaving [the head]; for tamattu' each of them requires a camel; and he specified the hady of tamattu' and qiran to the day of Nahr only... [continues with detailed rulings on conditions, sacrifice location, etc.]
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the sacrificial animals (hady) in Hajj. It begins by stating that the minimum hady is a sheep, and can also be from camels or cattle. All conditions that apply to udhiyah (sacrificial animals for Eid) apply to hady as well, such as being free from defects like blindness and lameness. The sheep suffices for most cases where blood (dam) is required, except for two specific situations: performing the obligatory tawaf while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and having intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving the head. In these cases, a camel (badanah) is required due to the severity of the violation. Similarly, the hady for tamattu' and qiran must be sacrificed on the day of Nahr only, and the sacrifice must be within the Haram. Additional rulings cover: dyeing the animal's covering, not giving the slaughterer's fee from the meat, not riding the sacrificial animal unnecessarily, milking it only if its udder is full, etc. The passage also discusses the virtue of walking versus riding for the capable pilgrim, and concludes with a supplication.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the Haram during Hajj, often as a required atonement or voluntary offering.
ضحايا (dahaya): Plural of udhiyah, animals sacrificed on Eid al-Adha; their conditions apply to hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the minimum animal accepted as hady?
A) A camel
B) A cow
C) A sheep
D) Any animal from the camel, cattle, or sheep family

Key Takeaway
The minimum hady is a sheep, and all conditions for udhiyah apply, but exceptions exist where a camel is required.

When a Camel is Required for Hady
Exceptions to the general rule that a sheep suffices for hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two specific situations where a camel (badanah) is required instead of a sheep, and also the cases of tamattu' and qiran that require a camel.

Core Idea
A sheep suffices for most hady, but tawaf while junub and intercourse after wuquf each require a camel; tamattu' and qiran also require a camel.

The previous lesson established the general rule that a sheep is the minimum and suffices for most cases. This lesson dives into the exceptions explicitly mentioned in the text. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly fulfilling the sacrificial obligations during Hajj, especially when violations occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first exception: tawaf while junub
The text states that the sheep is permissible for everything except performing the obligatory tawaf (rukn) while in a state of major impurity (junub). In that case, a camel (badanah) is required.
The reason given in commentary: because janabah is a severe state, the expiation is intensified.
2
Identify the second exception: intercourse after wuquf
The text mentions 'wat' ba'da al-wuquf qabla al-halq' – intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving the head. This also requires a camel.
Note: This is considered a major violation that invalidates Hajj in some cases, hence the heavier expiation.
3
Understand the hady for tamattu' and qiran
The text says 'al-mut'ah fa fi kulli minhuma badanah' – for tamattu', each requires a camel. And he specified the hady of tamattu' and qiran to the day of Nahr only.
The requirement for tamattu' and qiran is wajib (obligatory), not just expiatory. They must be performed on the day of Nahr.
4
Distinguish between types of hady
Not all hady require a camel. The exceptions are specific: major violations and the obligatory hady of tamattu'/qiran. Other atonements (like killing game, omitting a wajib) require a sheep.
The commentary elaborates that the camel serves to show the disparity between minor and major faults.

Source Text

[البحر الرائق: ١٠٠/٣] بجلاله الجلال جمع الجل، وهو ما يلبس على الدابة، والخطام: هو الزمام، وهو ما يجعل في أنف البعير البحر الرائق: ١٠٠/٣] أجر الجزار إلخ قيد بالأجر؛ لأنه لو تصدق بشيء من لحمها عليه سوى أجرته جاز ؛ لأنه أهل للتصدق عليه . [ البحر الرائق: ۱۰۱/۳] ولا يركبه أشار إلى أنه لا يحمل عليها أيضا، وإلى أنه لو ركبها أو حمل عليها فنقصت فعليه ضمان ما نقص [البحر الرائق: ١٠١/٣] وينضح ضرعه إلخ أي يرش بالماء البارد حتى يتقلص والنقاخ بالنون المضمومة والقاف والخاء المعجمة: الماء العذب الذي ينقخ الفؤاد ببرده، كذا في "الصحاح" و"المغرب"، وفي "المصباح المنير": ينضح من بابي "ضرب ونفع" فعلى هذا تكسر ضاده وتفتح قالوا: هذا إذا كان قريبا من وقت الذبح وإن كان بعيدا يحلبها، ويتصدق بلبنها، كي لا يضر بها ذلك. [البحر الرائق: ۱۰۱/۳] لزمه قيل: يمشي من حين يحرم، وقيل: من بيته، وهو الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٥ زيارة النبي إلخ : قالوا: إن كان الحج فرضا قدمه عليها، وإلا يخير، =
Fasl: The lowest [type] of hady is a sheep. It is from camels, cattle, and sheep. And whatever is permissible for udhiyah is permissible for hady. It indicates that it has a highest [type]. And the sheep is permissible for everything except for the tawaf of the rukn while junub, and intercourse after standing [at Arafat] before shaving [the head]; for tamattu' each of them requires a camel; and he specified the hady of tamattu' and qiran to the day of Nahr only... [continues with detailed rulings on conditions, sacrifice location, etc.]
Source pages p. 274

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling on the sacrificial animals (hady) in Hajj. It begins by stating that the minimum hady is a sheep, and can also be from camels or cattle. All conditions that apply to udhiyah (sacrificial animals for Eid) apply to hady as well, such as being free from defects like blindness and lameness. The sheep suffices for most cases where blood (dam) is required, except for two specific situations: performing the obligatory tawaf while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and having intercourse after standing at Arafat but before shaving the head. In these cases, a camel (badanah) is required due to the severity of the violation. Similarly, the hady for tamattu' and qiran must be sacrificed on the day of Nahr only, and the sacrifice must be within the Haram. Additional rulings cover: dyeing the animal's covering, not giving the slaughterer's fee from the meat, not riding the sacrificial animal unnecessarily, milking it only if its udder is full, etc. The passage also discusses the virtue of walking versus riding for the capable pilgrim, and concludes with a supplication.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A camel that is sacrificed; required in severe cases of violation during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following requires a camel (badanah) according to this passage?
A) Omission of sa'i between Safa and Marwah
B) Performing tawaf al-rukn while junub
C) Killing a louse during ihram
D) Voluntary hady

Key Takeaway
A camel is required for tawaf while junub, intercourse after wuquf, and for the obligatory hady of tamattu' and qiran.

Timing, Location, and Handling of Hady
Rules on timing, location, and handling of hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the proper time and place for sacrificing hady, and state the rules regarding covering, riding, and milking the animal.

Core Idea
The hady must be sacrificed in the Haram, and for tamattu'/qiran specifically on the day of Nahr; additional rules apply to prevent burdening the animal.

Having covered the minimum and exceptions, this lesson addresses the temporal and spatial conditions for hady, as well as practical rules for handling the animal before slaughter. These details ensure that the sacrifice is performed correctly and with due care for the animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time restrictions for hady
The text specifies that the hady for tamattu' and qiran is limited to the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). For other types of hady (e.g., atonement, voluntary), there is no strict time limit within the Haram, though it is best to sacrifice on the day of Nahr.
The commentary from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that voluntary hady is not time-bound.
2
Identify the place: the Haram
All hady must be sacrificed within the boundaries of the Haram (the sanctuary of Makkah). The exception is a voluntary animal that becomes defective en route – then it can be sacrificed at its location.
The author mentions that it is not restricted to Mina specifically, though Mina is the preferred place for hady of tamattu' and qiran.
3
Learn about adorning the animal (taqlid)
The text mentions that only the hady of tamattu', qiran, and voluntary (nafl) are to be adorned with a garland (qilada) and marked (ish'arl), not the hady of atonement.
This distinguishes between obligatory and voluntary types.
4
Understand the rules of usage: no riding, no milking without necessity
The sacrificial animal should not be ridden unless necessary, and its milk should not be taken unless the udder is painfully full, in which case it is milked and the milk given in charity. The animal's covering (jall) and nose string (khatam) are to be given in charity as well.
The goal is to avoid burdening the animal and to ensure the entire benefit goes to charity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[فتح القدير : ١٦/٣] وكلب عقور: قيل: المراد به الذئب، وقيل: الأسد. (هداية، فتح القدير) برغوث بياء مضمومة وغين معجمة مضمومة وواو معروفة وثاء مثلثة نوع من الحشرات يقال له بالأردية: يسو. السلامة قراد بضم القاف ودال مهملة دويبة متطفلة تعيش على الحيوانات وخاصة على الكلب، يقال له بالأردية: چیچڑى. سلحفاة بضم الأول وفتح اللام وسكون الحاء المهملة وفاء وتاء حيوان برمائي من الزواحف يقال له بالأردية: کچھوا. الإبل إلخ ويكون مما مضى عليه خمس سنين، ومن البقر ما مضى عليه سنتان، ولو قال: وأعلاه إبل وبقر، لكان أولى [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] جاز في الهدايا فكل ما يشترط في الضحايا من عن العيوب التي تمنع الجواز كالعور والعرج يشترط هنا [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٤] تجوز إلخ يعني أن كل موضع ذكر فيه الدم من كتاب الحج تجزئ فيه الشاة إلا فيما ذكره، وليس مراده التعميم؛ فإن من نذر بدنة أو جزورا لا تجزئه الشاة، وإنما لزمت البدنة فيما إذا طاف جنبا؛ لأن الجنابة أغلظ، نقصانها بالبدنة إظهارا للتفاوت بين الأصغر والأكبر، ويلحق به ما إذا طافت حائضا أو نفساء، فيجب جبر وليس موضعا ثالثا كما في "فتح القدير"؛ لأن المعنى الموجب للتغليظ واحد. [البحر الرائق: ٩٨/٣] بيوم النحر فقط بيان لكون الهدي مؤقتا بالمكان سواء كان دم شكر أو جناية، وأما توقيته بالزمان فمخصوص والقرآن، وأما بقية الهدايا فلا يتقيد بزمان، وأفاد أن هدي التطوع إذا بلغ الحرم لا يتقيد بزمان، وهو الصحيح، وإن كان ذبحه يوم النحر أفضل البحر الرائق بحذف: ١٠٠/٣] بهدي المتعة  ٢٧٤ زيارة النبي كتاب الحج وخص ذبح كل هدي بالحرم إلا أن يكون تطوعا وتعيب في الطريق، فينحر في محله، ولا يشترط له منى ولا يأكله غني وفقير الحرم وغيره سواء، وتقلّد بدنة التطوع والمتعة والقرآن فقط، لكن فقيره أفضل ندبا ويتصدق بجلاله وخطامه ولا يعطى أجر الجزار منه ولا يركبه بلا ضرورة، زمام الذباح ولا يحلب لبنه إلا أن بعد المحل فيتصدق به، وينضح ضرعه إن قرب المحل بالنقاخ، هو الماء البارد ولو نذر حجا ماشيا لزمه ولا يركب حتى يطوف للركن، فإن ركب أراق دما، أي صبه وفضل المشي على الركوب للقادر عليه. وفقنا الله تعالى بفضله، ومن علينا بالعود على أحسن حال إليه بجاه سيدنا محمد الحج فصل في زيارة النبي على سبيل الاختصار تبعا لما قال في الاختيار لما كانت زيارة النبي من أفضل القرب وأحسن المستحبات، كل هدي دخل فيه الهدي المنذور، بخلاف البدنة المنذورة، فإنها لا تتقيد بالحرم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد حما. Visiting the Prophet's Grave (Ziyarah)
Brief note on the recommendation and priority of visiting the Prophet's grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling and etiquette of visiting the Prophet Muhammad's grave after Hajj, and identify the preference for prioritizing obligatory Hajj over ziyarah.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a highly recommended act, but one should prioritize obligatory Hajj over it if needed.

This lesson covers a brief passage at the end of the source text regarding the visitation (ziyarah) of the Prophet's grave in Medina. Although not directly about hady, it is a common practice after Hajj. The text provides guidance on the timeliness and priority.

Guided Path
1
Understand the virtue of ziyarah
The text describes ziyarah as 'from the best of acts and most beautiful of recommended practices'. It is a sunnah and a means of gaining barakah.
This sets the tone: highly recommended but not obligatory.
2
Determine the priority relative to Hajj
The scholars quoted in the passage say: if the Hajj is obligatory (fard), one should perform Hajj before ziyarah. If the Hajj is voluntary, one may choose.
This is important because ziyarah is often combined with Hajj, but the obligatory act takes precedence.
3
Note the time recommendation
The text does not specify a particular time for ziyarah, but it is often done after completing the Hajj rituals.
The passage mentions that it is a 'a great act of worship' but does not give detailed ritual.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Virtue of Visiting the Prophet's Grave
Statement that visiting the Prophet's grave is among the best acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on visiting the Prophet's grave and explain when it should be prioritized over other acts.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is among the best recommended acts, but obligatory Hajj takes precedence.

In this passage from Nur al-Idah, the author highlights the virtue of visiting the Prophet’s grave (ziyarah) as one of the best acts of worship. He also provides a crucial practical guideline: if a pilgrim intends to perform obligatory Hajj, it must come before visiting the grave. We will examine the ruling and its proper application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its status
Recognize that visiting the Prophet's grave (ziyarah) is a recommended act (mustahab) and counts among the best deeds. The text describes it as 'among the best acts of worship and the best recommended deeds'.
The act itself is not obligatory.
2
Determine the priority rule
Understand that if one has an obligatory Hajj to perform, it takes precedence over ziyarah. The commentary states: 'If the Hajj is obligatory, he prioritizes it over ziyarah'.
Obligatory acts override recommended ones.
3
Apply the rule in practice
When planning a trip, a Muslim who has not yet performed his obligatory Hajj should first perform Hajj, then may visit the Prophet's grave at another time, as it remains a recommended act.
If Hajj is already performed, visiting the grave is a free choice.

فصل في زيارة النبي على سبيل الاختصار تبعا لما قال في الاختيار لما كانت زيارة النبي من أفضل القرب وأحسن المستحبات، كل هدي دخل فيه الهدي المنذور، بخلاف البدنة المنذورة، فإنها لا تتقيد بالحرم عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد حما. [البحر الرائق: ۱۰۱/۳] لزمه قيل: يمشي من حين يحرم، وقيل: من بيته، وهو الأصح. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٥ زيارة النبي إلخ : قالوا: إن كان الحج فرضا قدمه عليها، وإلا يخير، =
Fasl on visiting the Prophet, summarized, following what was said in al-Ikhtiyar: Since visiting the Prophet is among the best acts of worship and the best recommended deeds... [then commentary on various hady rulings] ... They said: If the Hajj is obligatory, he prioritizes it over ziyarah, otherwise he has a choice. =
Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of visiting the Prophet's grave (Ziyarat al-Nabi), stating that it is one of the best acts of worship and most excellent recommended deeds, following the authority of al-Ikhtiyar. The commentary that follows, however, is not directly about ziyarah but continues from the earlier section on hady, discussing rulings about sacrificial animals, including: vowed hady is included in the general rules, but a vowed camel is not restricted to the Haram according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; the use of the animal's covering and halter; not giving the slaughterer's fee; not riding the animal; milking it only if near the place of sacrifice, etc. The final note states that if the Hajj is obligatory, one should prioritize it over ziyarah; otherwise, one has a choice.

Key Terms
زيارة (ziyarah): Visiting the grave of the Prophet Muhammad, considered a recommended act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what should a pilgrim do if his Hajj is obligatory?
A) Visit the Prophet's grave first
B) Postpone Hajj and visit the grave
C) Prioritize Hajj over visiting the grave
D) Neither, both are equal

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a highly recommended act, but obligatory acts such as Hajj must be performed first.

Ziyarat al-Nabi: Recommended Etiquettes for Visiting the Prophet's Mosque and Grave
Describes the recommended sequence of etiquettes for visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the sequence of recommended acts (sunan) for visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah and explain the significance of each.

Core Idea
The Prophet's mosque and grave are honored places; visiting them with proper etiquette is a highly recommended sunnah.

This passage from Nur al-Idah concludes the Hajj section by outlining the etiquettes of visiting the Prophet (peace be upon him) in Madinah. These acts are not obligatory but are deeply recommended by the Hanafi school. The author organizes them as a sequence from the moment the traveler sees Madinah's walls to standing at the noble grave, emphasizing reverence and gratitude.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall legal status
The entire sequence is classified as sunnah (recommended), not fard or wajib. Understand the difference: omitting sunnah results in loss of reward but does not invalidate the visit.
Hanafis consider the visit itself mustahabb (commendable), not an obligation of Hajj.
2
List the actions in order
The text prescribes a specific order: upon seeing Madinah's walls, send blessings and recite a du'a; perform ghusl, apply perfume, wear best clothes; enter the city on foot; enter the mosque; pray tahiyyat al-masjid at the minbar; then perform two rak'ahs of gratitude; supplicate; then approach the grave with adab.
The sequence is not legally binding but following it is meritorious.
3
Distinguish general and specific etiquettes
Some acts are common to any mosque visit (e.g., tahiyyat al-masjid), while others are specific to the Prophet's presence (e.g., standing at a certain distance from the grave). This distinction is made by the author (kulliyyat wa juz'iyyat).
General etiquettes include entering with humility; specific ones include facing away from qiblah when at the grave.
4
Note the virtues cited
The text includes hadith about the reward of frequent salawat, and that the area between grave and pulpit is a garden of Paradise. This motivates adherence to the sunan.
These virtues are well-known; they encourage sincere intention.
5
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Consider a traveler who is ill and cannot walk. The text says to enter Madinah walking 'if possible without necessity'; thus, riding is allowed when needed. This shows flexibility while maintaining the ideal.
Necessity (darurah) overrides the preferred action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج
زيارة النبي
ولما رأينا أكثر الناس غافلين عن أداء حق زيارته، وما يسن للزائرين من الكُلِيَّاتِ والجزئيات، أحببنا أن نذكر بعد المناسك وأدائها ما فيه نبذة الآداب؛ تتميما لفائدة الكتاب. أي بعد ذكرها فنقول: ينبغي لمن قصد زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يكثر من الصلاة عليه، فإنه يسمعها وتبلغ إليه، وفضلها أشهر من أن يذكر، فإذا عاين حيطان المدينة المنورة يصلي على النبي ويقول: "اللهم هذا حرم نبيك ومهبط وحيك فامنن عليَّ بالدخول فيه، واجعله وقاية لي من النار، وأمانا من العذاب واجعلني من الفائزين بشفاعة المصطفى يوم المآب"، ويغتسل قبل الدخول أو بعده قبل التوجه للزيارة إن أمكنه، ويتطيب ويلبس أحسن ثيابه تعظيما للقدوم على النبي ثم يدخل المدينة المنورة ماشيا إن أمكنه بلا ضرورة بعد وضع ركبه متواضعا بالسكينة والوقار ملاحظا جلالة المكان، قائلا: "بسم الله وعلى ملة رسول الله، رب أدخلني مدخل صدق، وأخرجني مخرج صدق، واجعل لي من لدنك سلطانا نصيرا اللهم صل على سيدنا محمد وعلى آل محمد إلى آخره واغفر لي ذنوبي وافتح لي أبواب رحمتك وفضلك". ثم يدخل المسجد الشريف، فيصلي تحيته عند منبره ركعتين، ويقف بحيث يكون عمود المنبر الشريف بحذاء منكبه الأيمن، فهو موقف النبي، وما بين قبره ومنبره روضة من رياض الجنة كما أخبر به، وقال: "منبري على حوضي". فتسجد شكرا لله تعالى بأداء ركعتين غير تحية المسجد؛ شكرا لما وفقك الله تعالى ومن عليك بالوصول إليه، ثم تدعو بما شئت ثم تنهض متوجها إلى القبر الشريف، فتقف بمقدار أربعة أذرع بعيدا عن المقصورة الشريفة بغاية الأدب مستدبر القبلة محاذيا لرأس النبي،

[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٦] نبذة: بالفتح وتضم القطعة الشيء. يسمعها: أي إذا كانت بالقرب منه . وتبلغ إلخ: أي يبلغها الملك إليه إذا كان المصلي بعيدا. وفضلها أشهر إلخ فمنها ما ذكره العارف بالله سنان أفندي له في "تبيين المحارم": قال : "من قال: أهله، أتعب سبعين كاتبا ألف "صباح". رواه الطبراني ، وقال : "من صلى علي عشر مرات صلى الله عليه يوم القيامة مع الجنة". رواه ابن شاهين، وفي رواية: من صلى علي كل يوم ثلاث مرات وكل ليلة ثلاث مرات، حبا وشوقا إليَّ، كان حقا على الله أن يغفر له ذنوب تلك الليلة وذلك اليوم". رواه الطبراني. حرم نبيك: أي مسجده، أو ما يحترم لأجله. المنورة: لقبت بها، فإنها منورة بصاحبها. ركبه : أي بعد استقرار من معه من الركاب؛ ليعرف محلهم في العود.
[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٦-٧٤٧] حشمه: الحشم محركة للواحد والجمع وهو العيال والقرابة، وخاصته الذين يغضبون له من أهل أو عبيد أو جيرة. جلالة المكان: أما بالجيم فمعناه يلاحظ عظمة مكان حضر لديه، وأما بالحاء المهملة فمعناه يلاحظ من حلّ المكان وهو النبي. مدخل صدق: أي إدخالا مرضيا لا أرى فيه ما يكره. مخرج صدق: أي إخراجا مرضيا لك بحيث لا يكون عليّ فيه مواخذة. سلطانا نصيرا: أي قوة تنصرني بها على أعدائك. إلى آخره أي إلى آخر صلاة التشهد. أبواب رحمتك أي هيئ لي الأسباب المقتضية للرحمة والإحسان. روضة من رياض إلخ أي إنه يصير كذلك يوم القيامة، أو إنه لما يحصل فيه من الثواب والأجر كأنه كذلك، أو لأنه يوصل إليها. منبري: لا مانع لمن حمله على الحقيقة. ثم تنهض إلخ أي تقوم بالأدب، والمراد أنه لا يتراخى وإن كان بالتأني والتمهل مستدبر القبلة كما هو السنة في زيارة الأموات.
Book of Hajj: Visit of the Prophet. And since we have seen most people heedless of fulfilling the right of visiting him, and what is recommended for visitors from the general and specific etiquettes, we wished to mention after the rituals and their performance a synopsis of the etiquettes, completing the benefit of the book. So we say: It is befitting for one who intends to visit the Prophet (peace be upon him) to increase blessings upon him, for he hears it and it reaches him. Then when he sees the walls of Madinah al-Munawwarah, he should send blessings upon the Prophet and say: 'O Allah, this is the sanctuary of Your Prophet and the place of revelation of Your inspiration, so grant me the favor of entering it, make it a protection for me from the Fire, and a security from punishment, and make me among the successful with the intercession of the Chosen One on the Day of Return.' And he should perform ghusl before entering or after it before proceeding to the visit if possible, apply perfume, and wear his best clothes out of reverence for coming to the Prophet. Then he should enter Madinah walking if possible without necessity after placing his baggage (or after his mount is settled), humble with tranquility and dignity, observing the majesty of the place, saying: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah. O Lord, cause me to enter a good entry and cause me to exit a good exit, and grant me from Yourself a helping authority. O Allah, bless our master Muhammad and the family of Muhammad... and forgive my sins and open for me the doors of Your mercy and bounty.' Then he enters the noble mosque, prays its greeting (tahiyyah) at the pulpit (minbar) two rak'ahs, stands such that the pillar of the noble pulpit is parallel to his right shoulder - that is the place where the Prophet (peace be upon him) stood. What is between his grave and his pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise, as he informed. He said: 'My pulpit is upon my basin.' So he prostrates in gratitude to Allah for performing two rak'ahs other than the mosque greeting, thanking Allah for enabling and favoring him to arrive there. Then he supplicates as he wishes. Then he rises, heading towards the noble grave, stands at a distance of four cubits from the noble enclosure with utmost reverence, facing away from the qiblah (i.e., towards the Prophet), parallel to the head of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is a statement of recommended acts (sunan) for visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah. It opens by noting that many people are neglectful of the proper etiquettes, so the author includes a summary here after the Hajj rituals section. The text then lists a sequence of recommended actions: the visitor should increase salawat upon the Prophet, as it is heard by him or conveyed by angels. Upon sighting Madinah's walls, a specific du'a is recommended. Before entering, ghusl, perfume, and best clothes are advised. Entering Madinah on foot is preferable, displaying humility. Upon entering the mosque, one prays two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid at the minbar, then stands at a specific spot and recalls the hadith about the garden between the grave and pulpit. An additional two rak'ahs of gratitude are recommended, followed by supplication. Finally, the visitor approaches the grave from the direction of the qiblah, standing four cubits away, parallel to the head, with great respect. The footnotes from al-Tahtawi explain lexical terms: 'nabdhah' means a piece, 'yasma'uha' means if near, 'tablugh' means the angel conveys, and 'hurm nabiyyik' means his mosque or what is honored for him. They also cite hadiths on the virtue of salawat, such as one by al-Tabarani about blessings leading to forgiveness.

Key Terms
زيارة النبي (ziyarat al-nabi): Visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah, consisting of a set of recommended acts and supplications.
الكليات والجزئيات (al-kulliyyat wa al-juz'iyyat): General etiquettes common to all mosque visits (e.g., tahiyyat al-masjid) and specific etiquettes unique to visiting the Prophet (e.g., standing at the grave).
الروضة (al-rawdah): The area between the Prophet's grave and his pulpit, which is specifically called a garden of Paradise in hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first recommended action upon seeing the walls of Madinah al-Munawwarah?
A) Perform ghusl
B) Apply perfume
C) Send blessings upon the Prophet and recite a specific supplication
D) Enter the mosque immediately

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's mosque and grave in Madinah is a highly recommended sunnah; the etiquettes prescribed ensure respect and spiritual reward.
