Entering the Prophet's Mosque with Humility and Du'a
Etiquette for entering the mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi etiquette for entering the Prophet's mosque, including the prescribed du'a and the state of mind required.

Core Idea
Enter the Prophet's mosque with humility, reciting the specific du'a, and pray two rak'ahs at the minbar.

Visiting the Prophet's mosque in Medina is a highly recommended act. The Hanafi school has detailed etiquette for this sacred visit. This lesson covers the opening steps: the visitor's state of mind, the du'a upon entering, and the prayer at the minbar.

Guided Path
1
Prepare Your State of Mind
The visitor should be at ease regarding his dependents and belongings, and enter with humility, tranquility, and dignity, observing the grandeur of the place.
This sets the spiritual tone for the visit.
2
Recite the Entering Du'a
Upon entering the mosque, say: 'Bismillah wa 'ala millati rasulillah, Rabbi adkhilni madkhala sidq...' This du'a asks for a truthful entrance and departure.
The du'a includes seeking a 'supporting authority' from Allah.
3
Pray the Greeting of the Mosque
Before approaching the grave, pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid near the Prophet's minbar, aligning your right shoulder with its pillar.
This is based on the Prophet's own practice.
4
Understand the Significance
The area between the grave and minbar is a garden from Paradise, and the minbar is over the Prophet's hawd (cistern). Reflect on this blessing.
This increases reverence.

كتاب الحج

زيارة النبي

ووجهه الأكرم مُلاحظا نظره السعيد إليك، وسماعه كلامك، ورده عليك سلامك، وتأمينه على دعائك، وتقول : السلام عليك يا سيدي يا رسول الله، السلام عليك يا نبي الله، السلام عليك يا حبيب الله، السَّلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة، السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة، السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين، السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين، السلام عليك يا ،مزمل السلام عليك يا مدثر السلام عليك وعلى أصولك الطيبين
وأهل بيتك الطاهرين، الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيرا، جزاك الله الإثم عنا أفضل ما جزى نبيا عن قومه، ورسولا عن أمته، أشهد أنك رسول الله، قد

ملاحظا أي تلاحظ أنه النشا واللا ناظر إليك [حاشية الطحطاوي (٧٤٧] :مزمل أصله المتزمل أدغمت التاء في الزاء، أي المتلفف بثيابه حين مجيء الوحي له؛ خوفا منه لهيبته، ومثله المدثر أصلا ومعنى [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] أصولك الطيبين هو يعم الذكور والإناث. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] الأمانة: أي الصلاة وغيرها مما في فعله ثواب وتركه عقاب، أي بلغت ذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] جهاده: أي جهاده الحق، أو أعظم جهاده. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] بعلم الله : متعلق بـ"كان" و"يكون" على التنازع . لأمدها : الأمد بفتح الميم: الغاية والمنتهى. (أقرب الموارد) وفدك: أي الوافدون والواردون عليك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨]
Book of Hajj. Visiting the Prophet. And his being at ease regarding his dependents or his belongings, humbly with tranquility and dignity, observing the grandeur of the place, saying: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, O Lord, cause me to enter a truthful entrance, and to depart a truthful departure, and grant me from Yourself a supporting authority. O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad to the end, and forgive me my sins and open for me the doors of Your mercy and bounty.' Then he enters the noble mosque, and prays its greeting (tahiyyah) at his pulpit two rak'ahs, and stands such that the pillar of the noble pulpit is opposite his right shoulder, for that is the standing place of the Prophet, and what is between his grave and pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise as he informed, and he said: 'My pulpit is upon my cistern.' Then you prostrate in gratitude to Allah the Exalted by performing two rak'ahs other than the greeting of the mosque; gratitude for what Allah the Exalted has enabled you and bestowed upon you to reach him. Then you supplicate as you wish, then you rise heading towards the noble grave, and you stand at a distance of four cubits away from the noble enclosure with utmost respect, turning your back to the qiblah, aligning with the head of the Prophet. 'Hashmuhu' (his dependents): Al-hasham (with vowel movements) is used for singular and plural, meaning family and relatives, and his special people who get angry for him, from family, slaves, or neighbors, as stated in al-Qamus; the intended meaning is the first. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 746] 'Jalalat al-makan' (grandeur of the place): If with jim, it means he observes the greatness of the place he is in; if with ha, it means he observes the one who occupies the place, i.e., the Prophet. And I have resolved my intention to follow the religion of the Messenger of Allah. 'Madkhala sidq' (truthful entrance): Meaning an entrance pleasing in which I do not see anything disliked. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Makhraja sidq' (truthful departure): Meaning a departure pleasing to you such that I am not taken to task over it. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Sultanan nasiran' (a supporting authority): Meaning strength with which you support me against Your enemies. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Ila akhirihi': i.e., to the end of the prayer of tashahhud. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Abwaba rahmatika' (doors of Your mercy): Meaning prepare for me the means necessitating mercy and goodness. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Rawdah min riyad' (a garden from the gardens): i.e., it will become so on the Day of Judgment, or because of the reward and recompense obtained therein it is as if it is so, or because it leads to it. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Minbari' (my pulpit): There is no obstacle to taking it literally. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Thumma tanhadu' (then you rise): i.e., you stand with respect, meaning you do not delay, though with slowness and deliberation, turning your back to the qiblah as is the Sunnah in visiting the dead. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] And his noble face, observing his blessed gaze upon you, his hearing your speech, his returning your greeting, and his saying 'Amin' to your supplication, and you say: Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah; peace be upon you, O beloved of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of mercy; peace be upon you, O intercessor of the ummah; peace be upon you, O master of the messengers; peace be upon you, O seal of the prophets; peace be upon you, O al-Muzzammil; peace be upon you, O al-Muddaththir; peace be upon you and upon your good ancestors and your pure household, those from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best of what He has rewarded a prophet for his people and a messenger for his nation. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah; you have conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the ummah, established the proof, and struggled in the path of Allah with His true striving, and established the religion until certainty (death) came to you. May Allah bless you and grant you peace. And upon the most noble place that is honored by the settlement of your noble body in it, blessings and peace eternal from the Lord of the worlds, as many as what has been and what will be by the knowledge of Allah, a blessing whose end does not come. O Messenger of Allah, we are your visitors and the visitors of your sanctuary, we are honored to be present before you, and we have come from vast lands and distant places. 'Mulahi'an' (observing): i.e., you observe that he is looking at you. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Muzzammil': Originally al-mutazammil, the ta was assimilated into the zay, i.e., the one wrapped in his clothes at the time of revelation coming to him, fearing it due to its awe; similarly al-Muddaththir in origin and meaning. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Usuluka al-tayyibin' (your good ancestors): It includes males and females. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Al-amanah' (the trust): i.e., the prayer and other things whose doing entails reward and leaving entails punishment, meaning you conveyed that. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748] 'Jihadahu' (his striving): i.e., his true striving, or his greatest striving. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748] 'Bi'ilm Allah' (by the knowledge of Allah): It is connected to 'was' and 'will be' on the basis of competition (tanazu'). 'Li-amadiha' (its end): Al-amad (with fatha on mim): the limit and end. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) 'Wafduka' (your visitors): i.e., those who come and arrive to you. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748]
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the etiquette (adab) of visiting the Prophet Muhammad's grave in Medina, as part of the rituals of Hajj or Umrah. The text is from Nur al-Idah, a Hanafi manual, with extensive explanatory notes from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. The ruling here is that visiting the Prophet's grave is a recommended act (sunnah or mustahabb) with specific protocols. The passage begins by describing the state of mind of the visitor: he should be at ease regarding his belongings and family, and enter the mosque with humility, tranquility, and dignity, observing the grandeur of the place. The visitor recites a specific du'a upon entering the mosque, invoking Allah to enable a truthful entrance and departure. After entering, he prays two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting of the mosque) near the Prophet's pulpit (minbar), standing so that the pillar of the pulpit aligns with his right shoulder—this was the Prophet's own standing place. The text then mentions the hadith that the area between the Prophet's grave and pulpit is a garden from Paradise, and that his pulpit is over his cistern (hawd). Then, as a gesture of gratitude for reaching this blessed place, the visitor performs two additional rak'ahs (not the greeting) as a prostration of thanks (sajdat al-shukr). After supplication, he approaches the grave, standing about four cubits away with utmost respect, turning his back to the qiblah (as is the sunnah in visiting graves), aligning with the Prophet's head. The Tahtawi commentary clarifies key terms: 'hasham' means dependents, 'jalalat al-makan' refers to the grandeur of the place or the occupant (the Prophet), and explains the du'a phrases. The passage then instructs the visitor to be aware that the Prophet sees him, hears his salaam, returns it, and says 'Amin' to his du'a. The visitor then recites a lengthy salaam and shahadah, acknowledging the Prophet's completion of his mission. The Tahtawi commentary explains that 'muzzammil' and 'muddaththir' refer to the Prophet's epithets, and that the Prophet's ancestors and family are included in the salutations. The visitor concludes by expressing that he is a visitor (wafd) from distant lands. This passage is primarily a practical manual for the ziyarah, and does not provide proof texts, but rather assumes the sunnah status of the visit.

Key Terms
حشم (hasham): Dependents, including family, relatives, slaves, and close associates who would be angered if harm befell them.
جلالة المكان (jalalat al-makan): Grandeur of the place (if with jim) or the person occupying the place (the Prophet, if with ha).
مدخل صدق (madkhala sidq): An entrance that is pleasing to Allah, wherein the person does not see anything disliked.
مخرج صدق (makhraja sidq): A departure pleasing to Allah, without being held accountable.
سلطانا نصيرا (sultanan nasiran): A supporting authority, i.e., strength from Allah to overcome enemies.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi text, what should the visitor do immediately after entering the Prophet's mosque?
A) Rush to the grave to kiss it.
B) Pray two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid at the minbar.
C) Recite the entire Quran.
D) Give charity to the poor.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi etiquette for entering the Prophet's mosque involves a state of humility, a specific du'a, and a two-rak'ah prayer at the minbar before approaching the grave.

The Gratitude Prayer and Approaching the Grave
Gratitude prayer and approaching grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi protocol for performing the gratitude prayer (sajdat al-shukr) and approaching the Prophet's grave with proper adab.

Core Idea
After the greeting prayer, perform two rak'ahs of gratitude, then approach the grave with dignity, standing four cubits away with your back to the qiblah.

Once the visitor has prayed the tahiyyat al-masjid, the next step is to express gratitude to Allah for reaching this blessed place. This is done through an additional prayer. Then, the visitor approaches the Prophet's grave with specific positioning and respect.

Guided Path
1
Perform the Gratitude Prayer
After completing personal supplications, perform two rak'ahs with the intention of shukr (gratitude) to Allah for enabling you to reach the Prophet's mosque.
This is separate from tahiyyat al-masjid.
2
Make Personal Supplication
After the gratitude prayer, make any du'a you wish. This is a time for personal requests.
The text says 'thumma tad'u bima shi'ta'.
3
Rise and Approach the Grave
Then rise with respect and head towards the noble grave. Stand about four cubits away from the enclosure, with utmost adab.
Four cubits is roughly 2 meters.
4
Position Yourself Correctly
Turn your back to the qiblah and align yourself with the Prophet's head. This is the sunnah when visiting graves.
The commentary notes that turning one's back to the qiblah is the sunnah for visiting the dead.
5
Be Aware of the Prophet's Presence
The text mentions that the Prophet sees you, hears your speech, and responds. This awareness increases reverence.
This is a matter of spiritual belief.

زيارة النبي

ووجهه الأكرم مُلاحظا نظره السعيد إليك، وسماعه كلامك، ورده عليك سلامك، وتأمينه على دعائك، وتقول : السلام عليك يا سيدي يا رسول الله، السلام عليك يا نبي الله، السلام عليك يا حبيب الله، السَّلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة، السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة، السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين، السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين، السلام عليك يا ،مزمل السلام عليك يا مدثر السلام عليك وعلى أصولك الطيبين
وأهل بيتك الطاهرين، الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيرا، جزاك الله الإثم عنا أفضل ما جزى نبيا عن قومه، ورسولا عن أمته، أشهد أنك رسول الله، قد

The passage then instructs the visitor to be aware that the Prophet sees him, hears his salaam, returns it, and says 'Amin' to his du'a. The visitor then recites a lengthy salaam and shahadah, acknowledging the Prophet's completion of his mission. The Tahtawi commentary explains that 'muzzammil' and 'muddaththir' refer to the Prophet's epithets, and that the Prophet's ancestors and family are included in the salutations. The visitor concludes by expressing that he is a visitor (wafd) from distant lands. This passage is primarily a practical manual for the ziyarah, and does not provide proof texts, but rather assumes the sunnah status of the visit.

Key Terms
روضة من رياض الجنة (rawdah min riyad al-jannah): A garden from Paradise; interpreted as being actually a garden in the afterlife, or metaphorically due to the reward obtained there.
أصولك الطيبين (usuluka al-tayyibin): Your pure ancestors, including both male and female forebears.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Facing the qiblah, with his back to the grave.
B) Facing the grave, with his back to the qiblah.
C) Facing the qiblah and the grave at the same time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi etiquette includes a gratitude prayer after tahiyyat al-masjid, then approaching the grave with specific positioning: four cubits away, back to qiblah, aligned to the head.

The Salutation (Salam) at the Prophet's Grave
Prescribed salutation at the grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the Hanafi prescribed salutation upon the Prophet when visiting his grave, including the various titles and the shahadah.

Core Idea
The visitor recites a comprehensive salutation, acknowledging the Prophet's station, his family, and his mission, while believing he hears and responds.

After positioning correctly, the visitor recites a lengthy greeting that includes multiple titles of the Prophet, blessings on his ancestors and family, and a testimony of his fulfillment of his mission. The commentary explains the meaning of the epithets 'Muzzammil' and 'Muddaththir' and the inclusion of female ancestors in 'usuluka al-tayyibin'.

Guided Path
1
Begin with the Standard Salam
Start by saying 'As-salamu 'alayka ya sayyidi ya rasulallah' and continue through the sequence of salutations listed in the text.
Each title emphasizes a different aspect of the Prophet's role.
2
Include Ancestors and Family
After addressing the Prophet, include his pure ancestors and his purified household (ahl al-bayt).
The commentary notes that 'usuluka al-tayyibin' includes both male and female forebears.
3
Recite the Shahadah and Praise
Then testify that the Prophet conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the ummah, and struggled in Allah's path until death.
This is a form of praising his completion of his duties.
4
Request Reward for the Prophet
Ask Allah to reward the Prophet on behalf of the ummah with the best reward given to any prophet.
This shows gratitude and asks for continued blessings.
5
Express Arrival as Visitors
Conclude by acknowledging that we are his visitors (wafd) who have come from distant lands.
This reinforces the purpose of the visit.

كتاب الحج

زيارة النبي

ووجهه الأكرم مُلاحظا نظره السعيد إليك، وسماعه كلامك، ورده عليك سلامك، وتأمينه على دعائك، وتقول : السلام عليك يا سيدي يا رسول الله، السلام عليك يا نبي الله، السلام عليك يا حبيب الله، السَّلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة، السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة، السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين، السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين، السلام عليك يا ،مزمل السلام عليك يا مدثر السلام عليك وعلى أصولك الطيبين
وأهل بيتك الطاهرين، الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيرا، جزاك الله الإثم عنا أفضل ما جزى نبيا عن قومه، ورسولا عن أمته، أشهد أنك رسول الله، قد
بلغت الرسالة، وأدَّيت الأمانة، ونصحت الأمة، وأوضحت الحجة، وجاهدت في
سبيل
الله
البرهان
حق جهاده وأقمت الدين حتى أتاك اليقين صلى الله عليك وسلم
الموت
وعلى أشرف مكان تشرف بحلول جسمك الكريم فيه صلاة وسلاما دائمين من رب العالمين عدد ما كان وعدد ما يكون بعلم الله ، صلاة لا انقضاءَ لأَمَدِها يا رسول الله، نحن وفدك وزُوَّار حرمك تشرفنا بالحلول بين يديك، وقد جئناك

بالنزول
ملاحظا أي تلاحظ أنه النشا واللا ناظر إليك [حاشية الطحطاوي (٧٤٧] :مزمل أصله المتزمل أدغمت التاء في الزاء، أي المتلفف بثيابه حين مجيء الوحي له؛ خوفا منه لهيبته، ومثله المدثر أصلا ومعنى [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] أصولك الطيبين هو يعم الذكور والإناث. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] الأمانة: أي الصلاة وغيرها مما في فعله ثواب وتركه عقاب، أي بلغت ذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] جهاده: أي جهاده الحق، أو أعظم جهاده. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] بعلم الله : متعلق بـ"كان" و"يكون" على التنازع . لأمدها : الأمد بفتح الميم: الغاية والمنتهى. (أقرب الموارد) وفدك: أي الوافدون والواردون عليك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨]
Book of Hajj. Visiting the Prophet. And his being at ease regarding his dependents or his belongings, humbly with tranquility and dignity, observing the grandeur of the place, saying: 'In the name of Allah and upon the religion of the Messenger of Allah, O Lord, cause me to enter a truthful entrance, and to depart a truthful departure, and grant me from Yourself a supporting authority. O Allah, send blessings upon our master Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad to the end, and forgive me my sins and open for me the doors of Your mercy and bounty.' Then he enters the noble mosque, and prays its greeting (tahiyyah) at his pulpit two rak'ahs, and stands such that the pillar of the noble pulpit is opposite his right shoulder, for that is the standing place of the Prophet, and what is between his grave and pulpit is a garden from the gardens of Paradise as he informed, and he said: 'My pulpit is upon my cistern.' Then you prostrate in gratitude to Allah the Exalted by performing two rak'ahs other than the greeting of the mosque; gratitude for what Allah the Exalted has enabled you and bestowed upon you to reach him. Then you supplicate as you wish, then you rise heading towards the noble grave, and you stand at a distance of four cubits away from the noble enclosure with utmost respect, turning your back to the qiblah, aligning with the head of the Prophet. 'Hashmuhu' (his dependents): Al-hasham (with vowel movements) is used for singular and plural, meaning family and relatives, and his special people who get angry for him, from family, slaves, or neighbors, as stated in al-Qamus; the intended meaning is the first. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 746] 'Jalalat al-makan' (grandeur of the place): If with jim, it means he observes the greatness of the place he is in; if with ha, it means he observes the one who occupies the place, i.e., the Prophet. And I have resolved my intention to follow the religion of the Messenger of Allah. 'Madkhala sidq' (truthful entrance): Meaning an entrance pleasing in which I do not see anything disliked. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Makhraja sidq' (truthful departure): Meaning a departure pleasing to you such that I am not taken to task over it. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Sultanan nasiran' (a supporting authority): Meaning strength with which you support me against Your enemies. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Ila akhirihi': i.e., to the end of the prayer of tashahhud. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Abwaba rahmatika' (doors of Your mercy): Meaning prepare for me the means necessitating mercy and goodness. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Rawdah min riyad' (a garden from the gardens): i.e., it will become so on the Day of Judgment, or because of the reward and recompense obtained therein it is as if it is so, or because it leads to it. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Minbari' (my pulpit): There is no obstacle to taking it literally. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Thumma tanhadu' (then you rise): i.e., you stand with respect, meaning you do not delay, though with slowness and deliberation, turning your back to the qiblah as is the Sunnah in visiting the dead. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] And his noble face, observing his blessed gaze upon you, his hearing your speech, his returning your greeting, and his saying 'Amin' to your supplication, and you say: Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah; peace be upon you, O beloved of Allah; peace be upon you, O Prophet of mercy; peace be upon you, O intercessor of the ummah; peace be upon you, O master of the messengers; peace be upon you, O seal of the prophets; peace be upon you, O al-Muzzammil; peace be upon you, O al-Muddaththir; peace be upon you and upon your good ancestors and your pure household, those from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best of what He has rewarded a prophet for his people and a messenger for his nation. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah; you have conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the ummah, established the proof, and struggled in the path of Allah with His true striving, and established the religion until certainty (death) came to you. May Allah bless you and grant you peace. And upon the most noble place that is honored by the settlement of your noble body in it, blessings and peace eternal from the Lord of the worlds, as many as what has been and what will be by the knowledge of Allah, a blessing whose end does not come. O Messenger of Allah, we are your visitors and the visitors of your sanctuary, we are honored to be present before you, and we have come from vast lands and distant places. 'Mulahi'an' (observing): i.e., you observe that he is looking at you. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Muzzammil': Originally al-mutazammil, the ta was assimilated into the zay, i.e., the one wrapped in his clothes at the time of revelation coming to him, fearing it due to its awe; similarly al-Muddaththir in origin and meaning. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Usuluka al-tayyibin' (your good ancestors): It includes males and females. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 747] 'Al-amanah' (the trust): i.e., the prayer and other things whose doing entails reward and leaving entails punishment, meaning you conveyed that. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748] 'Jihadahu' (his striving): i.e., his true striving, or his greatest striving. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748] 'Bi'ilm Allah' (by the knowledge of Allah): It is connected to 'was' and 'will be' on the basis of competition (tanazu'). 'Li-amadiha' (its end): Al-amad (with fatha on mim): the limit and end. (Aqrab al-Mawarid) 'Wafduka' (your visitors): i.e., those who come and arrive to you. [Hashiyah al-Tahtawi: 748]
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition on the etiquette (adab) of visiting the Prophet Muhammad's grave in Medina, as part of the rituals of Hajj or Umrah. The text is from Nur al-Idah, a Hanafi manual, with extensive explanatory notes from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi. The ruling here is that visiting the Prophet's grave is a recommended act (sunnah or mustahabb) with specific protocols. The passage begins by describing the state of mind of the visitor: he should be at ease regarding his belongings and family, and enter the mosque with humility, tranquility, and dignity, observing the grandeur of the place. The visitor recites a specific du'a upon entering the mosque, invoking Allah to enable a truthful entrance and departure. After entering, he prays two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid (greeting of the mosque) near the Prophet's pulpit (minbar), standing so that the pillar of the pulpit aligns with his right shoulder—this was the Prophet's own standing place. The text then mentions the hadith that the area between the Prophet's grave and pulpit is a garden from Paradise, and that his pulpit is over his cistern (hawd). Then, as a gesture of gratitude for reaching this blessed place, the visitor performs two additional rak'ahs (not the greeting) as a prostration of thanks (sajdat al-shukr). After supplication, he approaches the grave, standing about four cubits away with utmost respect, turning his back to the qiblah (as is the sunnah in visiting graves), aligning with the Prophet's head. The Tahtawi commentary clarifies key terms: 'hasham' means dependents, 'jalalat al-makan' refers to the grandeur of the place or the occupant (the Prophet), and explains the du'a phrases. The passage then instructs the visitor to be aware that the Prophet sees him, hears his salaam, returns it, and says 'Amin' to his du'a. The visitor then recites a lengthy salaam and shahadah, acknowledging the Prophet's completion of his mission. The Tahtawi commentary explains that 'muzzammil' and 'muddaththir' refer to the Prophet's epithets, and that the Prophet's ancestors and family are included in the salutations. The visitor concludes by expressing that he is a visitor (wafd) from distant lands. This passage is primarily a practical manual for the ziyarah, and does not provide proof texts, but rather assumes the sunnah status of the visit.

Key Terms
مزمل (Muzzammil): An epithet of the Prophet meaning 'the one wrapped in garments' at the time of revelation coming to him out of awe.
مدثر (Muddaththir): An epithet of the Prophet meaning 'the one enwrapped in his cloak', similar in origin and meaning to Muzzammil.
وفد (wafd): Visitors, specifically those who come to the Prophet as pilgrims or visitors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By reciting Surah al-Fatiha.
B) By acknowledging themselves as visitors (wafd) from distant lands.
C) By asking for worldly wealth.
D) By praying for the Prophet's enemies.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi salutation at the Prophet's grave is a comprehensive blessing that includes multiple titles, testimony to his mission, and acknowledgment of the visitor's journey.

beginner

Etiquette of Visiting the Prophet's Grave
Prescribed supplication and actions for visiting the Prophet's grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recite the prescribed greeting and supplication for visiting the Prophet's grave and state the Hanafi ruling on conveying greetings (tablīgh al-salām).

Core Idea
Conveying a greeting to the Prophet is wajib as part of fulfilling the trust.

Visiting the Prophet's grave is a deeply spiritual act. The Hanafi school prescribes a specific set of greetings and supplications that the visitor should recite, while also emphasizing the importance of conveying the greetings of others. This lesson will guide you through the recommended words and the legal status of conveying salaam.

Guided Path
1
Understand the spiritual context
Recognize that the Prophet hears your greeting and responds. This is based on hadith and is the foundation of the etiquette.
2
Recite the salām phrases
Follow the sequence of honorific titles: Ya Rasul Allah, Ya Nabi Allah, etc. Learn the exact wording provided.
3
State the purpose of the visit
Declare yourself as a delegate, seek intercession, and recite Qur'an 4:64 to affirm the practice.
4
Convey greetings of others
If someone asked you to convey salaam, use the formula: 'Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so...' This is wajib.
5
Make personal supplication
After the prescribed words, pray for anything while facing the grave with your back to the qiblah.

كتاب الحج
زيارة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
ووجهه الأكرم مُلاحظا نظره السعيد إليك، وسماعه كلامك، ورده عليك سلامك، وتأمينه على دعائك، وتقول : السلام عليك يا سيدي يا رسول الله، السلام عليك يا نبي الله، السلام عليك يا حبيب الله، السَّلام عليك يا نبي الرحمة، السلام عليك يا شفيع الأمة، السلام عليك يا سيد المرسلين، السلام عليك يا خاتم النبيين، السلام عليك يا مزمل السلام عليك يا مدثر السلام عليك وعلى أصولك الطيبين وأهل بيتك الطاهرين، الذين أذهب الله عنهم الرجس وطهرهم تطهيرا، جزاك الله الإثم عنا أفضل ما جزى نبيا عن قومه، ورسولا عن أمته، أشهد أنك رسول الله، قد بلغت الرسالة، وأدَّيت الأمانة، ونصحت الأمة، وأوضحت الحجة، وجاهدت في سبيل الله حق جهاده وأقمت الدين حتى أتاك اليقين صلى الله عليك وسلم وعلى أشرف مكان تشرف بحلول جسمك الكريم فيه صلاة وسلاما دائمين من رب العالمين عدد ما كان وعدد ما يكون بعلم الله ، صلاة لا انقضاء لأَمَدِها يا رسول الله، نحن وفدك وزُوَّار حرمك تشرفنا بالحلول بين يديك، وقد جئناك من بلاد شاسعة وأمكنة بعيدة، نقطع السهل والوعر بقصد زيارتك لنفوز بشفاعتك، والنظر إلى مآثرك ومعاهدك، والقيام بقضاء بعض حقك، والاستشفاع بك إلى ربنا فإن الخطايا قد قصمت ظهورنا، والأوزار قد أثقلت كواهلنا وأنت الشافع المشفّع الموعود بالشفاعة العظمى، والمقام المحمود والوسيلة، وقد قال الله تعالى: ﴿وَلَوْ أَنَّهُمْ إِذْ ظَلَمُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ جَاءُوكَ فَاسْتَغْفَرُوا اللَّهَ وَاسْتَغْفَرَ لَهُمُ الرَّسُولُ لَوَجَدُوا اللهَ تَوَّابا رَحِيما﴾ (النساء: ٦٤) وقد جئناك ظالمين لأنفسنا مستغفرين لذنوبنا، فاشفع لنا إلى ربك واسأله أن يميتنا على سنتك، وأن يحشرنا في زمرتك، وأن يوردنا حوضك وأن يسقينا بكأسك غير خزايا ولا ندامى، الشفاعة الشفاعة الشفاعة يا رسول الله. يقولها ثلاثا. ﴿رَبَّنَا اغْفِرْ لَنَا وَلِإِخْوَانِنَا الَّذِينَ سَبَقُونَا بِالْإِيمَانِ وَلا تَجْعَلْ فِي قُلُوبِنَا غِلَا لِلَّذِينَ آمَنُوا رَبَّنَا إِنَّكَ رَؤُوفٌ رَحِيمٌ﴾ (الحشر: ١٠) وتبلغه سلام من أوصاك به، فتقول: السلام عليك يا رسول الله من فلان بن فلان يتشفّع بك إلى ربك فاشفع له وللمسلمين. ثم تصلّي عليه، وتدعو بما شئت عند وجهه الكريم مستدبر القبلة.
[حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] مزمل أصله المتزمل أدغمت التاء في الزاء، أي المتلفف بثيابه حين مجيء الوحي له؛ خوفا منه لهيبته، ومثله المدثر أصلا ومعنى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] أصولك الطيبين هو يعم الذكور والإناث. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٧] الأمانة: أي الصلاة وغيرها مما في فعله ثواب وتركه عقاب، أي بلغت ذلك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] جهاده: أي جهاده الحق، أو أعظم جهاده. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] بعلم الله: متعلق بـ"كان" و"يكون" على التنازع. لأمدها: الأمد بفتح الميم: الغاية والمنتهى. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] وفدك: أي الوافدون والواردون عليك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] السهل: هو من الأرض ضد الحزن. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] مآثرك: جمع مأثرة، وهي المكرمة المتواترة. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] ومعاهدك جمع معهد المنزل المعهود به الشيء. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] قصمت من القصم الكسر مع الإبانة أو عدمها. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] كواهلنا: جمع كاهل: الحارك أو مقدم أعلى الظهر مما يلي العنق، وهو الثلث الأعلى، وفيه ست فقر، أو ما بين الكتفين، أو موصل العنق في الصلب. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] والوسيلة هي منزلة في الجنة لا تكون إلا له. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] الرسول فيه التفات عن الخطاب تفخيما لشانه. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] بكأسك الكأس الإناء الذي يشرب فيه، أو ما دام الشراب فيه والمراد كؤوس حوضك. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٨] غير خزايا: جمع خزيان بمعنى مهين ولا ندامى جمع ندمان بالفتح بمعنى متأسف. [حاشية الطحطاوي: ٧٤٩] تبلغه: ذكروا أن تبليغ السلام واجب؛ لأنه من أداء الأمانة.
Book of Hajj. Visit of the Prophet (peace be upon him). And his noble face, observing his blessed glance towards you, his hearing your speech, his returning your greeting, and his saying Āmīn to your supplication. And you say: Peace be upon you, O my master, O Messenger of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Beloved of Allah. Peace be upon you, O Prophet of Mercy. Peace be upon you, O Intercessor of the Ummah. Peace be upon you, O Leader of the Messengers. Peace be upon you, O Seal of the Prophets. Peace be upon you, O Enwrapped. Peace be upon you, O Enshrouded. Peace be upon you and upon your pure ancestors and your purified Household, from whom Allah has removed impurity and purified them thoroughly. May Allah reward you on our behalf with the best reward He has rewarded any prophet for his people and any messenger for his nation. I bear witness that you are the Messenger of Allah; you have conveyed the message, fulfilled the trust, advised the Ummah, clarified the proof, and strived in the path of Allah with true striving, and established the religion until certainty came to you. May Allah send prayers and peace upon you and upon the most honorable place that is honored by the settlement of your noble body therein, eternal prayers and peace from the Lord of the worlds, as many as what has been and what will be by Allah's knowledge, prayers with no end to their extent. O Messenger of Allah, we are your delegates and visitors of your sanctuary; we are honored to settle before you, and we have come to you from distant lands and far places, traversing the easy and the rugged with the intention of visiting you to gain your intercession, to see your noble deeds and your places, to fulfill some of your right, and to seek intercession through you to our Lord, for sins have broken our backs and burdens have weighed down our shoulders. You are the intercessor whose intercession is accepted, promised the great intercession, the praised station, and the means (al-wasīlah). And Allah Most High said: "And if they, when they wronged themselves, had come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah Accepting of repentance, Merciful" (Qur'an 4:64). And we have come to you wronging ourselves, seeking forgiveness for our sins. So intercede for us with your Lord and ask Him to cause us to die upon your Sunnah, to gather us in your company, to bring us to your Basin, and to give us to drink from your cup, neither disgraced nor regretful. Intercession, intercession, intercession, O Messenger of Allah (he says it three times). "Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith and do not place in our hearts any resentment against those who have believed. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful" (Qur'an 59:10). And you convey the greeting of whoever has charged you with it. So you say: Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so son of so-and-so, he seeks intercession through you to your Lord, so intercede for him and for the Muslims. Then you send prayers upon him, and supplicate as you wish at his noble face, turning your back to the qiblah.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is the prescribed etiquette for visiting the grave of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) according to the Hanafi school, as recorded in Nur al-Idah. It begins by describing the state of the visitor, who should be aware that the Prophet perceives his presence, hears his speech, returns his greeting, and says Āmīn to his supplication. The visitor then recites a lengthy greeting (salām) containing many honorific titles. After the greeting, one sends ṣalawāt upon the Prophet and praises him for fulfilling his mission. The visitor then states his purpose: to seek intercession, to witness the Prophet's virtues, and to ask for forgiveness. A verse from Surah al-Nisa (4:64) is recited to emphasize that seeking forgiveness through the Prophet is a Quranic practice. The visitor then asks for the Prophet's intercession for a good death and resurrection in his company. The phrase 'intercession' is repeated three times. Another verse from Surah al-Hashr (59:10) is recited for forgiveness for all believers. The section ends with instructions on conveying someone else's greeting to the Prophet. This is considered wajib (obligatory) according to the hashīyah, because it is part of fulfilling the trust (amānah). Finally, the visitor sends prayers and makes personal supplication while facing the Prophet's grave with one's back to the qiblah. The marginal notes by Tahtawi explain linguistic terms: 'Muzammil' and 'Muddaththir' refer to the Prophet's state when receiving revelation; 'uṣūl' (ancestors) includes both men and women; 'amānah' refers to the religious duties; 'jihād' means true striving; 'saḥl' is level ground; 'ma'āthir' are noble deeds; 'ma'āhid' are places; 'qaṣama' means breaking; 'kāhil' is the upper back; 'wasīlah' is a station in Paradise unique to the Prophet; and 'ka's' is the cup of the Basin. The obligation of conveying salaam is highlighted as a wajib act.

Key Terms
مزمل (muzammil): One wrapped in garments, a title of the Prophet when receiving revelation.
أصولك الطيبين (uṣūluka al-ṭayyibīn): Your pure ancestors, including both male and female.
الأمانة (al-amānah): The trust, meaning religious duties such as prayer and other acts with reward for doing and punishment for leaving.
الوسيلة (al-wasīlah): A station in Paradise that is unique to the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).
كأس (ka's): The cup from which one drinks at the Prophet's Basin (Ḥawḍ).
تبليغ السلام (tablīgh al-salām): Conveying a person's greeting to the Prophet; considered wajib as it is part of fulfilling the trust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hashiyat al-Tahtawi quoted in the passage, what is the ruling on conveying someone's greeting to the Prophet (tablīgh al-salām)?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is mubah.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave involves prescribed supplications, and conveying someone's greeting is wajib.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Ziyarat al-Nabi: Ruling and Quranic Proof
Ruling with Quranic proof for visiting the Prophet's grave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on visiting the Prophet's grave and explain how Surah al-Nisa' 4:64 is used as evidence.

Core Idea
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a sunnah, affirmed by Quran 4:64 and the practice of the Companions.

This passage from Nur al-Idah instructs the pilgrim on the recommended act of visiting the Prophet's grave in Medina. It begins with a heartfelt supplication seeking the Prophet's intercession and cites Quranic verse 4:64 as a proof for the practice, which the Hanafi school interprets as a basis for tawassul and ziyarah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is visiting the Prophet's grave (ziyarah). According to the Hanafi school, it is a sunnah muakkadah (recommended but not obligatory).
The text begins by stating the intention to gain the Prophet's intercession.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 4:64: 'If they had, when they wronged themselves, come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah forgiving and merciful.'
This verse is used as evidence for the permissibility of seeking the Prophet's intercession even after his death.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The verse implies that coming to the Prophet and seeking forgiveness through him is a means to Allah's mercy. The Hanafi interpretation extends this to visiting his grave.
The dalala is zanni (probable) because the verse does not explicitly mention visitation after death; the Hanafi school uses analogy and the generality of the command.
4
Note the cross-madhhab consideration
Some schools (e.g., the Zahiri or some later Salafis) restrict the verse to the Prophet's lifetime. The Hanafi school maintains it is general.
The text also includes the practice of the Companions as further proof.

Visitation of the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. Book of Hajj: We traverse the easy and difficult terrain with the intention of visiting you, to gain your intercession, and to look upon your noble traces and your landmarks, and to fulfill some of your right, and to seek intercession through you to our Lord, for sins have broken our backs and burdens have weighed down our shoulders. You are the intercessor, the one whose intercession is accepted, promised the great intercession, the praiseworthy station, and the means. And Allah Almighty said: 'If they had, when they wronged themselves, come to you and asked forgiveness of Allah and the Messenger had asked forgiveness for them, they would have found Allah forgiving and merciful.' And we have come to you wronging ourselves, seeking forgiveness for our sins, so intercede for us with your Lord and ask Him to make us die upon your Sunnah and to gather us in your group, and to bring us to your Basin and give us to drink from your cup, not disgraced nor regretful. 'Intercession, intercession, intercession, O Messenger of Allah' - he says it three times. 'Our Lord, forgive us and our brothers who preceded us in faith and do not place in our hearts any rancor toward those who believe. Our Lord, indeed You are Kind and Merciful.' And you convey the greeting of whoever entrusted you with it, so you say: 'Peace be upon you, O Messenger of Allah, from so-and-so son of so-and-so, he seeks intercession through you to your Lord, so intercede for him and for the Muslims.' Then you send blessings upon him and supplicate as you wish at his noble face, facing away from the qiblah. Then you move a cubit until you are parallel to the head of al-Siddiq Abu Bakr and say: 'Peace be upon you, O Caliph of the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon you, O Companion of the Messenger of Allah, his intimate in the cave, his companion in journeys, his trustee of secrets, may Allah reward you with the best that He has rewarded an imam for the nation of his Prophet. You succeeded him with the best succession, followed his path and methodology in the best way, fought the people of apostasy and innovations, established Islam, strengthened its pillars, and were the best imam, and you upheld family ties. You remained upholding the truth, supporting the religion and its people until certainty came to you. Ask Allah for us to continue loving you, to be gathered with your party, and to accept our visitation. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' Then you move similarly until you are parallel to the head of the Commander of the Faithful Umar ibn al-Khattab, and say: 'Peace be upon you, O Commander of the Faithful, peace be upon you, O manifestor of Islam, peace be upon you, O breaker of idols, may Allah reward you with the best reward. You supported Islam and the Muslims, conquered most lands after the master of the messengers, sponsored the orphans, upheld family ties, and Islam was strengthened through you. You were for the Muslims a satisfied imam, a guide, guided, you united them, helped their poor, and mended their broken. Peace be upon you and the mercy of Allah and His blessings.' Then you step back half a cubit.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage is from the Book of Hajj in Nur al-Idah, detailing the recommended acts (sunan) of visiting the Prophet's grave in Medina. It begins with a supplication seeking the Prophet's intercession, citing Quran 4:64 as evidence that visiting the Prophet and seeking forgiveness through him is a means to Allah's mercy. The text instructs the visitor to say specific invocations three times, then convey greetings from others. After supplicating at the Prophet's grave, the visitor moves a cubit to the right to face the grave of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, offering a lengthy greeting praising his caliphate and role. Then moving a similar distance to face Umar ibn al-Khattab, greeting him and acknowledging his contributions. Finally, stepping back half a cubit. The hashiah of al-Tahtawi provides lexical definitions and notes that conveying salaam is wajib (obligatory) as it is an amanah. This reflects the Hanafi position that ziyarat al-Nabi is mustahabb (recommended), and respect for the Companions is emphasized.

Key Terms
الشفاعة (al-shafa'ah): Intercession; the Prophet’s act of pleading with Allah on behalf of sinners, which he is promised to have on the Day of Judgment (shafa'ah 'uzma).
الزيارة (al-ziyarah): Visitation, specifically to the Prophet's grave in Medina, performed as a recommended act during or outside of Hajj.
الوسيلة (al-wasilah): A high rank in Paradise uniquely granted to the Prophet, mentioned in the Quran (5:35) and sought in the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which Quranic verse does the author cite to support the practice of seeking the Prophet's intercession during ziyarah?
A) Surah al-Nisa' 4:64
B) Surah al-Hashr 59:10
C) Surah al-Baqarah 2:125
D) Surah al-Ahzab 33:56

Key Takeaway
Visiting the Prophet's grave is a sunnah muakkadah, rooted in Quranic encouragement and the practice of the Companions, and includes seeking his intercession.
